Methods for Detecting Narrator Confusion (Ikhtilat)
Two case studies illustrating methods for detecting narrator confusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two methods used by hadith scholars to detect ikhtilat and explain how each method impacts the evaluation of narrator reliability in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Confused narrators can be detected by consistency tests or by flipping chains; a narrator who passes remains reliable.

This lesson introduces two practical methods used by hadith critics to assess whether a narrator has become confused (mukhtalit). Since the Hanafi school relies on hadith for legal deduction, knowing how to evaluate narrator reliability is essential for usul al-fiqh. We will examine the method of re-hearing after a time interval and the method of flipping chains (qalb al-asanid wa al-mutun), as described with classical examples.

Guided Path
1
Understand ikhtilat and its impact
Ikhtilat is a confusion that affects a narrator's accuracy. Hanafi usul considers narrations predating confusion acceptable, so detecting when confusion occurred is critical.
This lesson focuses on detection methods, not the ruling on accepting confused narrators.
2
Analyze the consistency test over time
The first method involves re-hearing the same hadiths from the same shaykh after a period and comparing. The example of Abu Hurayrah shows that after a full year, his narration matched exactly, proving his precision.
This test requires a written record or a reliable memorizer to compare.
3
Analyze the flipping test (qalb al-asanid wa al-mutun)
The second method involves intentionally inverting chains and texts to see if the narrator notices. The story of Ibn 'Ajlan shows students flipping his hadiths; some scholars like Ibn Idris refrained, considering it impermissible.
This method is used only by expert critics and requires caution.
4
Consider the ethical dimension
Not all scholars approved of flipping chains, viewing it as a form of deception. Ibn Idris sat outside and said 'la astahill' (I do not consider it permissible). This highlights the tension between methodological rigor and ethical limits.
Hanafi usul may accept such tests if done purely for evaluation and without intent to deceive.

المحدثون أحياناً يعيدون سماع الأحاديث نفسها التي سمعوها من ذلك الشيخ من أجل أن يعرفوا ويحددوا الاختلاط من عدمه، ويحددوا وقت الاختلاط؛ لذلك قال حماد بن زيد: شعبة كان لا يرضى أن يسمع الحديث مرة يعاود صاحبه مراراً. ومما يذكر في هذه الباب ما قاله حماد ابن زيد قال: حدثني عمرو بن عبيد الأنصاري، قال: حدثني أبو الزعيزعة كاتب مروان أن مروان أرسل إلى أبي هريرة، فجعل يسأله، وأجلسني خلف السرير وأنا أكتب حتى إذا كان رأس الحول، دعا به فأقعده من وراء الحجاب، فجعل يسأله من ذلك الكتاب، فما زاد ولا نقص ولا قدم ولا أخر. وروى الحافظ أبو خيثمة زهير بن حرب في "كتاب العلم" قال: حدثنا عن عمارة بن القعقاع، قال: قال لي إبراهيم: حدثني عن أبي زرعة فإني سألته عن حديث، ثم سألته عنه بعد سنتين فما أخرمنه حرفاً. وهذا نوع من أنواع الكشف عن الخلل المتوقع طرؤه على المحدث عند تقدم السماع له، وكانت ثمة طرق أخرى للمحدثين يستطيعون من خلالها الكشف عن حال المحدث، وهل طرأ له اختلاط في ما يرويه أو بعض ما يرويه أم أنه حافظ ومتقن لما يروي ويحدث؟ ومن طرق المحدثين في معرفة اختلاط الرواة: أن الناقد منهم كان يدخل على الراوي ليختبره فيقلب عليه الأسانيد والمتون ويلقنه ما ليس من روايته، فإن لم ينتبه الشيخ لما يراد به فإنه يعد مختلطاً ويعزف الناس عن الرواية عنه، ومما يذكر في هذه البابة ما أسند إلى يحيى بن سعيد قال: قدمت الكوفة وبها ابن عجلان وبها ممن يطلب الحديث: مليح بن وكيع وحفص بن غياث وعبد الله بن إدريس ويوسف بن خالد السمتي، فقلنا: نأتي ابن عجلان، فقال يوسف بن خالد: نقلب على هذا الشيخ حديثه، ننظر تفهمه، قال: فقلبوا فجعلوا ما كان عن سعيد عن أبيه، وما كان عن أبيه عن سعيد، ثم جئنا إليه، لكن ابن إدريس تورع وجلس بالباب وقال: لا استحل وجلست معه. ودخل حفص، ويوسف بن خالد ومليح فسألوه فمر فيها، فلما كان عند
The hadith scholars sometimes repeat hearing the same ahadith that they heard from that shaykh in order to know and determine whether there is confusion (ikhtilat) or not, and to determine the time of confusion. Therefore, Hammad ibn Zayd said: Shu'bah was not satisfied to hear the hadith once; he would return to his companion repeatedly. Among what is mentioned in this chapter is what Hammad ibn Zayd said: 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd al-Ansari narrated to me, saying: Abu al-Zu'ayzi'ah, the scribe of Marwan, narrated to me that Marwan sent to Abu Hurayrah, and he began to question him, and he seated me behind the curtain while I was writing until the end of the year. Then he called him and seated him behind a screen, and began to question him from that book, and he did not add, did not subtract, did not advance, and did not delay. And al-Hafiz Abu Khaythamah Zuhayr ibn Harb narrated in 'Kitab al-'Ilm' saying: He narrated to us from 'Umarah ibn al-Qa'qa', who said: Ibrahim said to me: Narrate to me from Abu Zur'ah, for I asked him about a hadith, then I asked him about it after two years, and he did not omit a single letter from it. This is a type of revealing the defect expected to occur on the narrator after a long time since hearing. There were other methods for hadith scholars by which they could discover the condition of the narrator: whether confusion (ikhtilat) occurred in what he narrates or in some of what he narrates, or whether he is a memorizer and precise in what he narrates and relates. Among the methods of hadith scholars in knowing the confusion of narrators is that the critic would enter upon the narrator to test him, so he would flip the chains of transmission (asanid) and the texts (mutun) on him, and prompt him with what is not from his narration. If the shaykh did not notice what was intended, he would be considered confused, and people would refrain from narrating from him. Among what is mentioned in this regard is what is attributed to Yahya ibn Sa'id: He said: I came to Kufah, and there was Ibn 'Ajlan there, and among those seeking hadith were Mulayh ibn Wakii', Hafs ibn Ghiyath, 'Abdullah ibn Idris, and Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samti. So we said: Let us go to Ibn 'Ajlan. Yusuf ibn Khalid said: Let us flip the hadith of this shaykh for him to see his understanding. He said: So they flipped: they made what was from Sa'id from his father into what was from his father from Sa'id. Then we came to him. But Ibn Idris refrained and sat at the door and said: I do not consider it permissible. And I sat with him. Hafs, Yusuf ibn Khalid, and Mulayh entered and asked him, and he passed through them. When he came to...
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage from the introductory chapter discusses the nature of disagreement (ikhtilaf) among jurists by examining hadith transmission. The author presents two key methods used by hadith scholars to detect confusion (ikhtilat) in narrators, which directly impacts the reliability of hadiths and consequently the rulings derived from them. The first method involves re-hearing the same hadiths from the same shaykh after a period to check for consistency. The example of Abu Hurayrah's dictation being checked after a full year demonstrates this: the written record matched exactly, proving his precision. Similarly, the narration from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i shows consistency after two years. The second method is more active: the critic intentionally flips the chains of transmission (isnad) and the texts (matn) to test the narrator's awareness. The story of Ibn 'Ajlan illustrates this — students flipped his hadiths, but some scholars like Ibn Idris refrained out of caution. This method helps distinguish between a precise memorizer and one who has become confused. Understanding these methods is crucial for hanafis because the reliability of hadiths affects istinbat (deduction) of legal rulings. The author here lays groundwork for later discussion on how variations in hadith transmission lead to juristic disagreement, emphasizing that such differences are not arbitrary but traceable to methodological rigor in evaluating narrators.

Key Terms
اختلاط (ikhtilat): Confusion in the mind of a narrator leading to mixing up hadiths, especially in chains or texts.
قلاب الأسانيد والمتون (qalb al-asanid wa al-mutun): Flipping or inverting the chains of transmission and texts to test a narrator's memory and awareness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the story of Ibn 'Ajlan, which scholar refrained from participating in flipping the hadith and why?
A) Hafs ibn Ghiyath, because he considered it a waste of time.
B) Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samti, because he was the instigator.
C) Abdullah ibn Idris, because he deemed it impermissible (la astahill).
D) Mulayh ibn Wakii', because he was not present.

Key Takeaway
Hadith critics used two rigorous methods—time-based consistency checks and intentional flipping of chains—to detect narrator confusion, ensuring that only precise narrators are relied upon in Hanafi istinbat.

Ikhtilat and Its Effect on Narration Acceptance in Usul al-Fiqh
Definition and classification of ikhtilat's impact on hadith narration acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ikhtilat, classify transmitters from mixed narrators, and apply the ruling on ambiguous narrations.

Core Idea
Narrations from a mixed narrator are accepted only if heard before ikhtilat and clearly distinguished.

In Hanafi usul, the Sunnah is a primary source. Evaluating hadith narrators is crucial for accepting or rejecting narrations as legal proof. This lesson examines ikhtilat—a mental affliction affecting a narrator's reliability—and the scholarly system for determining which narrations remain accepted.

Guided Path
1
Define Ikhtilat
Ikhtilat is a mental affliction that begins gradually and worsens over time, affecting a narrator's accuracy.
The passage describes it as an affliction that starts simply and grows.
2
Understand the Four Transmitter Categories
Transmitters from a mixed narrator are divided into four groups: those who heard only before ikhtilat, only after, both without distinction, and both with distinction.
This classification is key to determining acceptance.
3
Apply the Ruling per Category
Narrations heard before ikhtilat are accepted if distinguished; after ikhtilat are rejected; if not distinguished, all are rejected.
Ambiguity leads to rejection.
4
Classify the Mixed Narrators Themselves
Al-'Ala'i divides mixed narrators into three categories: those unaffected (short ikhtilat or no narrations during it), those already weak, and those who become completely unreliable.
The effect varies; ijtihad is involved.
5
Appreciate the Flexibility
All classifications are subject to scholarly ijtihad, meaning that rulings depend on careful assessment of each case.
This nuance prevents mechanical rejection.

Source Text

الفصل التمهيدي بيان ماهية الاختلاف
بسنة). وحددوا وقت اختلاط سعيد بن أبي سعيد المقبري (٢) ، قَالَ ابن سعد إلا أنه اختلط قَبْلَ موته بأربع سنين ) .

وعلى الرغم من احتياطات المُحَدِّثِيْنَ وإمعانهم في تحديد وقت الاختلاط، فإنهم لم يتمكنوا من تحديد الساعات الأولى لبدء الاختلاط، فالاختلاط - كما سبق - آفة عقلية تبدأ بسيطة ثُمَّ تكبر شَيْئاً فشيئاً، ويتعاظم أمرها بالتدريج، وفي هذه الفترة الواقعة بَيْنَ بداية الاختلاط وظهوره وتفشيه يَكُون المختلط قَدْ رَوَى أحاديث تناقلها الرُّوَاة عَنْهُ، من غَيْر أن يعرفوا اختلاطه حين أخذهم عَنْهُ، ولربما كَانَ هَذَا الأمر سبباً في دخول الاختلاف والاضطراب في بعض أحاديث الثقات. غَيْر أن علماء الْحَدِيث – رحمهم الله - لَمْ يتركوا قضية الاختلاط والمختلطين عَلَى عواهنها، بَلْ إنهم نقبوا وفتشوا أحوال الرُّوَاة جيداً، وقسموا الرُّوَاة عَنْ المختلطين عَلَى أربعة أقسام: الأول: الَّذِيْنَ رووا عَنْ المختلط قَبْلَ اختلاطه. الثاني: الَّذِيْنَ رووا عَنْهُ بَعْدَ اختلاطه.
الثالث: الَّذِيْنَ رووا عَنْهُ قَبْلَ الاختلاط وبعده، وَلَمْ يميزوا هَذَا من هَذَا.
الرابع: الَّذِيْنَ رووا عَنْهُ قَبْلَ اختلاطه وبعده وميزوا هَذَا مِنْ هَذَا.
ووضعوا حكماً لكل قسم من هَذِهِ الأقسام فمن رَوَى عَنْ المختلط قَبْلَ الاختلاط قبلت روايته عَنْهُ، ومن رَوَى عَنْهُ قَبْلَ الاختلاط وبعده، وميز ما سَمِعَ قَبْلَ الاختلاط قُبِلَ، وَلَمْ يُقبل ما سَمِعَ بَعْدَ الاختلاط، ومن لَمْ يميز حديثه أو سَمِعَ بَعْدَ الاختلاط لَمْ تقبل روايته). ولعل الحافظ العراقي كَانَ أشمل في بيان الحكم من غيره، إِذْ قَالَ: «ثُمَّ الحكم فيمن اختلط أنه لا يقبل من حديثه ما حدث بهِ في حال الاختلاط، وكذا ما أبهم أمره وأشكل ، فَلَمْ ندرِ أحدث بِهِ قَبْلَ الاختلاط أو بعده؟ وما حدث بِهِ قَبْلَ الاختلاط قُبِلَ وإنما يتميز ذلك باعتبار الرُّوَاة عَنْهُمْ، فمنهم من سَمِعَ مِنْهُمْ قَبْلَ الاختلاط فَقَطْ، ومنهم من سَمِعَ بعده فقط، ومنهم من سَمِعَ في الحالين، وَلَمْ يتميز) (۳). وَقَدْ قسم الْمُحَدِّثُونَ المختلطين من حَيْثُ تأثير الاختلاط في قبول مروياتهم عَلَى ثلاثة أقسام قَالَ العلائي (۳): «أما الرُّوَاة الَّذِيْنَ حصل لَهُمْ الاختلاط في آخر عمرهم فهم على ثلاثة أقسام:
أحدها: من لَمْ يوجب ذَلِكَ لَهُ ضعفاً أصلاً، وَلَمْ يحط مـن مـرتبته؛ إمـا لـقـصـر مـدة الاختلاط وقلتِهِ كسفيان بن عيينة (4) ، وإسحاق بن إبراهيم بن راهويه، وهما من أئمة الإسلام المتفق عليهم؛ وإما لأنه لم يرو شيئاً حال اختلاطه، فسلم حديثه من الوهم كجرير بن حازم وعفان بن مسلم، ونحوهما.
ثانيها: من كَانَ مُتَكلّماً فِيْهِ قَبْلَ الاختلاط ، فَلَمْ يحصل من الاختلاط إلا زيادة في ضعفه؛ كابن لهيعة () ، ومحمد بن جابر الشحيمي)، ونحوهما.
ثالثها: من كَانَ قَبْلَ الاختلاط ثقةً فاختلط فَخَلَطَ وعظم أمره فَصَارَ متروك الحديث؛ كعبد الله بن لهيعة (في رواية) ونظرائه. (وكل هَذَا تابع للاجتهاد).
Introductory chapter: Explanation of the nature of difference. (Based on Sunnah). And they determined the time of ikhtilat of Sa'id ibn Abi Sa'id al-Maqburi, Ibn Sa'd said: except that he became mixed four years before his death. Despite the precautions of the hadith scholars and their thoroughness in determining the time of ikhtilat, they were unable to determine the first hours of the onset of ikhtilat. For ikhtilat - as previously mentioned - is a mental affliction that begins simply, then grows gradually, and its matter intensifies progressively. During this period between the beginning of ikhtilat and its appearance and spread, the mixed narrator may have narrated hadiths that narrators transmitted from him, without knowing of his ikhtilat when they received from him. Perhaps this was a cause for the entry of difference and disturbance in some hadiths of trustworthy narrators. However, the hadith scholars - may Allah have mercy on them - did not leave the issue of ikhtilat and mixed narrators uncontrolled; rather, they investigated and examined the conditions of narrators thoroughly, and divided the narrators from the mixed narrators into four categories: First: those who narrated from the mixed narrator before his ikhtilat. Second: those who narrated from him after his ikhtilat. Third: those who narrated from him before and after ikhtilat, and did not distinguish this from that. Fourth: those who narrated from him before and after ikhtilat and distinguished this from that. And they placed a ruling for each of these categories: whoever narrated from the mixed narrator before ikhtilat, his narration from him is accepted. Whoever narrated from him before and after ikhtilat, and distinguished what he heard before ikhtilat, it is accepted; what he heard after ikhtilat is not accepted. Whoever did not distinguish his hadith or heard after ikhtilat, his narration is not accepted. And perhaps al-Hafiz al-'Iraqi was more comprehensive in explaining the ruling than others, as he said: 'Then the ruling on one who became mixed: his hadith that he narrated during the state of ikhtilat is not accepted, and likewise what is ambiguous and problematic, so we do not know whether he narrated it before ikhtilat or after. And what he narrated before ikhtilat is accepted. And this is distinguished by considering the narrators from them: some heard from them only before ikhtilat, some heard only after, and some heard in both states and did not distinguish.' And the hadith scholars divided the mixed narrators in terms of the effect of ikhtilat on the acceptance of their narrations into three categories. Al-'Ala'i said: 'As for the narrators who experienced ikhtilat at the end of their lives, they are of three categories: First: those for whom this did not cause any weakness at all, nor lower their rank; either due to the short duration of the ikhtilat and its scarcity, like Sufyan ibn 'Uyaynah and Ishaq ibn Ibrahim ibn Rahawayh, both agreed upon as imams of Islam; or because he did not narrate anything during his ikhtilat, so his hadith remained safe from error, like Jarir ibn Hazim and 'Affan ibn Muslim and similar ones. Second: those who were criticized before ikhtilat, so ikhtilat only increased their weakness; like Ibn Lahi'ah and Muhammad ibn Jabir al-Suhaymi and similar ones. Third: those who were trustworthy before ikhtilat, then became mixed, confused, and his matter became great, so he became abandoned in hadith; like 'Abdullah ibn Lahi'ah (in one narration) and his peers. And all this is subject to ijtihad.'
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a theoretical introduction to the concept of ikhtilat in hadith sciences, which directly impacts usul al-fiqh when evaluating narrations used as legal proofs. The author explains the gradual nature of ikhtilat and how hadith scholars meticulously categorized narrators based on when they heard from a mixed narrator. The four-fold division of transmitters from a mixed narrator establishes clear rules: only what was heard before ikhtilat is accepted. Al-'Iraqi's ruling emphasizes that ambiguous narrations are rejected. Then al-'Ala'i's three-part division of the mixed narrators themselves shows that not all ikhtilat is equal: some narrators' truthfulness remains intact due to short duration or lack of narrations during ikhtilat; others were already weak; and some become completely unreliable. This classification is crucial for Hanafi usul because it affects the grading of hadith and thus the derivation of rulings. The passage underscores the precision required in evaluating narrators, a foundational element for istinbat.

Key Terms
الاختلاط (al-ikhtilat): A mental affliction that affects a narrator in old age, causing confusion and error in narration.
المختلط (al-mukhtalit): A narrator who has experienced ikhtilat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a narration from a mixed narrator where the transmitter heard from the narrator both before and after ikhtilat but did not distinguish?
A) All narrations are accepted regardless.
B) All narrations are rejected.
C) Only the pre-ikhtilat narrations are accepted if distinguishable, but if not distinguished, all are rejected.
D) Only the post-ikhtilat narrations are accepted.

Key Takeaway
Ikhtilat does not invalidate all narrations; pre-ikhtilat narrations are accepted if clearly distinguished.

Defining Dabit: Accuracy in Hadith Narration
Definition of dabit and its two types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define dabit as a condition for hadith authenticity, distinguish its two types (apparent and hidden), and apply the Hanafi view that apparent accuracy suffices for narration by meaning.

Core Idea
Accuracy (dabit) requires both linguistic precision and understanding of meaning; Hanafis accept apparent accuracy for narration by meaning.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the reliability of a hadith depends on the narrator's accuracy (dabit). Loss of eyesight is a factor that can compromise accuracy, but it is not automatically disqualifying. This lesson unpacks the technical definition of dabit and its two dimensions: apparent (linguistic) and hidden (jurisprudential understanding). Understanding this distinction is crucial for evaluating hadith and the Hanafi practice of narrating by meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for narrator reliability
Extract all elements required for a narrator to be considered accurate: attentiveness, memory or book accuracy, and knowledge of meaning.
These elements are explicitly listed in the passage.
2
Distinguish between apparent and hidden accuracy
Apparent accuracy refers to linguistic precision in wording; hidden accuracy refers to understanding the legal implications (fiqh) of the narration.
The passage defines both types and notes that absolute dabit is apparent accuracy according to the majority.
3
Analyze the Hanafi stance on narration by meaning
The Hanafi school permits narrating hadith by meaning, provided the narrator understands the meaning. This affects which type of dabit is required.
Because narration by meaning is allowed, apparent accuracy suffices as long as the legal meaning is preserved.
4
Connect loss of eyesight to impairment of dabit
Loss of eyesight is a risk factor that can lead to errors, but it does not automatically invalidate a narrator's accuracy. Accuracy is assessed by comparing narrations with those of reliable narrators.
The passage states that frequent disagreement harms dabit, not loss of eyesight per se.
5
Derive the ruling on narrator reliability
A narrator who meets the conditions (apparent dabit) is considered trustworthy (thiqah) and his narrations are accepted, even if he narrates by meaning.
This is the operative ruling in Hanafi usul.

رابعاً. ذهاب البصر: من المعروف في بدائع علم الحديث أن الضبط شرط أساسي في صحة الحديث النبوي الشريف، والضبط: هو إتقان ما يرويه الراوي بأن يكون متيقظاً لما يروي غير مغفل، حافظاً لروايته إن روى من حفظه ضابطاً لكتابه إن روى من الكتاب عالماً بمعنى ما يرويه، وبما يحيل المعنى عن المراد إن روى بالمعنى، حتى يثق المطلع على روايته والمتتبع لأحواله بأنه أدى الأمانة كما تحملها، لم يغير منها شيئاً، وهذا مناط التفاضل بين الرواة الثقات، فإذا كان الراوي عدلاً ضابطاً سمي ثقة. ويعرف ضبطه بموافقة الثقات الضابطين المتقنين إذا اعتبر حديثه بحديثهم، ولا تضر مخالفته النادرة لهم، فإن كثرت مخالفته لهم، وندرت الموافقة، اختل ضبطه ولم يحتج بحديثه. والضبط نوعان: ظاهر وباطن. فالظاهر من حيث اللغة. والباطن: ضبط معناه من حيث تعلق الحكم الشرعي به، وهو الفقه ومطلق الضبط الذي هو شرط الراوي، هو الضبط ظاهراً عند الأكثر؛ لأنه يجوز نقل الحديث بالمعنى عند الكثير من العلماء.
Fourth: loss of eyesight. It is well-known in the fundamentals of hadith science that accuracy (dabit) is a basic condition for the authenticity of the noble prophetic hadith. Dabit is: mastery of what the narrator narrates, so that he is attentive to what he narrates, not negligent; he memorizes his narration if he narrates from memory, and he is accurate with his book if he narrates from a book; he knows the meaning of what he narrates, and [knows] what would change the meaning from the intended if he narrates by meaning, so that the one who examines his narration and follows his conditions is confident that he fulfilled the trust as he received it, without changing anything. This is the criterion of excellence among trustworthy narrators. If the narrator is upright and accurate, he is called trustworthy. His accuracy is known by his agreement with the accurate, precise trustworthy narrators when his hadith are compared with theirs. His rare disagreement with them does not harm. If his disagreement with them is frequent and agreement is rare, his accuracy is compromised and his hadith are not used as evidence. Accuracy is of two types: apparent and hidden. The apparent is with respect to language. The hidden is accuracy of meaning with respect to the connection of a legal ruling to it; it is fiqh. And absolute accuracy, which is the condition of the narrator, is apparent accuracy according to the majority, because narrating hadith by meaning is permissible according to many scholars.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage introduces a fourth factor affecting hadith acceptance: loss of eyesight, which can lead to errors in transmission. It then defines dabit (accuracy), a crucial condition for narrator reliability. Dabit requires the narrator to be precise, whether narrating from memory or from a book, and to understand the meaning to avoid distorting it when narrating by meaning. A narrator is considered trustworthy only if he is both upright and accurate. Accuracy is verified by comparing his narrations with those of other reliable narrators: frequent agreement indicates accuracy, while frequent disagreement indicates weakness. Finally, accuracy is divided into two types: apparent (linguistic precision) and hidden (understanding of legal implications). In Hanafi usul, apparent accuracy suffices, since narrating by meaning is allowed as long as the legal meaning is preserved.

Key Terms
الضبط (al-dabit): Accuracy and precision in narrating hadith, ensuring the narration is transmitted as received.
ثقة (thiqah): A narrator who is both upright and accurate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is a narrator's accuracy (dabit) known?
A) By his own assertion.
B) By the number of hadith he narrates.
C) By comparing his narrations with those of other accurate, trustworthy narrators.
D) By his loss of eyesight.

Key Takeaway
A narrator's accuracy is measured by comparison with other reliable narrators; the Hanafi school requires only apparent (linguistic) accuracy for hadith acceptance, permitting narration by meaning.

The Relative Nature of Dabt and Its Impact on Hadith Differences
Explaining how narrator precision varies and causes differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify examples of regional and contextual variations in narrator precision and explain how such variations lead to differences in hadith texts and chains.

Core Idea
A narrator's precision (dabt) is not absolute; it varies by region, time, and whether narrating from a book or memory.

In hadith sciences, precision (dabt) is a key condition for accepting narrations. However, as this passage explains, precision is relative—it can fluctuate even among trustworthy narrators based on circumstances. Understanding this relativity helps us reconcile conflicting reports and recognize why Hanafi usul scholars scrutinize the mode and context of transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept of dabt
Define dabt as precision in preserving and transmitting hadith. Note that it is a condition for hadith authenticity.
Dabt is not a binary quality; it has degrees.
2
Recognize the relativity of dabt
Analyze the examples of Ma'mar ibn Rashid and Isma'il ibn 'Ayyash. Their dabt varied by region because their books were not always with them.
Ma'mar in Yemen (books present) vs. Basra (books absent).
3
Examine the book vs. memory pattern
Study the case of Sharik al-Qadi: narrators with sound books but weak memory. Their narrations from memory are unreliable; from books are authentic.
This shows dabt depends on the mode of transmission.
4
Apply to Hanafi usul
Consider how such variations affect which narrations are accepted in fiqh. Differences in dabt lead to differences in hadith texts and chains, causing ikhtilaf in rulings.
Hanafi scholars weigh the context of transmission when evaluating conflicting hadiths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل التمهيدي بيان ماهية الاختلاف
لمعمر بن راشد قال ابن رجب: حديثه بالبصرة فيه اضطراب كثير، وحديثه باليمن جيد، وَقَالَ الإمام أحمد في رِوَايَة الأثرم: حَدِيث عَبد الرزاق عن معمر أحب إلي من حَدِيث هؤلاء البصريين كَانَ يتعاهد كتبه وينظر يعني باليمن، وَكَانَ يحدّثهم بخطأ بالبصرة. وَقَالَ يعقوب بن شيبة: سَمَاع أهل البصرة من معمر، حين قدم عليهم فيه اضطراب؛ لأن كتبه لَمْ تَكُنْ مَعَهُ. ومن هَؤُلاَءِ أَيْضاً: إسماعيل بن عياش قَالَ مُحَمَّد بن عثمان بن أبي شيبة: سَمِعْتُ يَحْيَى بن مَعِيْنِ يَقُول: إسماعيل بن عياش ثقة فِيْمَا رَوَى عَنْ الشاميين، وأما روايته عَنْ أهل الحجاز فإن كتابه ضاع فخلط في حفظه عَنْهُمْ.

سادساً. عدم الضبط:
سبق الكلام أن الضبط من شروط صحة الحَدِيث الأساسية؛ ولكن بعض الرُّوَاة - وإن كانوا ضابطين - إلا أنهم في بعض الأحايين يخف ضبطهم لبعض الأحاديث خاصة، وَهُوَ أمرٌ اعتيادي يحصل لبني الإنسان؛ لأن الضبط كما سبق أمرٌ نسبي. وهذا الباب الذي يمكن من خلاله دخول الوهم في بعض أحاديث الثقات يعد سبباً من أسباب اختلاف الروايات متناً وإسناداً مِمَّا يؤدي بالمحصلة النهائية إلى حصول بعض الاختلافات في بَعْض الأحاديث. وهذا الأمر نراه جلياً في أحاديث الثقات التي أخطؤوا فيها. وما يأتي في كثير من الأمثلة اللاحقة دليل لما أصلناه في أن الضبط أمر نسبي ينفك عَنْ بعض الثقات أحياناً في بعض الأحاديث.

وَكَانَ هناك رواة، لَهُمْ كتب صحيحة متقنة وفي حفظهم شيء وهؤلاء كانوا أحياناً إذا حدثوا من حفظهم غلطوا وإذا حدثوا من كتابهم أصابوا، وهذا أمر أولاه العلماء عناية؛ لأن فِيْهِ مزيد ضبط في رِوَايَة هَذَا الرَّاوِي خاصة، ومن الأمثلة عَلَى ذَلِكَ شريك القاضي وَهُوَ شريك بن عَبْد الله النخعي، الكوفي، القاضي بواسط، ثُمَّ الكوفة، أبـو عبد الله: صدوق يخطئ كثيراً، تغير حفظه منذ ولي القضاء بالكوفة.

قَالَ فِيْهِ مُحَمَّد بن عَبْد الله بن عمار الموصلي: «شريك كتبه صحاح فمن سَمِعَ مِنْهُ من كتبه فهو صَحِيح، قَالَ: وَلَمْ يَسْمَع من شريك من كتابه إلا إسحاق الأزرق. وَقَالَ فِيْهِ يعقوب بن شيبة: كتبه صحاح. وفي رِوَايَة الْخَطِيْب البغدادي عَنْ يعقوب في شريك: «ثقة صدوق، صَحِيح الكتاب رديء الحفظ مضطربه.

ومن الأمور التي يدخل الاختلاف بسببها لعدم الضبط، هو عدم الضبط في بلد معين، وَهُوَ أَن يَكُون الرَّاوِي ضابطاً إلا أنه في سماعه لحديث أهل بلد معين لا يَكُون
The introductory chapter: Explanation of the nature of difference. Regarding Ma'mar ibn Rashid: Ibn Rajab said: His hadith in Basra contains much disorder, but his hadith in Yemen is good. Imam Ahmad said in the narration of al-Athram: The hadith of Abd al-Razzaq from Ma'mar is more beloved to me than the hadith of these Basrans; he used to review his books and check, meaning in Yemen, and he would narrate to them with error in Basra. Ya'qub ibn Shaybah said: The hearing of the people of Basra from Ma'mar when he came to them contains disorder because his books were not with him. Among these also is Isma'il ibn 'Ayyash: Muhammad ibn 'Uthman ibn Abi Shaybah said: I heard Yahya ibn Ma'in say: Isma'il ibn 'Ayyash is trustworthy in what he narrated from the Syrians, but as for his narration from the people of Hijaz, his book was lost so he confused in his memory from them.

Sixth: Lack of precision. The discussion has preceded that precision is among the basic conditions for the authenticity of hadith; however, some narrators - even if they are precise - in some cases their precision weakens for certain hadiths in particular, and this is a usual matter that happens to humans because precision, as mentioned, is relative. This door through which doubt can enter some hadiths of trustworthy narrators is considered a cause of differences in narrations in text and chain, leading in the final outcome to the occurrence of some differences in some hadiths. And this matter we see clearly in the hadiths of trustworthy narrators in which they erred. And what comes in many later examples is evidence for what we have established that precision is relative, sometimes detaching from some trustworthy narrators in some hadiths.

And there were narrators who had sound, meticulous books but in their memory there was something. These ones would sometimes err when they narrated from memory, and when they narrated from their books they would be correct. And this matter the scholars paid attention to because in it there is greater precision in the narration of this particular narrator. Among examples of that is Sharik al-Qadi, and he is Sharik ibn 'Abd Allah al-Nakha'i, al-Kufi, the judge in Wasit then Kufa, Abu 'Abd Allah: truthful, he errs much, his memory changed since he became judge in Kufa.

Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah ibn 'Ammar al-Mawsili said about him: 'Sharik's books are sound, so whoever heard from him from his books, it is authentic. He said: No one heard from Sharik from his book except Ishaq al-Azraq.' Ya'qub ibn Shaybah said about him: 'His books are sound.' And in the narration of al-Khatib al-Baghdadi from Ya'qub regarding Sharik: 'Trustworthy, truthful, sound in book, poor in memory, disturbed.'

And among the matters by which difference enters due to lack of precision is lack of precision in a specific region, which is that the narrator is precise except that in his hearing of hadith of the people of a specific region he is not...
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is from the introductory chapter of the book, explaining the nature of differences in hadith. It identifies 'lack of precision' (عدم الضبط) as a sixth cause of discrepancy in hadith texts and chains, which in turn leads to differences in fiqh rulings. The author first gives examples of narrators whose reliability varies by region: Ma'mar ibn Rashid was more reliable in Yemen than in Basra because his books were with him in Yemen; similarly, Isma'il ibn 'Ayyash was trustworthy for Syrian narrations but confused for Hijazi narrations after his book was lost. The author then defines precision as a relative condition, sometimes decreasing even in trustworthy narrators for specific hadiths. The main discussion focuses on narrators with sound books but weak memory, such as Sharik al-Qadi. When such narrators narrated from memory, they erred; when from their written books, they were accurate. The author cites critical opinions to emphasize that the reliability of a narrator can depend on the source (book vs. memory) and the region. This passage is crucial for Hanafi usul because hadith differences often stem from such variations in narrator precision, affecting which narrations are accepted in deriving legal rulings.

Key Terms
الضبط (al-dabt): Precision in preserving and transmitting hadith; a relative quality that may vary by region or time.
ثقة (thiqa): Trustworthy narrator; one whose narration is generally accepted due to reliability.
صدوق (saduq): Truthful narrator but may have errors; used for narrators like Sharik who are truthful but make mistakes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He lost his books
B) His memory changed after becoming judge
C) He only narrated from memory
D) He mixed up Syrian and Hijazi hadiths

Key Takeaway
Lack of precision is a relative condition; a narrator may be reliable in one context but not another, which is a legitimate cause of hadith differences.

Tadlīs al-Isnād: Definition and Its Impact on Hadith Authenticity
Definition of tadlis and explanation of tadlis al-isnad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tadlīs al-isnād and identify the ambiguous wording that triggers its ruling.

Core Idea
Tadlīs al-isnād conceals a missing link using ambiguous wording; such hadith is rejected unless hearing is confirmed.

Tadlīs (concealment) is a major cause of variation in hadith texts and chains. Understanding its definition and types is crucial for evaluating hadith authenticity and their use in legal derivation. This lesson focuses on the first type: tadlīs al-isnād, where a narrator uses ambiguous phrases that do not confirm direct hearing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic meaning of tadlīs
Derived from 'dals' (darkness) meaning mixing of darkness, and hiding a defect. This sets the conceptual foundation.
2
Distinguish between linguistic and technical definitions
Technically, tadlīs is narrating from someone met using wording that does not confirm direct hearing, thus concealing the lack of audition.
The key is that the narrator met the person but did not hear directly.
3
Analyze the first type: tadlīs al-isnād
The narrator uses ambiguous phrases like 'an, qāla, haddath, rawā, dhakara instead of explicit hearing terms like haddathanā, akhbaranā.
Ambiguous wording allows both connection and disconnection in the chain.
4
Recognize the consequence
Hadith scholars do not accept such narrations unless the narrator explicitly states hearing. This impacts the hadith's admissibility as evidence in usul al-fiqh.
The ruling protects the integrity of the chain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سابعاً. التدليس: هُوَ أحد الأسباب الرئيسة التي تدخل الاختلاف في المتون والأسانيد؛ لأن التدليس يكشف عَنْ سقوط راءٍ أحياناً فيكون لهذا الساقط دور في اختلاف الأسانيد والمتون ولما كَانَ الأمر عَلَى هَذِهِ الشاكلة، فلا بد لنا من تفصيل القول في التدليس: فالتدليس لغة: من الدَّلس - بالتحريك - وَهُوَ اختلاط الظلام، والتدليس: إخفاء العيب وكتمانه.
أما في الاصطلاح، فإن التدليس عندهم يتنوع إلى عدة أنواع:
الأول: تدليس الإسناد: وَهُوَ أن يروي الرَّاوِي عمن لقيه ما لَمْ يسمعه منه بصيغة محتملة". والمراد من الصيغة المحتملة: أن لا يصرح بالسماع أو الإخبار مثل: حَدَّثَنَا، وأخبرنا، وأنبأنا، وسمعت وَقَالَ لنا، وإنما يجيء بلفظ يحتمل الاتصال وعدمه، مثل: إن وعن وَقَالَ، وحدّث، وروى، وذكر، لذا لَمْ يقبل الْمُحَدِّثُوْنَ حَدِيث المدلس ما لم يصرح بالسماع.
(۱) انظر في التدليس: مَعْرِفَة علوم الْحَدِيث ۱۰۳، والمدخل إلى الإكليل: ۳۹، والكفاية (٥٠۸ ت، ٣٥٥ هـ)، والتمهيد ١٥/١، وجامع الأصول ١٦٧/١، ومعرفة أنواع علم الحَدِيث: ٦٦ طبعة نور الدين، ١٥٦ طبعتنا، والإرشاد ۲۰٥/١، والتقريب ٦٣ وطبعتنا ۱۰۹ والاقتراح ۲۰۹ والمنهل الروي: ۷۲ والخلاصة: ٧٤، والموقظة: ٤٧، وجامع التحصيل ٩٧، والتذكرة ١٦، ومحاسن الاصطلاح: ١٦٥، وشرح التبصرة والتذكرة ۱۷۹/١ الطبعة العلمية و ۲۲٤/١ طبعتنا، والتقييد والإيضاح ٩٥، ونزهة النظر: ۱۱۳، والنكت عَلَى كتاب ابن الصلاح ٦١٤/٢، ومقدمة طبقات المدلسين: ۱۳، والمختصر: ۱۳۲ وفتح المغيث ١٩٦/١، وألفية السيوطي: ۳۳، وتوضيح الأفكار ٣٤٦/١، وظفر الأماني: ۳۷۳، وقواعد التحديث: ١٣٢.
(۲) الصحاح (۹۳۰/۳)، ولسان العرب ٨٦/٦، وتاج العروس ٨٤/١٦ مادة (دلس). (۳) انظر: مَعْرِفَة علوم الْحَدِيث: ۱۰۳، وجامع الأصول: ١٦٧، ومعرفة أنواع علم الْحَدِيث: ٦٦ طبعة نور الدين و ١٥٧ طبعتنا وإرشاد طلاب الحقائق ۲۰٥/١، وجامع التحصيل: ٩٧، وشرح ألفية العراقي: ٣٣ للسيوطي، وتوضيح الأفكار ٣٤٧/١، وظفر الأماني: ٣٧٤. (٤) ثُمَّ شاع تخصيص "أخبرنا" في العصور المتأخرة بالإجازة. انظر: مَعْرِفَة أنواع علم الْحَدِيث: ٦٦ طبعة نور الدين و ١٥٩ طبعتنا. (٥) انظر: مَعْرِفَة أنواع علم الْحَدِيث: ٦٧ طبعة نور الدين و ١٥٩ طبعتنا وإرشاد طلاب الحقائق ۱/ ۲۱۰، والتقريب ٦٥ والمقنع ١٥٧/١، وشرح التبصرة والتذكرة ١٨٤/١ الطبعة العلمية، و۱/ ۲۳۲ طبعتنا، والعواصم والقواصم ٦٠/٣، وطبقات المدلسين: ١٦.
Seventh: Tadlīs. It is one of the main causes that introduces discrepancy in texts and chains, because tadlīs reveals the dropping of a narrator sometimes, and this dropped narrator has a role in the difference of chains and texts. Since the matter is on this footing, we must detail the discussion on tadlīs. Tadlīs linguistically: from al-dals (with fatḥa), which is the mixing of darkness, and tadlīs: hiding a defect and concealing it. As for terminology, tadlīs according to them is divided into several types: The first: Tadlīs al-isnād: it is that the narrator narrates from someone he met what he did not hear from him, using a wording that is ambiguous. And what is meant by ambiguous wording is that he does not explicitly state hearing or informing, such as: haddathanā, akhbaranā, anba'anā, sami'tu, qāla lanā, but rather uses a wording that allows for both connection and disconnection, such as: in, 'an, qāla, haddath, rawā, dhakara. Therefore, the muhaddithūn do not accept the hadith of the mudallis unless he explicitly states hearing.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage defines tadlīs (concealment) as a major cause of variation in hadith texts and chains. It begins with the linguistic meaning: from 'dals' (darkness) and 'ikhfā' al-'ayb' (hiding a defect). The technical definition follows. The first type is tadlīs al-isnād, where a narrator uses ambiguous wording (like 'an, qāla) that does not confirm direct hearing, even though he met the narrator. This ambiguity creates doubt about the chain's continuity. The rule among hadith scholars is that such a narration is not accepted unless the narrator explicitly states hearing (e.g., haddathanā). This principle is essential for evaluating the authenticity of hadith and their use in legal derivation in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
التدليس (al-tadlīs): Concealing a defect in the chain by using ambiguous wording
تدليس الإسناد (tadlīs al-isnād): Narrating from a contemporary using wording that does not confirm hearing

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the rule regarding a hadith narrated through tadlīs al-isnād?
A) It is accepted without question.
B) It is accepted only if the narrator is trustworthy.
C) It is not accepted unless the narrator explicitly states hearing (e.g., haddathanā).
D) It is rejected outright regardless of any clarification.

Key Takeaway
Tadlīs al-isnād requires a narrator to confirm direct hearing for the hadith to be accepted; ambiguous wording renders the chain suspect.

Definition of Tadlis al-Isnad
Defining tadlis linguistically and introducing the first type: tadlis al-isnad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tadlis al-isnad, distinguish it from its linguistic meaning, and apply the Hanafi usul condition that ambiguous narrations require explicit hearing confirmation.

Core Idea
Tadlis al-isnad: a narrator's ambiguous wording conceals a missing direct hearing, rendering the hadith rejected unless hearing is confirmed.

In hadith studies, understanding the types of tadlis is crucial for evaluating narrations. This lesson presents the linguistic and terminological definition of tadlis and focuses on the first type: tadlis al-isnad. We will dissect this definition and see how it affects the acceptance of hadith in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic origin
Tadlis comes from 'dalas' meaning mixing of darkness; hence hiding a defect.
2
State the terminological definition
Narrating from someone met but not directly heard, using ambiguous wording.
3
Recognize the key condition
The narrator must have met the shaykh (otherwise it would be irsal).
4
Identify the ambiguous wording
Words like 'an, qala, haddatha, rawa that could imply connection or disconnection.
5
Understand the ruling
Such narrations are not accepted unless explicit hearing is confirmed (sami'tu, haddathana).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سابعاً. التدليس(۱): هُوَ أحد الأسباب الرئيسة التي تدخل الاختلاف في المتون والأسانيد؛ لأن التدليس يكشف عَنْ سقوط راءٍ أحياناً فيكون لهذا الساقط دور في اختلاف الأسانيد والمتون ولما كَانَ الأمر عَلَى هَذِهِ الشاكلة، فلا بد لنا من تفصيل القول في التدليس: فالتدليس لغة: من الدَّلس - بالتحريك - وَهُوَ اختلاط الظلام، والتدليس: إخفاء العيب وكتمانه (۲).
أما في الاصطلاح، فإن التدليس عندهم يتنوع إلى عدة أنواع:
الأول: تدليس الإسناد: وَهُوَ أن يروي الرَّاوِي عمن لقيه ما لَمْ يسمعه منه بصيغة محتملة". والمراد من الصيغة المحتملة: أن لا يصرح بالسماع أو الإخبار مثل: حَدَّثَنَا، وأخبرنا () ،وأنبأنا، وسمعت وَقَالَ لنا، وإنما يجيء بلفظ يحتمل الاتصال وعدمه، مثل: إن وعن وَقَالَ، وحدّث، وروى، وذكر ، لذا لَمْ يقبل الْمُحَدِّثُوْنَ حَدِيث المدلس ما لم يصرح بالسماع).
Seventh: Tadlis (1): It is one of the main causes that introduce difference in texts (mutun) and chains (asanid); because tadlis sometimes reveals the dropping of a narrator, and this dropped narrator has a role in the difference of chains and texts. Since the matter is of this nature, we must detail the discussion on tadlis: Tadlis linguistically: from al-dalas (with vowel movement) which is the mixing of darkness, and tadlis: hiding and concealing a defect (2). As for terminologically, tadlis according to them is divided into several types: First: Tadlis al-Isnad: It is that a narrator relates from someone he met what he did not hear from him using a probable wording. What is meant by probable wording is that he does not explicitly state hearing or reporting such as haddathana, akhbarana, anba'ana, sami'tu, qala lana, but rather uses a wording that could imply connection or disconnection, such as 'an, qala, haddatha, rawa, dhakara. Therefore, the muhaddithun do not accept the hadith of a mudallis unless he explicitly states hearing (5).
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the discussion on tadlis (deception/dissimulation) in hadith narration, identified as a primary source of disagreement in both chains (asanid) and texts (mutun). The author begins with a linguistic definition: tadlis derives from 'dalas,' meaning the mixing of darkness, hence concealing a defect. Then the terminological definition follows: it involves a narrator using ambiguous wording that suggests direct hearing without actually stating it. The first type, tadlis al-isnad, is defined: a narrator who met a shaykh but did not hear the hadith directly from him, yet uses a phrase like 'an or qala that could imply either connection or disconnection. Because of this ambiguity, hadith scholars do not accept such narrations unless the narrator explicitly confirms hearing (using terms like sami'tu). This is purely a hadith terminology classification; the discussion is foundational for understanding how differences in chains can lead to legal disagreement.

Key Terms
تدليس (tadlis): Linguistically: mixing or darkness; terminologically: narrating with ambiguity to hide a defect in the chain.
تدليس الإسناد (tadlis al-isnad): Narrating from someone met without directly hearing from them, using ambiguous wording.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The narrator never met the shaykh
B) The narrator met the shaykh but did not hear the hadith directly from him
C) The narrator heard the hadith from another source
D) The narrator uses explicit wording like 'haddathana'

Key Takeaway
Tadlis al-isnad is a form of concealment where ambiguous wording hides the lack of direct hearing; it is a critical concept for evaluating hadith authenticity in Hanafi usul.

Tadlis al-Shuyukh: Definition and Classification
Explaining tadlis al-shuyukh and its ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tadlis al-shuyukh, distinguish it from tadlis al-isnad, and apply the Hanafi rule on its varying disapproval based on motive.

Core Idea
Tadlis al-Shuyukh obscures the teacher's identity and is lighter than tadlis al-isnad, with its ruling depending on motive.

This passage introduces the second type of tadlis: tadlis al-shuyukh. Unlike tadlis al-isnad which hides a gap in the chain, tadlis al-shuyukh involves disguising a shaykh's name or kunya to make it difficult for others to assess his reliability. The Hanafi school treats this type as less severe, but the degree of disapproval varies with the narrator's motive. Understanding this distinction is crucial when evaluating the reliability of narrators in hadith chains used for deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal classification
Identify tadlis al-shuyukh as the act of narrating from a shaykh using an unfamiliar name/kunya to obscure identity. Note the passage states it is 'lighter in ruling than the previous one' (tadlis al-isnad).
'Lighter' means it does not automatically invalidate the hadith.
2
Compare with tadlis al-isnad
Contrast tadlis al-shuyukh with tadlis al-isnad. Tadlis al-isnad involves a gap in the chain; tadlis al-shuyukh only obscures the teacher's identity. The passage calls it 'lighter' because it does not break continuity.
3
Analyse the motive and its effect on ruling
List the four possible motives given: the teacher is not trustworthy, is younger than the narrator, died later with shared students, or the narrator prefers not to repeat the same name. The passage states: 'the degree of disapproval varies according to the reason that prompts it.'
If the teacher is unreliable, the tadlis is worse; if done to avoid repetition, it is less reprehensible.
4
Derive the usul principle
From the analysis, derive the principle: tadlis al-shuyukh does not automatically reject a hadith; the narrator's overall trustworthiness and the reason for tadlis determine acceptance.
This is consistent with the Hanafi emphasis on the narrator's 'adalah (moral probity) and dabit (accuracy).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني: تدليس الشيوخ:
وَهُوَ أن يأتي باسم شيخه أو كنيته عَلَى خلاف المشهور به تعمية لأمره وتوعيراً للوقوف على حاله). وهذا النوع حكمه أخف من السابق، وفي هذا النوع تضييع للمروي عَنْهُ وللمروي وتوعير لطريق مَعْرِفَة حالهما. ثُمَّ إن الحال في كراهيته يختلف بحسب الغرض الحامل عَلَيْهِ، إِذْ إن من يدلس هَذَا التدليس قد يحمله كون شيخه الَّذِي غيّر سمته غَيْر ثقة، أو أصغر من الرَّاوِي عَنْهُ، أو متأخر الوفاة قد شاركه في السَّمَاعَ مِنْهُ جَمَاعَة دونه، أو كونه كثير الرِّوَايَة عَنْهُ فلا يحب تكرار شخص عَلَى صورة واحدة(٢).
Second: Tadlis al-Shuyukh: It is that a narrator mentions the name or kunya of his shaykh in a way contrary to what is well-known about him, in order to obscure his affair and make it difficult to ascertain his condition. This type is lighter in ruling than the previous one. In this type, there is a waste of the one narrated from and the narrated, and a difficulty in knowing their condition. Then the degree of disapproval varies according to the reason that prompts it, since one who commits this tadlis may be motivated by the fact that his shaykh, whose description he altered, is not trustworthy, or is younger than the narrator, or died later such that a group below him share in hearing from him, or that he narrates frequently from him and does not like to repeat a person in one form (2).
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
The passage discusses the second type of tadlis: tadlis al-shuyukh. Here, the narrator deliberately uses a name, nickname, or title for his teacher that is not the commonly known one, making it hard for others to identify the teacher and assess his reliability. The author notes that this type is less severe than tadlis al-isnad (which involves a chain gap), but still problematic because it obscures the identity of the narrator's source. The degree of disapproval, however, depends on the motive: if the teacher is unreliable, the tadlis is worse; if done to avoid repetition or because the teacher is younger, it may be less reprehensible. This classification is important in Hanafi usul because it affects how we evaluate the narrators in a chain, which in turn affects whether a hadith can be used as evidence for a ruling.

Key Terms
تدليس الشيوخ (tadlis al-shuyukh): A narrator disguises his teacher's identity by using an unfamiliar name or title.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the passage, what is the primary effect of tadlis al-shuyukh?
A) It always invalidates the hadith.
B) It makes it difficult to know the condition of the shaykh and the hadith.
C) It is worse than tadlis al-isnad.
D) It is permissible (mubah) without dislike.

Key Takeaway
Tadlis al-shuyukh is a lighter form of tadlis that does not invalidate a hadith; its severity depends on the narrator's motive.

Tadlis al-Taswiyah: Definition and Hanafi Assessment
Explaining tadlis al-taswiyah: dropping a weak narrator between two trustworthy ones

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tadlis al-taswiyah, distinguish it from other tadlis types, and apply the Hanafi rule of rejecting narrations from mudallis in such cases unless explicitly confirmed.

Core Idea
Tadlis al-taswiyah hides a weak narrator between two trustworthy ones – the hadith is rejected unless explicit confirmation is given.

This lesson unpacks the most severe form of tadlis – tadlis al-taswiyah. The passage defines it, gives real examples from early narrators, and hints at the Hanafi position. Understanding this concept is crucial because it directly affects the reliability of a hadith chain and thus the legal rulings derived from it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition
Read the Arabic definition: what does the mudallis do? He narrates from his shaykh, then drops a weak narrator who lies between two trustworthy ones, and uses ambiguous wording to make the chain appear continuous.
The key is 'dropping a weak link' between two thiqat.
2
Distinguish from other tadlis
Tadlis al-taswiyah is not the same as tadlis al-isnad (omitting the shaykh) or tadlis al-shuyukh (using a different name). Here the weak narrator is specifically removed to 'level' the chain.
This type is considered most objectionable.
3
Note the condition and famous practitioners
The mudallis must have heard from both the upper and lower trustworthy narrators, and must use tahdith/ikhbar phrasing. Famous examples: al-Walid bin Muslim and Baqiyya bin al-Walid.
These narrators are known for this practice.
4
Apply the Hanafi rule
In Hanafi usul, such a chain is considered marjuh (weak). The hadith is rejected unless the mudallis explicitly confirms hearing from the upper shaykh. This affects whether a hadith can be used as dalil.
This is stricter than some other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث: تدليس التسوية (۳):
وَهُوَ أن يروي عَنْ شيخه، ثُمَّ يسقط ضعيفاً بَيْنَ ثقتين قَدْ سَمِعَ أحدهما من الآخر أو لقيه، ويرويه بصيغة محتملة بَيْنَ الثقتين). وممن اشتهر بهذا النوع: الوليد بن مُسْلِم، وبقية بن الوليد ) . وهذا النوع من التدليس يشترط فيه التحديث والإخبار من المدلس إلى آخره).
Third: Tadlis al-Taswiyah (3): It is that a narrator narrates from his shaykh, then drops a weak narrator between two trustworthy ones who either heard from one another or met, and he narrates it with a probable wording between the two trustworthy ones. Among those famous for this type are: al-Walid bin Muslim and Baqiyya bin al-Walid (5). This type of tadlis requires the mudallis to have narrated (tahdith) and informed (ikhbar) until the end (7).
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
The passage introduces tadlis al-taswiyah, the most severe form of tadlis. In this type, the narrator deletes a weak link that appears between two trustworthy narrators in the chain, using ambiguous phrasing to make the chain appear 'leveled' (musawwa) with only trustworthy names. The author mentions two famous practitioners: al-Walid bin Muslim and Baqiyya bin al-Walid. This type is particularly dangerous because it removes a known weak narrator, making the chain seem stronger than it is. The condition mentioned is that the mudallis must use tahdith (like 'haddathana') or ikhbar (like 'akhbarana') to complete the chain, implying that the dropped link is omitted from the very beginning of the narration. In Hanafi usul, such chains are highly suspect because they hide a weakness that would affect the legal validity of a hadith.

Key Terms
تدليس التسوية (tadlis al-taswiyah): Dropping a weak narrator between two trustworthy ones in narration.
تحديث وإخبار (tahdith wa ikhbar): Explicit forms of narration ('haddathana', 'akhbarana') that confirm direct hearing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It uses a non-standard name for the shaykh
C) It omits the entire beginning of the chain
D) It is only found in narrations from al-Walid and Baqiyya

Key Takeaway
Tadlis al-taswiyah is the most severe tadlis because it deliberately hides a weak link; Hanafis reject such hadith unless the narrator explicitly confirms direct hearing.

The Seven Types of Tadlis and Their Impact
Defines seven types of tadlis with a critical example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the seven types of tadlis and explain how tadlis can affect the authenticity of a hadith chain.

Core Idea
Tadlis is a hidden defect that weakens a hadith only if the concealed link is unreliable.

Hadith scholars identified several forms of tadlis (concealment) in transmission. This lesson introduces the seven types, focusing on the most common ones that cause differences in hadith authenticity. Understanding these types is crucial for evaluating the reliability of a hadith chain in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
List the seven types of tadlis
Name all seven types mentioned in the passage: tadlis al-isnad (first), tadlis al-shuyukh (second), tadlis al-‘atf, tadlis al-sukut, tadlis al-qat‘, tadlis siyagh al-ada', and 'an‘anat al-mudallis. Note that the passage only describes types 4-7 explicitly, but the first three are implied.
The first two are the most well-known and relevant for hadith criticism.
2
Differentiate between well-known and uncommon types
Identify that only the first two types (tadlis al-isnad and tadlis al-shuyukh) are commonly discussed; the others are less frequent. When 'tadlis' is used without qualification, it usually means the first type.
This helps prioritize study: focus on tadlis al-isnad (concealing a weak link) and tadlis al-shuyukh (naming a shaykh in a misleading way).
3
Analyze the example of Ibn Jurayj
Apply the definition of tadlis to the hadith 'Do not urinate standing'. Ibn Jurayj used 'an'anah (saying 'from Nafi‘') without explicit hearing. Critics discovered a hidden weak narrator ('Abd al-Karim) between him and Nafi‘, revealing tadlis.
Even though Ibn Jurayj was generally reliable, the hidden link weakened this particular narration.
4
Assess the impact of tadlis on authenticity
Conclude that tadlis does not automatically invalidate a hadith. It only weakens the chain if the concealed narrator is found to be weak or unknown. If the hidden link is reliable, the hadith remains acceptable.
Hanafi usul: the 'an'anah of a mudallis is not accepted unless his direct hearing from that shaykh is confirmed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل التمهيدي بيان ماهية الاختلاف
الرابع: تدليس العطف:
وَهُوَ مثل أن يقول الرَّاوِي: حَدَّثَنَا فُلان وفلان، وَهُوَ لَمْ يَسْمَع من الثاني.
الخامس تدليس السكوت
وَهُوَ كأن يقول الرَّاوِي: حَدَّثَنَا أَوْ سَمِعْتُ، ثُمَّ يسكت برهة، ثُمَّ يقول: هشام بن عروة أو الأعمش موهماً أنه سَمِعَ منهما، وليس كذلك.
السادس: تدليس القطع
وَهُوَ أن يحذف الصيغة ويقتصر عَلَى قوله مثلاً: الزهري عَنْ أنس.
السابع: تدليس صيغ الأداء:
وَهُوَ ما يقع من الْمُحَدِّثِينَ من التعبير بالتحديث أو الإخبار عن الإجازة موهماً للسماع، وَلَمْ يَكُنْ تحمله لِذَلِكَ المروي عن طريق السَّماع.
وهذه الأنواع السبعة ليست كلها مشتهرة إنما المشتهر منها والشائع الأول والثاني وعند الإطلاق يراد الأول. وهذا القسم هُوَ الَّذِي لَهُ دورٌ في الاختلافات الحديثية متوناً وأسانيد، إذ قَدْ يكشف خلال البحث بَعْدَ التنقير والتفتيش عن سقوط رجل من الإسناد وربما كَانَ هَذَا الساقط ضعيفاً أَوْ في حفظه شيء، أو لَمْ يضبط حديثه هَذَا.
ومن الأمثلة عَلَى ذَلِكَ ما رَوَاهُ ابن حبان من طريق ابن جريج، عَنْ نافع، عَنْ ابن عمر، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لا تَبُل قائماً». وهذا الإسناد رجاله ثقات إلا أنَّ ابن جريج مدلس وَقَدْ عنعن هنا وَلَمْ يصرح بسماعه من نافع، وَهُوَ قَدْ سَمِعَ من نافع أحاديث كثيرة، فهُوَ معروف بالرواية عَنْهُ، وروايته عَنْهُ في الكتب الستة. ولكن النقاد ببصيرتهم الناقدة ونظرهم الثاقب كشفوا أنَّ في هَذَا السند واسطة بَيْنَ ابن جريج ونافع، وأن ابن جريج لم يسمعه من نافع مباشرة، بَلْ سمعه من عبد الكريم بن أبي المخارق الضعيف، وقد صرّح ابن جريج في بعض طرق الحَدِيث بهذا الساقط، فبان تدليسه؛ فَقَدْ رَوَى عَبْد الرزاق، ومِنْ طریقه ابن ماجه، وأبو عوانة، وابن عدي، وتمام الرازي،
The preliminary chapter: Explanation of the nature of difference. Fourth: Tadlis of conjunction: It is like the narrator saying: 'So-and-so and so-and-so narrated to us,' while he did not hear from the second. Fifth: Tadlis of silence: It is like the narrator saying: 'So-and-so narrated to us' or 'I heard,' then he pauses for a moment, then says: 'Hisham ibn Urwah' or 'al-A'mash,' falsely implying that he heard from them, while it is not so. Sixth: Tadlis of cutting: It is to omit the formula and limit oneself to saying, for example: 'al-Zuhri from Anas.' Seventh: Tadlis of performance formulas: It is what occurs among hadith scholars of expressing with 'tahdith' or 'ikhbar' regarding an ijazah, falsely implying hearing, while he did not receive that narrated material through hearing. These seven types are not all well-known; rather, the well-known and common are the first and second, and when unqualified, the first is intended. And this category is the one that plays a role in hadith differences, both in texts and chains, as sometimes through research after scrutiny and investigation, the fall of a man from the chain is revealed, and perhaps this fallen one is weak or has something in his memory, or did not preserve his hadith. An example of that is what Ibn Hibban narrated from the path of Ibn Jurayj, from Nafi', from Ibn Umar, who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Do not urinate while standing.' This chain has trustworthy narrators except that Ibn Jurayj is a mudallis, and he used 'an'anah here and did not explicitly state his hearing from Nafi', and he indeed heard many hadith from Nafi', so he is known for narrating from him, and his narration from him is in the six books. But the critics, with their critical insight and penetrating view, uncovered that there is an intermediary between Ibn Jurayj and Nafi' in this chain, and that Ibn Jurayj did not hear it directly from Nafi', but rather heard it from 'Abd al-Karim ibn Abi al-Mukhariq al-Da'if. And Ibn Jurayj clarified in some paths of this hadith this dropped person, so his tadlis became apparent; for 'Abd al-Razzaq narrated it, and from his path Ibn Majah, Abu 'Awanah, Ibn 'Adi, and Tammam al-Razi ...
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage defines the types of tadlis (concealment) in hadith transmission and provides an example. Tadlis is a form of hidden defect where the narrator gives a false impression of reliable transmission. Seven types are listed: (1) Tadlis al-‘Aṭf: The narrator combines two names with 'and' when he only heard from one. (2) Tadlis al-Sukūt: The narrator pauses and then names a shaykh, implying he heard from him, but he did not. (3) Tadlis al-Qaṭ‘: The narrator drops the saying formula and directly links two narrators. (4) Tadlis Ṣiyagh al-Adā’: Using words like 'hadathana' for an ijazah. The author notes that only the first two are common, and the first (tadlis al-isnad) is the most relevant for causing differences in hadith. The example involves the hadith 'Do not urinate while standing' narrated by Ibn Jurayj from Nafi‘ from Ibn ‘Umar. Although Ibn Jurayj is reliable and known to narrate from Nafi‘, he was a mudallis and used 'an'anah without explicit hearing. Critics discovered that he actually heard it through the weak narrator ‘Abd al-Karim ibn Abi al-Mukhariq, thus exposing his tadlis. This shows how tadlis can affect the authenticity of a hadith and lead to differing rulings.

Key Terms
تدليس العطف (tadlis al-'aṭf): The narrator says 'hadathana fulan wa fulan' but did not hear from the second.
تدليس السكوت (tadlis al-sukūt): The narrator pauses after saying 'hadathana' or 'sami'tu' and then names a shaykh, implying hearing without it.
تدليس القطع (tadlis al-qaṭ‘): Omitting the transmission formula and directly connecting two narrators.
تدليس صيغ الأداء (tadlis siyagh al-ada'): Using strong wording like 'hadathana' for an ijazah.
عنعنة المدلس (‘an‘anat al-mudallis): The use of 'عن' (from) by a mudallis without clarification of hearing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of tadlis involves the narrator saying 'hadathana fulan wa fulan' but only heard from one?
A) Tadlis al-sukut
B) Tadlis al-‘atf
C) Tadlis al-qat‘
D) Tadlis siyagh al-ada'

Key Takeaway
Tadlis is a hidden defect that can weaken a hadith chain if the concealed link is unreliable; recognizing its types is essential for hadith criticism in Hanafi usul.

Chain Criticism of the Hadith on Urinating Standing: Tadlis and Its Impact
Examination of a hadith chain revealing tadlis and weak link

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify tadlis in a hadith chain and apply the Hanafi rule regarding 'an'anah to evaluate the strength of a textual proof.

Core Idea
A trustworthy narrator's 'an'anah can conceal a weak link, making the hadith unreliable for fiqh rulings.

In this lesson, we examine a hadith prohibiting urinating standing. At first glance, the chain seems reliable, but hadith critics uncovered a hidden weak narrator through Ibn Juraij's tadlis. We will follow the steps of chain analysis and see how this affects the legal value of the hadith in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its apparent chain
Read the hadith 'Do not urinate standing' and note the chain: Ibn Juraij from Nafi' from Ibn Umar. Recognize that Ibn Juraij is a mudallis.
The chain seems strong at first glance.
2
Recognize the sign of tadlis
Ibn Juraij uses 'an'anah (the word 'an) instead of explicitly stating 'I heard'. In Hanafi usul, this is a red flag for possible tadlis.
The 'an'anah of a mudallis is not accepted without explicit hearing.
3
Uncover the hidden weak narrator via alternative chains
Compare with other narrations where Ibn Juraij explicitly includes 'Abd al-Karim ibn Abi al-Mukhariq, a weak narrator, between him and Nafi'. This exposes the tadlis.
The critics discovered the intermediary.
4
Apply the Hanafi usul rule for 'an'anah
According to Hanafi usul, the 'an'anah of a mudallis is not accepted unless he states that he heard directly. Since Ibn Juraij did not specify hearing, the hadith is considered weak.
Even if the mudallis is generally trustworthy, his 'an'anah is not proof.
5
Conclude the impact on the fiqh ruling
Because the hadith is weak, it cannot be used to establish a prohibition. The ruling on urinating standing remains permissible (mubah) based on other evidence.
This illustrates how chain criticism directly affects legal rulings.

الفصل التمهيدي بيان ماهية الاختلاف عن نافع عن ابن عمر قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لا تبل قائما». وهذا الإسناد رجاله ثقات إلا أن ابن جريج مدلس وقد عنعن هنا ولم يصرح بسماعه من نافع، وهو قد سمع من نافع أحاديث كثيرة، فهو معروف بالرواية عنه، وروايته عنه في الكتب الستة. ولكن النقاد ببصيرتهم الناقدة ونظرهم الثاقب كشفوا أن في هذا السند واسطة بين ابن جريج ونافع، وأن ابن جريج لم يسمعه من نافع مباشرة، بل سمعه من عبد الكريم بن أبي المخارق الضعيف، وقد صرح ابن جريج في بعض طرق الحديث بهذا الساقط، فبان تدليسه؛ فقد روى عبد الرزاق، ومن طريقه ابن ماجه، وأبو عوانة، وابن عدي، وتمام الرازي، والحاكم، والبيهقي عن ابن جريج عن عبد الكريم بن أبي المخارق عن نافع به. ومن بدائه علم الحديث أن حديث الثقة ليس كله صحيحا، كما أن حديث الضعيف ليس كله ضعيفا، ومعرفة كلا النوعين من أحاديث الفريقين ليس بالأمر اليسير إنما يطلع على ذلك الأئمة النقاد الغواصون في أعماق ما يكمن في الروايات من صحة أو خطأ، لذا فتش العلماء في حديث ابن أبي المخارق هل توبع عليه، أم أخطأ فيه؟ وخالف الثقات الأثبات أم انفرد؟ فنجدهم قد صرحوا بخطأ ابن أبي المخارق لمخالفته الثقات الأثبات في ذلك، قال البوصيري في مصباح الزجاجة – بعد أن ضعف حديث ابن أبي المخارق -: «عارضه خبر عبيد الله بن عمر العمري الثقة المأمون المجمع على ثقته، ولا يغتر بتصحيح ابن حبان هذا الخبر من طريق هشام بن يوسف عن ابن جريج عن نافع عن ابن عمر. فإنه قال بعده: أخاف أن». (ثم تتمة الفائدة في الحاشية)
Preliminary chapter: Explanation of the nature of disagreement. From Nafi', from Ibn Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Do not urinate standing.' This chain's narrators are trustworthy except that Ibn Juraij is a mudallis, and he used 'an'anah here and did not explicitly state his hearing from Nafi', although he did hear many hadiths from Nafi' and is known for narrating from him, and his narration from him is in the six books. But the critics with their critical insight and sharp sight uncovered that in this chain there is an intermediary between Ibn Juraij and Nafi', and that Ibn Juraij did not hear it from Nafi' directly, but rather heard it from 'Abd al-Karim ibn Abi al-Mukhariq, the weak one. Ibn Juraij explicitly stated this omission in some versions of the hadith, thus his tadlis became apparent. For 'Abd al-Razzaq narrated, and through him Ibn Majah, Abu 'Awanah, Ibn 'Adi, Tammam al-Razi, al-Hakim, and al-Bayhaqi, from Ibn Juraij, from 'Abd al-Karim ibn Abi al-Mukhariq, from Nafi', with it. From the basics of hadith science is that the hadith of a trustworthy narrator is not all authentic, just as the hadith of a weak narrator is not all weak. Knowing both types from the narrations of the two groups is not an easy matter; only the critical imams who dive deep into the depths of what lies in the narrations of authenticity or error come to know that. So the scholars investigated the hadith of Ibn Abi al-Mukhariq: was he followed (by others), or did he err in it? Did he contradict the reliable, trustworthy narrators or was he unique? We find that they explicitly stated the error of Ibn Abi al-Mukhariq due to his contradiction of the reliable, trustworthy narrators in that. Al-Busiri said in Misbah al-Zujajah, after weakening the hadith of Ibn Abi al-Mukhariq: 'It is contradicted by the report of 'Ubaidullah ibn 'Umar al-'Umari, the trustworthy, reliable, unanimously agreed upon for his reliability. And one should not be deceived by Ibn Hibban's authentication of this report via Hisham ibn Yusuf, from Ibn Juraij, from Nafi', from Ibn 'Umar. For he said after it: I fear that...'
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of a hadith chain, demonstrating how hadith criticism (jarh wa ta'dil) directly impacts the acceptance or rejection of a legal ruling. The author presents the hadith 'Do not urinate standing' narrated by Ibn Umar, and then scrutinizes its chain. The apparent chain includes Ibn Juraij who is a mudallis (one who conceals defects) and here he uses the term 'an (from) without specifying hearing. The critics discovered that there is an intermediary, Abd al-Karim ibn Abi al-Mukhariq, who is weak. When other narrators report the hadith with the intermediary included, it becomes clear that Ibn Juraij's 'an'anah was concealing this weak link. The passage then makes an important methodological point: not every narration from a trustworthy narrator is authentic, nor is every narration from a weak narrator weak. Only expert critics can discern the hidden defects. The scholars concluded that Ibn Abi al-Mukhariq erred and contradicted stronger narrations. Al-Busiri warns against relying on Ibn Hibban's authentication of this hadith because it goes through the same weak chain. This analysis shows how differences in evaluating chains lead to differences in juristic rulings — some scholars might consider the prohibition of urinating standing as weak and thus not binding, while others might accept it. The passage is from the preliminary chapter, setting the stage for the book's theme of how variations in chains and texts cause juristic disagreement.

Key Terms
تدليس (tadlis): Concealing a defect in the chain by using ambiguous wording like 'an (from) without specifying hearing, often to hide a weak narrator.
عنعنة ('an'anah): The practice of narrating using the word 'an (from) without stating clearly that the narrator heard directly from the source, often associated with tadlis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the scholars consider the hadith 'Do not urinate standing' weak despite being in some collections?
A) Because the narrator Nafi' was weak.
B) Because Ibn Juraij was a mudallis and the chain was found to have a weak intermediary.
C) Because the hadith contradicts the Qur'an.
D) Because the hadith is mursal.

Key Takeaway
A hadith's chain must be critically examined for tadlis; even a trustworthy narrator's 'an'anah is not sufficient proof in Hanafi usul if it conceals a weak link.

Tadlis as a Cause of Disagreement: The Hadith of Urinating Standing
Analyzing a hadith chain to show tadlis causing juristic disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify tadlis in a hadith chain, evaluate its impact on authenticity, and explain how it causes juristic disagreement between madhhabs.

Core Idea
Tadlis in a chain can create a false marfu' hadith, leading scholars to differ on the ruling derived from it.

This lesson unpacks a classic example of tadlis: the hadith prohibiting urination while standing. By examining the chain of Abd al-Karim ibn Abi al-Mukhariq, you will see how scholars detected a defect and preferred a stronger mawquf report. This concrete case reveals how chain criticism directly shapes fiqh rulings and madhhab differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested hadith and its chain
Locate the marfu' hadith (raised to the Prophet) that is under scrutiny. Note the narrator who caused the problem: Abd al-Karim ibn Abi al-Mukhariq, from Nafi', from Ibn Umar.
The chain is: Ibn Jurayj ← Abd al-Karim ← Nafi' ← Ibn Umar.
2
Recognize the criticism of the narrator
Understand why Abd al-Karim is weak: he contradicted reliable narrators (Ubayd Allah ibn Umar) and was weakened by Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani. Check if his report is supported by follow-ups (mutaba'at).
Al-Tirmidhi and al-Busiri stated his error.
3
Compare with the stronger mawquf report
Examine the mawquf (stopped at Companion) report from Umar: 'I have not urinated standing since I embraced Islam.' This is transmitted by Ubayd Allah, a trusted narrator, and is considered more authentic.
The mawquf does not prohibit; it merely reports Umar's practice.
4
Conclude the effect of tadlis
Realize that the weak marfu' hadith likely originated from tadlis: Ibn Jurayj may have heard it from the weak Ibn Abi al-Mukhariq, dropping his name or not confirming hearing. This creates a false impression of a Prophetic prohibition.
Tadlis omits a weak link, making the chain appear stronger than it is.
5
Connect to juristic disagreement
Understand that Hanafis, relying on the mawquf and general permissibility, do not consider urinating standing as prohibited, while other schools may deem it disliked based on the marfu' hadith. The tadlis caused this difference.
The practical effect (thamarah) is a difference in the ruling of a daily act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحاكم)، والبيهقي ()، عَنْ ابن جريج، عَنْ عَبْد الكريم بن أبي المخارق، عَنْ نافع، بِهِ. ومن بدائه علم الْحَدِيث أن حَدِيث الثقة ليس كله صحيحاً، كَمَا أَنْ حَدِيث الضعيف ليس كله ضعيفاً، ومعرفة كلا النوعين من أحاديث الفريقين ليس بالأمر اليسير إنما يطلع عَلَى ذَلِكَ الأئمة النقاد الغواصون في أعماق ما يكمن في الروايات من صحة أو خطأ، لذا فتّش العلماء في حَدِيث ابن أبي المخارق هل توبع عَلَيْهِ، أم أخطأ فِيهِ؟ وخالف الثقات الأثبات أم انفرد؟ فنجدهُمْ قَد صرحوا بخطأ ابن أبي المخارق لمخالفته الثقات الأثبات في ذَلِكَ، قَالَ البوصيري) في مصباح الزجاجة – بَعْدَ أن ضعف حَدِيث ابن أبي المخارق -: «عارضه خبر عبيد -: عارضه خبر عبيد الله بن عمر العمري ) الثقة المأمون المجمع عَلَى ثقته، ولا يُغتر بتصحيح ابن حبان هَذا الخبر من طريق هشام بن يوسف ، عَنْ ابن جريج عن نافع، عَنْ ابن عمر. فإنه قَالَ بعده أخاف أن يَكُون ابن جريج لَمْ يسمعه من نافع، وَقَدْ صح ظنُّه، فإنّ ابن جريج إما سمعه من ابن أبي المخارق كَمَا ثبت في رِوَايَة ابن ماجه هَذِهِ والحاكم في المستدرك واعتذر عَنْ تخريجه أنه إنّما أخرجه في المتابعات). وَقَالَ الترمذي: «إنما رفع هَذَا الْحَدِيث عَبْد الكريم بن أبي المخارق، وَهُوَ ضعيف عِنْدَ أهل الْحَدِيث ضعفه أيوب السختياني وتكلم فيه. وروى عبيد الله، عَنْ نافع عن ابن عمر قَالَ: قَالَ عمر ه ما بلتُ قائِماً منذ أسلَمْتُ. وهذا أصح من حَدِيث عبد الكريم). أقول: رِوَايَة عبيد الله الموقوفة أخرجها ابن أبي شيبة، والبزار في مسنده من طريق عبيد الله بن عمر عَنْ نافع، عَنْ ابن عمر، عَنْ عمر موقوفاً، وَهُوَ الصواب. ومما يدل على عدم صحة حَدِيث ابن أبي المخارق أن الحافظ ابن حجر وَلَمْ يثبت عَنْ النَّبِي الله في النهي عنه شيء ). بَعْدَ هَذَا العرض السريع بان لنا واتضح أن التدليس سبب من أسباب الاختلاف لدى الْمُحَدِّثِينَ؛ إِذْ إِنه قَدْ يسفر عن سقوط رجل من الإسناد فيخالف الرَّاوِي غيره من الرُّوَاة.
And al-Hakim and al-Bayhaqi from Ibn Jurayj from Abd al-Karim ibn Abi al-Mukhariq from Nafi' with it. Among the givens of hadith science is that the hadith of a trustworthy narrator is not all sound, just as the hadith of a weak narrator is not all weak, and knowing both types from the narrations of the two groups is not an easy matter; only the imams who are critics and divers into the depths of what lies hidden in narrations of soundness or error are aware of that. Therefore, the scholars investigated the hadith of Ibn Abi al-Mukhariq: was he followed up on it, or did he err in it? Did he contradict the reliable trustworthy narrators, or was he alone? We find that they explicitly stated the error of Ibn Abi al-Mukhariq due to his contradicting the reliable trustworthy narrators in that. Al-Busiri said in Misbah al-Zujaja after weakening the hadith of Ibn Abi al-Mukhariq: 'It is contradicted by the report of Ubayd Allah ibn Umar al-Amri, the trustworthy reliable one upon whose reliability there is consensus. And do not be deceived by Ibn Hibban's authentication of this report via Hisham ibn Yusuf from Ibn Jurayj from Nafi' from Ibn Umar, for he said after it: I fear that Ibn Jurayj did not hear it from Nafi'. And his conjecture proved correct, for Ibn Jurayj either heard it from Ibn Abi al-Mukhariq as established in this narration of Ibn Majah and al-Hakim in al-Mustadrak, and he apologized for producing it that he only produced it among follow-ups.' And al-Tirmidhi said: 'Only Abd al-Karim ibn Abi al-Mukhariq raised this hadith, and he is weak according to the hadith scholars; Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani weakened him and spoke against him. And Ubayd Allah narrated from Nafi' from Ibn Umar: Umar said: I have not urinated standing since I embraced Islam. And this is more correct than the hadith of Abd al-Karim.' I say: The mawquf narration of Ubayd Allah was produced by Ibn Abi Shayba and al-Bazzar in his Musnad via the chain of Ubayd Allah ibn Umar from Nafi' from Ibn Umar from Umar as mawquf, and that is correct. Among the evidence for the unsoundness of the hadith of Ibn Abi al-Mukhariq is that al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar did not prove anything from the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbidding it. After this brief presentation, it is clear to us that tadlis (deception in hadith) is a cause of disagreement among hadith scholars; for it may result in the omission of a narrator from the chain, causing the narrator to contradict other narrators.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of a specific hadith chain to demonstrate how tadlis (deception in hadith) becomes a cause of juristic disagreement. The author presents the case of the hadith prohibiting urination while standing, narrated by Abd al-Karim ibn Abi al-Mukhariq from Nafi' from Ibn Umar. The scholars critically examine this chain: Ibn Abi al-Mukhariq is weak, and his narration contradicts the more reliable mawquf statement of Umar that he never urinated standing after Islam. The author cites al-Busiri and al-Tirmidhi to show that the correct position is the mawquf version, meaning the hadith is not sound as a marfu' (raised to the Prophet). The conclusion is that tadlis—where a narrator may drop a weak link—leads to differing assessments of hadith authenticity, which in turn causes jurists to differ in rulings derived from such texts. This example is from the chapter on tahara (purification) concerning the ruling on urinating standing. The Hanafi position, based on the mawquf report and general permissibility, differs from those who hold it as disliked based on the weak marfu' hadith.

Key Terms
تدليس (tadlis): A defect in hadith where the narrator conceals a weakness in his chain, often by omitting a weak link or using ambiguous wording.
مرفوع (marfu'): A hadith attributed to the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) with a chain going back to him.
موقوف (mawquf): A narration attributed to a Companion, not directly to the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because it was narrated by a known liar
C) Because it was not found in any hadith collection
D) Because it was abrogated

Key Takeaway
Tadlis in a hadith chain can cause jurists to differ in rulings; rigorous chain criticism using the criteria of the hadith critics is essential to reach the correct fiqh position.
