Ruling on Tadlis and Acceptance of Mudallis Narrations
Discussion of tadlis ruling and acceptance of mudallis reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul accepts a mudallis's narration absolutely, and evaluate the competing schools' proofs.

Core Idea
Tadlis is not a lie; acceptance of a mudallis's report depends on whether we treat his silence as implicit approval of the intermediary.

This passage examines the nature of tadlis (concealment in hadith transmission) and its effect on the weight of evidence. While some scholars equate tadlis with lying, the majority — including the Hanafi school — view it as a mere ambiguity. The practical consequence appears in three competing schools of acceptance, with Hanafis adopting a position analogous to their acceptance of mursal hadith.

Guided Path
1
Define tadlis and distinguish it from lying
Understand that tadlis linguistically means hiding a flaw, and it does not constitute a lie. The majority view, cited from al-Shafi'i, holds that tadlis is a form of ambiguity, not a discrediting lie.
Shu'bah's strict statement is interpreted as a deterrent, not a literal equivalence.
2
Identify the ruling on tadlis and the Hanafi adoption of the moderate view
The passage shows that tadlis itself is not considered a lie that destroys reliability. Al-Shafi'i's statement is quoted to support that a known mudallis's weakness is revealed but his narrations are not automatically rejected.
The Hanafi position aligns with this moderate view.
3
Analyze the three schools on mudallis narrations
List the three schools: (1) absolute rejection, (2) absolute acceptance (attributed to some Hanafis), and (3) conditional acceptance based on dominant practice. Note the reasoning behind each.
The fourth school is mentioned but not detailed.
4
Examine the Hanafi proof: analogy to mursal acceptance
The Hanafi school bases its absolute acceptance on the principle that a trustworthy narrator's omission of an intermediary is an implicit approval: if the intermediary were unreliable, the narrator would have named him explicitly.
This is the same reasoning used for accepting mursal hadith.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf: when does this difference matter in practice?
Consider a scenario where a mudallis narrates a hadith without explicit hearing. Under the first school, it is rejected; under the Hanafi view, it may be accepted if the mudallis is overall trustworthy. This directly affects the evidentiary strength of such narrations in fiqh rulings.
The difference is not trivial; it can determine whether a proof is considered valid.

إذا تمهد هَذَا فإني سأتحدّث عن الاختلافات الواردة في الإسناد في مبحثين، وعلى النحو الآتي:
المبحث الأول: أثر التدليس في اختلاف الحديث
مَرَّ بنا في الفصل التمهيدي تعريف التدليس لغة وأرجأنا القول في تعريفه اصطلاحاً وسأفصل ذَلِكَ عَلَى النحو الآتي:
أولاً: أقسام التدليس.
ثانياً: حكم التدليس، وحكم من عرف به. ثالثاً: حكم الْحَدِيث المدلس.
رابعاً: أثر التدليس في اختلاف الرُّوَاة، وأثره في اختلاف الفقهاء.
أولاً. أقسام التدليس
فصلنا القول فِيهَا في الفصل التمهيدي في مبحث أسباب نشوء الاختلافات.
ثانياً. حكم التدليس، وحكم من عرف به:
مضى بنا في الفصل التمهيدي في تعريف التدليس لغة أن مجموع معانيه تؤول إلى إخفاء العيب، وليس من معانيه الكذب، ومع ذَلِكَ فَقَدْ اختلف العلماء في حكمه وحكم أهله. فَقَدْ ورد عن بعضهم ومنهم - شعبة - التشديد فيه فروي عَنْهُ أَنه قَالَ: «التدليس أخو الكذب»، وَقَالَ أَيْضاً: «لإنْ أزني أحب إلي من أن أدلس». ومنهم من سهل أمره وتسامح فِيْهِ كثيراً، قَالَ أبو بكر البزار: «التدليس ليس بكذب، وإنما هُوَ تحسين الظاهر الإسناد». وَالصَّحِيح الَّذِي عليه الجمهور أنه ليس بكذب يصح به القدح في عدالة الرَّاوِي حَتَّى نرد جميع حديثه، وإنما هُوَ ضَرْبٌ من الإيهام، وعلى هَذَا نص الشَّافِعِي -رحمه الله - فَقَالَ: ومن عرفناه دلس مرة فَقَدْ أبان لنا عورته في روايته، وليست تلك العورة بالكذب فنرد بها حديثه، ولا النصيحة في الصدق، فنقبل مِنْهُ ما قبلنا من أهل النصيحة في الصدق. ويمكن حمل التشدد الوارد عن شعبة عَلَى المبالغة في الزجر عنه والتنفير. وإذا تقرر هَذَا، فما حكم حَدِيث من عرف بِهِ؟ للعلماء فيه أربعة مذاهب: الأول: لا تقبل رِوَايَة المدلس، سواء صرح بالسماع أم لا، حكاه ابن الصَّلاحِ عن فريق من أهل الْحَدِيث والفقه، وهذا مبني عَلَى القَوْل بأن التدليس نفسه جرح من عُرِف بِهِ. وهذا الذي استظهره عَلَى أصول مذهب الإمام مالك القاضي عبد الوهاب في الملخص. الثاني: قبول رِوَايَة المدلس مطلقاً، وَهُوَ فرع لمذهب من قبل المرسل ونقله الْخَطِيب البغدادي عن جمهور من قبل المراسيل، وحكاه الزركشي عن بعض شارحي أصول البزدوي من الحنفية. وبنوا هَذَا عَلَى ما بنوا عَلَيْهِ قبول المرسل؛ من أنّ إضراب الثقة عن ذكر الرَّاوِي تعديل لَهُ، فإن من مقتضيات ثقته التصريح باسم من روى عَنْهُ إذا كَانَ غَيْر ثقة. الثالث: إذا كَانَ الغالب عَلَى تدليسه أن يَكُون عن الثقات فهو مقبول كيفما كانت صيغة التحديث، وإن كَانَ عن غَيْر الثقة هُوَ الغالب رد حديثه حَتَّى يصرح بالسماع حكاه الْخَطِيب عن بعض أهل العلم، ونقله الزركشي عن أبي الفتح الأزدي.
If this is established, then I will discuss the differences occurring in the chain in two sections, as follows: The first section: The effect of tadlis (concealment) on hadith disagreement. We have already passed in the introductory chapter the definition of tadlis linguistically, and we postponed its technical definition, and I will detail that as follows: First: Divisions of tadlis. Second: The ruling of tadlis, and the ruling of the one known for it. Third: The ruling of the mudallas (concealed) hadith. Fourth: The effect of tadlis on the differences among narrators, and its effect on the differences among jurists. First: Divisions of tadlis: We have already discussed this in the introductory chapter in the section on causes of disagreements. Second: The ruling of tadlis, and the ruling of the one known for it: It has passed with us in the introductory chapter on the linguistic definition of tadlis that the sum of its meanings amounts to hiding a flaw, and it does not include lying. Nevertheless, scholars have differed regarding its ruling and the ruling of its practitioners. For it has been reported from some of them - including Shu'bah - a strictness regarding it; it is narrated from him that he said: 'Tadlis is the brother of lying.' He also said: 'That I should commit fornication is more beloved to me than that I should commit tadlis.' And among them are those who made it easy and were lenient about it greatly. Abu Bakr al-Bazzar said: 'Tadlis is not a lie; rather it is an improvement of the outward appearance of the chain.' The correct view, which the majority hold, is that it is not a lie that would permit disparagement of the narrator's reliability so that we reject all his hadith; rather it is a kind of ambiguity. Based on this, al-Shafi'i - may God have mercy on him - said: 'He whom we know to have committed tadlis once has indeed revealed to us his weakness in his narration, nor is that weakness a lie so we reject his hadith on account of it, nor does it belong to sincerity in truthfulness, so we accept from him what we accept from people of sincerity in truthfulness.' And the strictness reported from Shu'bah may be interpreted as exaggeration in deterrence and warning against it. If this is settled, what is the ruling on the hadith of one known for it? Scholars have four schools regarding it: First: The narration of a mudallis is not accepted, whether he explicitly states hearing or not. This was narrated by Ibn al-Salah from a group of hadith specialists and jurists. This is based on the view that tadlis itself is a discrediting flaw for one known for it. This is what al-Qadi 'Abd al-Wahhab asserted according to the principles of Imam Malik in al-Mulakhkhas. Second: The absolute acceptance of the narration of a mudallis. This is a branch of the school that accepts the mursal hadith. Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi narrated it from the majority of those who accept mursal narrations, and al-Zarkashi narrated it from some commentators of Usul al-Bazdawi among the Hanafis. They based this on what they based their acceptance of mursal: that the trustworthy narrator's omission of mentioning the narrator is an approval of him, for it is a requirement of his trustworthiness to explicitly name the one from whom he narrates if he is unreliable. Third: If his tadlis is predominantly from reliable narrators, then his narration is accepted regardless of the wording of transmission; but if he predominantly reports from unreliable narrators, his hadith is rejected until he explicitly states hearing. This was narrated by al-Khatib from some scholars, and al-Zarkashi narrated it from Abu al-Fath al-Azdi.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is an extended ruling on tadlis (deliberate concealment in hadith transmission) and its effect on the acceptance of a narrator's reports. The author begins by outlining the planned discussion, then focuses on the second point: the legal ruling on tadlis and its practitioners. He notes that linguistically tadlis means hiding a flaw, not lying. Nevertheless, narrators like Shu'ba took a very strict view, equating it with lying or even worse. Others like Abu Bakr al-Bazzar were lenient, considering it merely an improvement of the chain. The majority view—and the one the author seems to adopt—is that tadlis is not a lie that destroys a narrator's reliability entirely, but a form of ambiguity that does require caution. Al-Shafi'i's statement is quoted to support this: a known mudallis's weakness is revealed, but his narrations are not automatically rejected. The strictness of Shu'ba is explained as a deterrent exaggeration. Then the author moves to the core issue: what is the ruling on hadith narrated by a mudallis? He presents four madhahib (schools), but only three are detailed in this passage. The first school (of some hadith scholars and jurists, and attributed to Maliki principles by al-Qadi 'Abd al-Wahhab) completely rejects a mudallis's narrations, whether he states hearing or not, because tadlis itself is a discrediting flaw. The second school (attributed to some Hanafis and those who accept mursal) accepts mudallis narrations absolutely, arguing that a trustworthy narrator's silence about an intermediary is an implicit endorsement: if the unnamed person were unreliable, the trustworthy narrator would have mentioned it. The third school (attributed to some scholars) differentiates: if the mudallis predominantly narrates from trustworthy sources, his narrations are accepted; if predominantly from unreliable, they are rejected unless he explicitly states hearing. The fourth school is mentioned but not elaborated here. This discussion is crucial for understanding how hadith critics and jurists handle narrations from mudallis, and it directly affects the strength of evidence in fiqh rulings when such narrations are used.

Key Terms
التدليس (al-tadlis): Hiding a flaw in the chain of narration, such as narrating from someone not directly met, without it being a lie.
المدلس (al-mudallis): A narrator known to practice tadlis, i.e., concealing flaws in his chain.
المرسل (al-mursal): A hadith where a successor (tabi'i) narrates directly from the Prophet without mentioning the companion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because tadlis is not a flaw at all.
B) Because the mudallis's silence about an intermediary implies the intermediary is trustworthy, based on the principle of accepting mursal.
C) Because the mudallis is always considered a thiqa regardless of his practice.
D) Because the majority of scholars agree on acceptance.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi acceptance of mudallis narrations is rooted in the principle that a trustworthy narrator's silence is an implicit endorsement of the omitted intermediary.

Tadlis: Definition, Positions, and Impact on Fiqh Differences
Definition of tadlis and four positions on accepting a mudallis's hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four scholarly positions on tadlis, explain the Hanafi analogy to mursal, and evaluate how tadlis leads to ikhtilaf in fiqh rulings.

Core Idea
Tadlis is not lying but ambiguity; its acceptance depends on the narrator's formula and the school's approach to mursal.

Tadlis is a critical concept in hadith criticism that directly affects how narrations are evaluated. The Hanafi school's acceptance of mursal hadith provides a basis for a permissive view on tadlis, while the majority of hadith scholars insist on explicit samā'. This lesson unpacks the definition, four positions, and a concrete fiqh example.

Guided Path
1
Define tadlis and distinguish it from lying
Read the opening: tadlis is ambiguity (iham), not kadhb (lying). Understand why it does not necessarily destroy a narrator's integrity.
Shu'bah's severity is seen as deterrent, not literal ruling.
2
Identify the four scholarly positions
List the four views: (1) absolute rejection, (2) absolute acceptance, (3) conditional on predominant source, (4) acceptance only with explicit samā'.
Know which groups hold each view, especially the Hanafi connection to mursal.
3
Analyze the Hanafi qiyas to mursal
The second position (absolute acceptance) analogizes to mursal: a trustworthy narrator's omission of an intermediate is a tacit endorsement.
This qiyas is the Hanafi justification; understand the illa.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the applied example: the hadith of Baqiyah on 'catching a rak'ah'. How does the position on tadlis affect whether that hadith is used as evidence?
The ikhtilaf leads to different fiqh rulings on Friday prayer completeness.
5
Identify the mufta bihi among the positions
The text indicates the fourth position (explicit samā') is the majority view, endorsed by al-Khatib and Ibn al-Salah. Recognize the tarjih.
This is the operative standard in most madhabs, though Hanafis may still accept under their mursal analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول الاختلاف في السند
وَالصَّحِيح الَّذِي عليه الجمهور أنه ليس بكذب يصح به القدح في عدالة الرَّاوِي حَتَّى نرد جميع حديثه، وإنما هُوَ ضَرْبٌ من الإيهام، وعلى هَذَا نص الشَّافِعِي -رحمه الله - فَقَالَ: ومن عرفناه دلس مرة فَقَدْ أبان لنا عورته في روايته، وليست تلك العورة بالكذب فنرد بها حديثه، ولا النصيحة في الصدق، فنقبل مِنْهُ ما قبلنا من أهل النصيحة في الصدق». ويمكن حمل التشدد الوارد عن شعبة عَلَى «المبالغة في الزجر عنه والتنفير». وإذا تقرر هَذَا، فما حكم حَدِيث من عرف بِهِ؟ للعلماء فيه أربعة مذاهب: الأول: لا تقبل رِوَايَة المدلس، سواء صرح بالسماع أم لا، حكاه ابن الصَّلاحِ عن فريق من أهل الْحَدِيث والفقه، وهذا مبني عَلَى القَوْل بأن التدليس نفسه جرح من عُرِف بِهِ. وهذا الذي استظهره عَلَى أصول مذهب الإمام مالك القاضي عبد الوهاب في الملخص. الثاني: قبول رِوَايَة المدلس مطلقاً، وَهُوَ فرع لمذهب من قبل المرسل ونقله الْخَطِيب البغدادي عن جمهور من قبل المراسيل، وحكاه الزركشي عن بعض شارحي أصول البزدوي من الحنفية. وبنوا هَذَا عَلَى ما بنوا عَلَيْهِ قبول المرسل؛ من أنّ إضراب الثقة عن ذكر الرَّاوِي تعديل لَهُ، فإن من مقتضيات ثقته التصريح باسم من روى عَنْهُ إذا كَانَ غَيْر ثقة. الثالث: إذا كَانَ الغالب عَلَى تدليسه أن يَكُون عن الثقات فهو مقبول كيفما كانت صيغة التحديث، وإن كَانَ عن غَيْر الثقة هُوَ الغالب رد حديثه حَتَّى يصرح بالسماع حكاه الْخَطِيب عن بعض أهل العلم، ونقله الزركشي عن أبي الفتح الأزدي. الرابع: التفصيل بَيْنَ أن يروي بصيغة مبينة للسماع، فيقبل حديثه، وبين أن يروي بصيغة محتملة للسماع وغيره فلا يقبل. وهذا الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ جمهور أَهْل الْحَدِيث وغيرهم وصححه جمع مِنْهُمْ : الخَطيب البغدادي وابن الصَّلاحِ وغيرهما.
ثالثاً. حكم الحديث المدلس:
لما كَانَ في حَدِيث المدلس شبهة وجود انقطاع بَيْنَ المدلس ومن عنعن عَنْهُ، بحيث قَدْ يَكُون الساقط شخصاً أو أكثر، وَقَدْ يَكُون ثقة أو ضعيفاً. فلما توافرت هَذِهِ الشبهة اقتضى ذلك الحكم بضعفه.
رابعاً. أثر التدليس في اختلاف الحديث وأثره في اختلاف الفقهاء:
كَانَ التدليس أحد الأسباب التي دفعت بالرواة إلى الاختلاف في أسانيد بعض الأحاديث، وترتب عَلَى ذَلِكَ تباين في آراء الفقهاء الَّذِيْنَ استدلوا بتلك الأحاديث، وفيما يأتي بعض المسائل التطبيقية:
النموذج الأول:
حَدِيث بقية بن الوليد، عن يونس بن يزيد الأيلي، عن الزهري عن سالم ابن عمر مرفوعاً: «من أدرك ركعة من صلاة الجمعة أو غيرها، فقد أدرك».
Chapter One: Disagreement in the Chain of Transmission. The correct view held by the majority is that it (tadlis) is not lying that could impugn the narrator's integrity such that we reject all his hadith. Rather, it is a type of ambiguity. And al-Shafi'i — may Allah have mercy on him — stated this, saying: 'Whoever we know to have concealed once has revealed his weakness in his narration. That weakness is not lying that we would reject his hadith because of it, nor is it the sincerity in truthfulness that we would accept from him what we accept from people of sincerity in truthfulness.' And the strictness reported from Shu'bah can be interpreted as 'exaggeration in deterring from it and repelling.' Having established this, what is the ruling on the hadith of one known for tadlis? Scholars have four schools on it: First: The narration of a mudallis is not accepted, whether he explicitly states hearing or not — reported by Ibn al-Salah from a group of hadith scholars and jurists. This is based on the view that tadlis itself is a defect in one known for it. This is what al-Qadi 'Abd al-Wahhab favored according to the principles of the school of Imam Malik in al-Mulakhkhas. Second: Accepting the narration of a mudallis absolutely. This is a branch of the view that accepts mursal, and al-Khatib al-Baghdadi transmitted it from the majority of those who accept mursal. al-Zarkashi reported it from some commentators of Usul al-Bazdawi among the Hanafis. They built this on what they built for accepting mursal: that the trustworthy person's omission of mentioning the narrator is a modification of him, for among the implications of his trustworthiness is that he would explicitly name the one he narrates from if he were not trustworthy. Third: If the predominant pattern of his tadlis is from trustworthy narrators, his narration is accepted regardless of the formula of transmission. If it is from untrustworthy narrators that is predominant, his hadith is rejected until he explicitly states hearing — reported by al-Khatib from some scholars, and al-Zarkashi transmitted it from Abu al-Fath al-Azdi. Fourth: Differentiation between narrating with a formula indicating hearing (in which case his hadith is accepted) and narrating with a formula that could indicate hearing or otherwise (in which case it is not accepted). This is the view of the majority of hadith scholars and others, and it was deemed correct by a group including al-Khatib al-Baghdadi and Ibn al-Salah and others. Third: The Ruling on the Mudallas Hadith. Since in the hadith of a mudallis there is the suspicion of an interruption between the mudallis and the one he reports from by 'an'anah, such that the missing person could be one or more, and could be trustworthy or weak, given this suspicion, it necessitates its being deemed weak. Fourth: The Effect of Tadlis on Hadith Differences and Its Effect on the Differences of Jurists. Tadlis was one of the causes that drove narrators to differ in the chains of some hadith, and this resulted in divergence in the opinions of jurists who used those hadith as evidence. The following are some applied examples: First Model: The hadith of Baqiyah ibn al-Walid from Yunus ibn Yazid al-Ayli from al-Zuhri from Salim ibn 'Umar marfu'an: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Friday prayer or other prayers has caught it.'
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a thorough discussion of tadlis (concealment) in hadith transmission. It begins by defining tadlis: the majority of scholars hold that it is not outright lying that would destroy a narrator's credibility, but rather a form of ambiguity (iham). Imam al-Shafi'i's statement clarifies that a mudallis is considered to have revealed a 'weakness' in his narration, but not a lie. Shu'bah's severe condemnation is understood as a deterrent, not a literal ruling. The passage then presents four scholarly positions on accepting the hadith of a mudallis: (1) Absolute rejection (attributed to a group, and favored by the Maliki school), (2) Absolute acceptance (from some Hanafis who analogize to mursal, arguing that omitting a name is a tacit endorsement), (3) Conditional acceptance based on whether the mudallis predominantly narrates from trustworthy sources, and (4) Acceptance only if he uses a clear formula of hearing (the position of the majority of hadith scholars, including al-Khatib and Ibn al-Salah). Under 'third' and 'fourth' headings, the passage explains the rationale for weakness: the suspicion of interruption (inqita') between the mudallis and his source. Finally, it introduces the practical impact of tadlis on fiqh differences, giving an example of a hadith narrated by Baqiyah ibn al-Walid (a known mudallis) about catching a rak'ah in Friday prayer. Because of differing assessments of Baqiyah's tadlis, jurists may disagree on the ruling derived from this hadith. The passage thus illustrates how chain-related defects lead to substantive legal disagreement.

Key Terms
التدليس (al-tadlis): Concealment of a defect in the chain of transmission, usually by using an ambiguous expression like 'an ('from') without clarifying whether the transmission was direct.
المدلس (al-mudallis): A narrator known to have engaged in tadlis, i.e., concealing the identity or weakness of an intermediate source.
المرسل (al-mursal): A hadith in which a Successor (tabi'i) narrates directly from the Prophet without mentioning the Companion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the four positions on tadlis is attributed to some Hanafis according to al-Zarkashi?
A) Absolute rejection of the mudallis's hadith
B) Absolute acceptance of the mudallis's hadith
C) Conditional acceptance based on the mudallis's predominant sources
D) Acceptance only if the mudallis explicitly states hearing

Key Takeaway
Tadlis is ambiguity, not lying, and its impact on hadith acceptance varies by school; the Hanafi qiyas to mursal leads to absolute acceptance, while the majority requires explicit samā'.

Fourth Position on Tadlis: Explicit vs Ambiguous Formulas
Stating the ruling on accepting mudallis hadith if hearing is explicit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between explicit and ambiguous transmission formulas and apply the Hanafi usul rule for accepting mudallis hadith.

Core Idea
A mudallis hadith is accepted if the narrator explicitly states hearing; ambiguity leads to rejection.

This lesson unpacks the fourth position on tadlis, which draws a clear line based on wording. Understanding this distinction is essential for evaluating hadith narrations in Hanafi usul, where the form of transmission determines acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two formula types
The passage distinguishes between a formula that clarifies hearing (e.g., sami'tu, haddathani) and one that is ambiguous (e.g., 'an, qala). Recognize each type.
2
Understand the ruling for each
If the mudallis uses an explicit formula, his hadith is accepted. If he uses an ambiguous formula, it is not accepted because the possibility of tadlis remains.
3
Note the authority
This position is held by the majority of hadith scholars and verified by al-Khatib al-Baghdadi and Ibn al-Salah.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a mudallis narrator, examine his wording. Apply the rule to decide acceptance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع: التفصيل بَيْنَ أن يروي بصيغة مبينة للسماع، فيقبل حديثه، وبين أن يروي بصيغة محتملة للسماع وغيره فلا يقبل. وهذا الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ جمهور أَهْل الْحَدِيث وغيرهم ) وصححه جمع مِنْهُمْ : الخَطيب البغدادي وابن الصَّلاحِ وغيرهما.
The fourth: the distinction between narrating with a formula that clarifies hearing, so his hadith is accepted, and between narrating with a formula that is possible for hearing and other, so it is not accepted. And this is what the majority of hadith scholars and others are upon, and it was considered correct by a group of them: al-Khatib al-Baghdadi and Ibn al-Salah and others.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage states the fourth position regarding tadlis. The rule: if the mudallis uses a clear phrase like 'I heard' (sami'tu) or 'he narrated to me' (haddathani), his hadith is accepted because it removes the doubt of discontinuity. But if he uses ambiguous terms like 'an or 'qala' that could be from listening or other, then the hadith is not accepted because the possibility of tadlis remains. This is the position of the majority of hadith scholars, confirmed by al-Khatib al-Baghdadi and Ibn al-Salah.

Key Terms
بصيغة مبينة للسماع (biṣīghatin mubayyinatin lil-samā‘): A clear phrase that explicitly indicates that the narrator heard the hadith directly, such as 'sami'tu' or 'haddathani'.
بصيغة محتملة للسماع وغيره (biṣīghatin muḥtamilatin lil-samā‘i wa ghayrih): An ambiguous formula that could indicate hearing or other means of transmission, such as 'an or 'qala'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is the hadith of a mudallis accepted?
A) When he uses any form of narration
B) When he uses a clear formula like 'sami'tu' or 'haddathani'
C) When he is a well-known mudallis
D) When he narrates from a trustworthy person

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of a mudallis hadith hinges on explicit wording indicating direct hearing; ambiguity leads to rejection.

The Ruling on Mudallis Hadith: Weak Due to Discontinuity Doubt
Stating the general ruling that mudallis hadith is weak

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mudallis hadith and identify the reason (suspicion of a missing link) that makes it weak.

Core Idea
Tadlis creates a suspicion of a missing link; that doubt makes the hadith weak.

In this lesson, we examine the default ruling on a hadith narrated by a mudallis. The Hanafi position is that such a hadith is weak due to the inherent uncertainty about the chain. Understanding this ruling helps you evaluate hadith evidence in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage states that the mudallis hadith is weak (da'if). This is the default ruling when the mudallis uses ambiguous wording like 'an.
2
Recognize the cause (sabab) of weakness
The weakness is due to 'shubhat inqiṭā‘' – a suspicion that one or more narrators might be missing between the mudallis and the one he claims to narrate from.
The missing narrator can be trustworthy or weak; the doubt itself is enough to weaken the hadith.
3
Note the condition (shart) for this ruling
The ruling applies when the mudallis does not explicitly state hearing (e.g., 'sami'tu' or 'haddathani'). If he clarifies, the weakness is removed.
This is implicit: the passage says the weakness comes from the ambiguous wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثاً. حكم الحديث المدلس: لما كَانَ في حَدِيث المدلس شبهة وجود انقطاع بَيْنَ المدلس ومن عنعن عَنْهُ، بحيث قَدْ يَكُون الساقط شخصاً أو أكثر، وَقَدْ يَكُون ثقة أو ضعيفاً. فلما توافرت هَذِهِ الشبهة اقتضى ذلك الحكم بضعفه.
Third: The ruling on the mudallis hadith: Because in the hadith of a mudallis there is a suspicion of the existence of a discontinuity between the mudallis and the one he narrates from with 'an, to the extent that the missing person may be one or more, and he may be trustworthy or weak. So when this suspicion is established, it necessitates the ruling of its weakness.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling (hukm) for hadith narrated with tadlis. The reasoning: the mudallis often omits an intermediary, creating a potential break in the chain. That missing person could be reliable or unreliable. Because of this uncertainty, the hadith is considered weak. This is the default ruling for any hadith where tadlis is suspected. However, as noted in the previous lesson, if the mudallis clarifies hearing, the doubt is removed and the hadith can be accepted.

Key Terms
شبهة انقطاع (shubhat inqiṭā‘): The suspicion that there is a missing link in the chain of narrators due to tadlis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the hadith of a mudallis ruled weak according to the passage?
A) Because the mudallis is always a liar
B) Because there is a suspicion of a missing link in the chain
C) Because the mudallis is not a scholar
D) Because the hadith contradicts the Quran

Key Takeaway
The mudallis hadith is weak due to the inherent suspicion of a missing link; only explicit hearing removes this weakness.

Baqiyyah's Tadlis and the Hadith of Catching One Rak'ah
Analyzing a concrete example of tadlis causing chain error and fiqh implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how tadlis al-taswiyah affects a hadith chain and apply the Hanafi principle of preferring a corroborated chain over a solitary mudallis narration.

Core Idea
A mudallis's solitary chain is rejected if the majority narrate it from a different chain.

This lesson examines a concrete example where a narrator's tadlis created a discrepancy in the chain of a hadith used to derive a fiqh ruling. By analyzing Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid's error, you will learn how careful hadith criticism is essential for correct fiqh derivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its two chains
Read the passage and note the two different chains: one via Salim ibn Umar (narrated by Baqiyyah) and one via Abu Salamah (narrated by the majority of al-Zuhri's students).
The hadith text is 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Friday prayer or other prayers, has caught the prayer.'
2
Recognize Baqiyyah's tadlis al-taswiyah
Understand that Baqiyyah is known for tadlis al-taswiyah, where he drops weak narrators to make the chain appear strong. This practice casts doubt on his narration.
Tadlis al-taswiyah is a serious form of tadlis in Hanafi hadith criticism.
3
Compare the solitary chain vs. the majority chain
The passage states that only Baqiyyah narrated this hadith from Yunus from al-Zuhri via Salim. The majority of al-Zuhri's students (Malik, etc.) narrated it via Abu Salamah from Abu Hurairah. This makes the majority chain more reliable.
The Hanafi principle: acceptance of a hadith requires that it be from a reliable narrator and not contradict a stronger chain.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the chain via Salim is weak, the ruling that catching one rak'ah of Friday prayer suffices still stands because the hadith is authentic through the Abu Hurairah chain. The difference is in the strength of evidence, not the ruling itself.
The ruling is not abandoned; rather, it is based on the stronger chain.
5
Apply the Hanafi preference for the stronger chain
In deriving rulings, Hanafi usul prioritizes a hadith with multiple corroborating chains over a solitary one, especially when the solitary narrator is a mudallis.
This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on certainty (thubut) and avoidance of weak evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعاً. أثر التدليس في اختلاف الحديث وأثره في اختلاف الفقهاء: كَانَ التدليس أحد الأسباب التي دفعت بالرواة إلى الاختلاف في أسانيد بعض الأحاديث، وترتب عَلَى ذَلِكَ تباين في آراء الفقهاء الَّذِيْنَ استدلوا بتلك الأحاديث، وفيما يأتي بعض المسائل التطبيقية: النموذج الأول: عن بقية بن الوليد، عن يونس بن يزيد الأيلي، عن الزهري عن سالم ابن عمر مرفوعاً: «من أدرك ركعة من صلاة الجمعة أو غيرها، فقد أدرك الصلاة». قال أبو بكر بن أبي داود: لَمْ يروه عن يونس إلا بقية». :أقول بقية مدلس ممن اشتهر بتدليس التسوية، وَقَدْ أَخطأَ فِي هَذَا الْحَدِيث من وجهين: الأول: إنه جعل الْحَدِيث من رِوَايَة الزهري عن سالم عن ابن عمر، ورواه الجمع الغفير من أصحاب الزهري عَنْهُ، عن أبي سلمة بن عَبْد الرَّحْمن، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة، مرفوعاً، وهم: 1. مالك بن أنس، وَقَدْ رَوَاهُ عَنْهُ: يحيى بن يحيى الليثي). أبو مصعب الزهري). مالك
Fourth: The effect of tadlis in hadith differences and its effect in juristic differences: Tadlis was one of the reasons that motivated narrators to differ in the chains of some hadith, and that led to disparity in the opinions of the jurists who adduced those hadith. The following are some applied issues: The first model: From Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid, from Yunus ibn Yazid al-Aili, from al-Zuhri, from Salim ibn Umar, marfu': 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Friday prayer or other prayers, has caught the prayer.' Abu Bakr ibn Abi Dawud said: No one narrated it from Yunus except Baqiyyah. I say: Baqiyyah is a mudallis, well-known for tadlis al-taswiyah, and he erred in this hadith in two ways: First: He made the hadith from the narration of al-Zuhri from Salim from Ibn Umar, while the great mass of al-Zuhri's companions narrated it from him, from Abu Salamah ibn Abd al-Rahman, from Abu Hurairah, marfu', and they are: 1. Malik ibn Anas, and the following narrated from him: Yahya ibn Yahya al-Laythi and Abu Mus'ab al-Zuhri. Malik
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage presents a practical example of how tadlis causes differences in hadith chains and consequently in fiqh rulings. The hadith in question is about catching one rak'ah of Friday or other prayers. Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid, a known mudallis who practiced tadlis al-taswiyah (dropping weak narrators in the middle of the chain), narrated it with a chain going through Salim ibn Umar from Ibn Umar. However, the majority of reliable narrators from al-Zuhri transmitted this hadith through Abu Salamah from Abu Hurairah. Abu Bakr ibn Abi Dawud confirms that Baqiyyah is the sole narrator of the chain via Yunus. The author points out two errors: (1) Baqiyyah changed the chain, and (2) the correct chain is well-established from Abu Hurairah. This discrepancy affects the strength of the hadith for fiqh rulings. For example, the Hanafi school uses this hadith to support that if someone catches a rak'ah of Friday prayer, they have caught the prayer; but if the Baqiyyah chain is weak, reliance is placed on the other authentic chain. The list of narrators given (Malik, etc.) confirms the correct version.

Key Terms
تدليس التسوية (tadlīs al-taswiyah): A type of tadlis where the narrator omits weak narrators in the middle of the chain to make the chain appear strong and all narrators trustworthy.
بقية بن الوليد (Baqiyyah ibn al-Walīd): A narrator famous for tadlis al-taswiyah, often criticized for his practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid's error in narrating the hadith about catching one rak'ah?
A) He narrated it from a weak narrator
B) He attributed the hadith to Ibn Umar instead of Abu Hurairah
C) He claimed he heard it directly from the Prophet
D) He changed the text of the hadith

Key Takeaway
Tadlis al-taswiyah can distort a hadith chain, but the Hanafi school relies on the stronger corroborated chain to derive the ruling.

Tarjih by Multiplicity of Narrators: The Case of al-Zuhri's Hadith
Analyzing multiplicity of narrators to prefer one transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi principle of tarjih by multiplicity of narrators and apply it to resolve conflicting hadith transmissions.

Core Idea
Multiplicity of narrators is a key qarina in Hanafi tarjih, outweighing a single contradictory narration.

In this lesson, we examine a classical textual analysis where a hadith transmitted by eleven narrators from al-Zuhri is preferred over a single contradictory narration from Baqiyya. This demonstrates how Hanafi usul uses kathrat al-ruwat (multiplicity of narrators) as a qarina for tarjih. Understanding this method equips you to evaluate conflicting hadith evidence systematically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting transmissions
Locate the two groups: eleven narrators from al-Zuhri vs. Baqiyya's single narration from Yunus. Note that the eleven are listed individually.
The list includes names like Abd al-Rahman ibn Ishaq, Ma'mar, etc.
2
Recognize the stated principle
Find and understand the explicit statement: 'وكثرة الرُّوَاة من القرائن التي ترجح بها الروايات' (multiplicity of narrators is among the evidences by which narrations are preferred). This is the core methodological rule.
This principle is applied immediately after listing the eleven.
3
Analyze internal corroboration
Observe that even within the chain of Yunus ibn Yazid, Baqiyya is contradicted by other reliable narrators like Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak and Ibn Wahb. This weakens Baqiyya's isolation.
The text says 'ثُمَّ إنّ بقية خالف الرُّوَاة عن يونس بن يزيد' then lists the opposing narrators.
4
Observe external corroboration
Note additional independent chains (Muslim via Abu Kurayb, al-Abbas, Khalid, Ibn Thawban) that confirm the majority version. This strengthens the case multivocally.
Each new chain adds weight to the multiplicity argument.
5
Apply the principle to fiqh derivation
Understand that the preferred narration (the one with many transmitters) becomes the basis for legal rulings. The single narration is considered shadhdh and is not acted upon.
For example, the hadith on prayer timings (as mentioned in footnotes) would be derived from the majority version.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عَبْد الرَّحْمن (1) بن إسحاق (2). عبد الوهاب (3) بن أبي بكر (4). عبيد الله بن عمر العمري (5). قرة (6) بن عَبْد الرَّحْمن معمر بن راشد (8). يزيد (9) بن الهاد (10). فهؤلاء أحد عشر نفساً من أصحاب الزهري رووه عَنْهُ، عَلَى خلاف رِوَايَة بقية ابن الوليد، عن يونس بن يزيد، وكثرة الرُّوَاة من القرائن التي ترجح بها الروايات). ثُمَّ إنّ بقية خالف الرُّوَاة عن يونس بن يزيد فَقَدْ رَوَاهُ عَبْد الله بن المبارك، عن يونس بن يزيد عن الزهري، عن أبي سلمة، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة (3)، بِهِ (3) (4) وتابع ابن المبارك عَلَى هَذِهِ الرِّوَايَة ابن وهب، عن يونس ورواه مُسْلِم (5) عن أبي كريب (6) ، عن ابن المبارك، عن معمر والأوزاعي ومالك ويونس أربعتهم مقرونين، عن الزهري بنحو رِوَايَة الجمع. وتابع أبا كريب على جمع هؤلاء الأربعة: العباس بن الوليد (7) النرس (8) ، وخالد بن مرداس (9) (10). ورواه ابن ثوبان (11)، عن الزهري ومكحول (12) مقرونين، عن أبي سلمة، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة.
Abd al-Rahman (1) ibn Ishaq (2). Abd al-Wahhab (3) ibn Abi Bakr (4). Ubaydullah ibn Umar al-Amri (5). Qurra (6) ibn Abd al-Rahman. Ma'mar ibn Rashid (8). Yazid (9) ibn al-Had (10). These are eleven persons from the companions of al-Zuhri who narrated it from him, contrary to the narration of Baqiyya ibn al-Walid from Yunus ibn Yazid. And the multiplicity of narrators is among the circumstantial evidences by which narrations are given preference. Then, indeed Baqiyya opposed the narrators from Yunus ibn Yazid. For Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak narrated it from Yunus ibn Yazid from al-Zuhri from Abu Salama from Abu Hurayra (3), with it (3) (4). And Ibn Wahb followed Ibn al-Mubarak in this narration, from Yunus. And Muslim (5) narrated it from Abu Kurayb (6), from Ibn al-Mubarak, from Ma'mar, al-Awza'i, Malik, and Yunus—all four combined—from al-Zuhri, similar to the narration of the group. And Abu Kurayb in combining these four was followed by al-Abbas ibn al-Walid (7) al-Narsi (8), and Khalid ibn Mirdas (9) (10). And Ibn Thawban (11) narrated it, from al-Zuhri and Mak-hul (12) combined, from Abu Salama from Abu Hurayra.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis demonstrating the principle of tarjih (preferring one narration over another) based on the multiplicity of narrators (kathrat al-ruwat). The author lists eleven narrators who transmitted a hadith from al-Zuhri on the authority of Abu Salama from Abu Hurayra. These eleven narrators are contrasted with the single narration of Baqiyya ibn al-Walid from Yunus ibn Yazid from al-Zuhri. The author states that multiplicity of narrators is one of the qara'in (circumstantial evidences) used to prefer one narration. Then, the author shows that even within the chain of Yunus ibn Yazid, Baqiyya contradicted other reliable narrators like Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak and Ibn Wahb, who transmitted the same hadith from Yunus. Furthermore, Muslim ibn al-Hajjaj narrated it via Abu Kurayb from Ibn al-Mubarak, combining Ma'mar, al-Awza'i, Malik, and Yunus together, all from al-Zuhri, confirming the group's version. Additional corroboration comes from al-Abbas ibn al-Walid al-Narsi and Khalid ibn Mirdas. Finally, Ibn Thawban narrated it from al-Zuhri and Makhul combined, further strengthening the majority version. The purpose is to establish that the transmission of the eleven companions of al-Zuhri is more reliable than Baqiyya's single narration, which has implications for fiqh rulings derived from this hadith.

Key Terms
قرينة (qarina): A circumstantial evidence or indicator that helps prefer one narration over another.
ترجيح (tarjih): The process of preferring one evidence over another due to stronger indicators.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many narrators from al-Zuhri are mentioned as transmitting the hadith contrary to Baqiyya's narration?
A) Five
B) Eleven
C) Four
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
Multiplicity of narrators is a core qarina in Hanafi tarjih, allowing systematic resolution of conflicting hadith by preferring widely transmitted versions.

Detecting Narrator Error: The Case of Baqiyya's Version of the Hadith on Catching a Rak'ah
Analyzing a narrator's error in chain and text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the error of Baqiyya in chain and text of the hadith 'Whoever catches a rak'ah' and explain its impact on the generality of the ruling.

Core Idea
Baqiyya added 'Friday' to a general hadith; the correct version shows no such specification.

This passage examines a famous hadith often cited in fiqh discussions about catching a prayer. A narrator named Baqiyya ibn al-Walid transmitted a version that includes the word 'Friday,' while the majority of narrators from al-Zuhri report a general wording. Understanding this error is crucial for correctly applying the hadith in fiqh, especially in the Hanafi school which relies on the generality of the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the correct chain
Trace the majority narration from al-Zuhri via Abu Salama from Abu Hurayrah. Note that Baqiyya opposed this chain.
2
Identify the correct text
The correct wording is general: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of prayer.' Baqiyya added 'of Friday prayer or other than it.'
3
Examine the evidence for the error
Look at the support from al-Zuhri's own statements and al-Bayhaqi's commentary.
4
Analyze the implications for fiqh
The general wording includes all prayers, including Friday, so no need for a specific mention.
5
Recognize secondary issues
Even if chain error is ignored, tadlis al-taswiya remains problematic.

الفصل الأول الاختلاف في السند ثُمَّ إنّ بقية خالف الرُّوَاة عن يونس بن يزيد فَقَدْ رَوَاهُ عَبْد الله بن المبارك، عن يونس بن يزيد عن الزهري، عن أبي سلمة، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة، وتابع ابن المبارك عَلَى هَذِهِ الرِّوَايَة ابن وهب، عن يونس ورواه مُسْلِم عن أبي كريب، عن ابن المبارك، عن معمر والأوزاعي ومالك ويونس أربعتهم مقرونين، عن الزهري بنحو رِوَايَة الجمع. وتابع أبا كريب على جمع هؤلاء الأربعة: العباس بن الوليد النرسي، وخالد بن مرداس ورواه ابن ثوبان، عن الزهري ومكحول مقرونين، عن أبي سلمة، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة. كرواية الأكثرين. الثاني: أنه أخطأ في متن الْحَدِيث فرواه بلفظ: «من أدرك ركعة من صلاة الجمعة أو غيرها، فَقَدْ أدرك الصلاة». ولفظ الْحَدِيث في رِوَايَة الجمع: (من أدرك ركعة من الصلاة فَقَدْ أدرك الصَّلاة» أو نحوه لا ذكر في شيء من ألفاظه للجمعة، فتبين أنها من وهم بقية، يؤيده: كَانَ مذهب الزهري حمل هَذَا الْحَدِيث المطلق عَلَى صلاة الجمعة، فيرى أن من أدرك من الجمعة ركعة فقد أدركها، ورواه عَنْهُ البخاري في القراءة خلف الإمامِ بلفظ: ونرى لما بلغنا عن رَسُول الله الله أنه من أدرك من الجمعة ركعة واحدة فقد أدرك». ٢. ومما يدل عَلَى أنّ لا ذكر للفظ الجمعة في حَدِيث الزهري هَذَا، أن البيهقي بَعْدَ أن رَوَى الْحَدِيث من طريق معمر عن الزهري، نقل قَوْل الزهري عقبه: «والجمعة من الصلاة». وعقب عَلَيْهِ فَقَالَ: «هَذَا هُوَ الصَّحِيح، وَهُوَ رِوَايَة الجماعة عن الزهري، وفي رِوَايَة معمر دلالة عَلَى أنّ لفظ الْحَدِيث في الصلاة مطلق، وأنها بعمومها تتناول الجمعة كَمَا تتناول غيرها من الصلوات». ومن هَذَا يتبين وهم بقية إسناداً ومتناً، وَقَدْ نص عَلَى هَذَا الإمام أبو حاتم الرازي، إِذْ سأله ابنه فَقَالَ: «سألت أبي عن حَدِيث رَوَاهُ بقية، عن يونس بن يزيد، عن الزهري عن سالم عن ابن عمر النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «من أدرك ركعة من الجمعة عن وغيرها فَقَدْ أدرك الصلاة. فسمعت أبي يقول: هَذا خطأ إنما هُوَ الزهري، عن أبي سلمة، عن أبي [؟] هُرَيْرَة، عن النَّبِيِّ». وَقَالَ الحافظ ابن حجر: إن سَلِمَ من وهم بقية، ففيه تدليسه التسوية؛ لأنه عنعن
Chapter One: Disagreement in the Chain. Then indeed Baqiyya opposed the narrators from Yunus ibn Yazid. For 'Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak narrated it from Yunus ibn Yazid from al-Zuhri from Abu Salama from Abu Hurayrah. And Ibn Wahb followed Ibn al-Mubarak in this narration from Yunus. Muslim narrated it from Abu Kurayb from Ibn al-Mubarak from Ma'mar, al-Awza'i, Malik, and Yunus—all four combined—from al-Zuhri, similar to the narration of the group. And Abu Kurayb was followed in combining these four by al-'Abbas ibn al-Walid al-Narsi and Khalid ibn Mirdas. And Ibn Thawban narrated it from al-Zuhri and Mak-hul combined, from Abu Salama, from Abu Hurayrah, as the majority narrated. Second: That he erred in the text of the hadith and narrated it with the wording: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of Friday prayer or other than it, he has caught the prayer.' And the wording of the hadith in the narration of the group is: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of prayer, he has caught the prayer' or similar—no mention in any of its wordings of Friday. So it became clear that it is from the error of Baqiyya. Supporting it: The position of al-Zuhri was to interpret this general hadith regarding Friday prayer, so he held that whoever catches a rak'ah of Friday prayer has caught it. And al-Bukhari narrated from him in 'al-Qira'a khalf al-Imam' with the wording: 'And we consider, based on what reached us from the Messenger of Allah, that whoever catches one rak'ah of Friday prayer has caught it.' 2. And what indicates that there is no mention of the word 'Friday' in this hadith of al-Zuhri is that al-Bayhaqi, after narrating the hadith via Ma'mar from al-Zuhri, transmitted al-Zuhri's statement after it: 'And Friday is part of prayer.' And he commented on it saying: 'This is correct, and it is the narration of the group from al-Zuhri. And in Ma'mar's narration is evidence that the wording of the hadith is absolute regarding prayer, and its generality includes Friday as it includes other prayers.' And from this the error of Baqiyya in chain and text becomes clear. And Imam Abu Hatim al-Razi explicitly stated this when his son asked him: 'I asked my father about a hadith narrated by Baqiyya from Yunus ibn Yazid from al-Zuhri from Salim from Ibn 'Umar from the Prophet: «Whoever catches a rak'ah of Friday prayer or other than it has caught the prayer.» And I heard my father say: This is a mistake; it is only al-Zuhri from Abu Salama from Abu Hurayrah from the Prophet.' And al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: 'If one is safe from the error of Baqiyya, then there is in it his tadlis al-taswiya because he narrates by 'an'anah.'
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage performs a critical analysis of a hadith to demonstrate a narrator's error (wahm) both in chain (sanad) and text (matn). The author, in a work on the effect of differences in chains and texts on juristic disagreements, examines the hadith 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of prayer has caught the prayer.' The correct version, narrated by the majority from al-Zuhri, does not specify Friday. However, Baqiyya ibn al-Walid narrated it with the addition 'of Friday prayer' and also altered the chain. The author first shows that in the chain, Baqiyya opposed many reliable narrators who all transmitted from Yunus ibn Yazid from al-Zuhri from Abu Salama from Abu Hurayrah. He lists supporting narrators like Ibn al-Mubarak, Ibn Wahb, and the group mentioned by Muslim. Then, the second point: the text error. Baqiyya's version includes 'Friday prayer,' while the authentic version is general. This is supported by al-Zuhri's own interpretation, as recorded by al-Bukhari, where al-Zuhri applied the general hadith to Friday. Al-Bayhaqi's report further confirms that the original hadith is absolute ('amm) and includes Friday by generality. The author then cites Abu Hatim al-Razi, who explicitly declared Baqiyya's version a mistake. Ibn Hajar adds that even if the chain error is ignored, Baqiyya's tadlis al-taswiye (dropping a weak link by using 'an) is problematic. The passage thus demonstrates how a single narrator's error can affect both the authenticity and the fiqh application of a hadith.

Key Terms
وهم (wahm): An error made by a narrator in the chain or text of a hadith, as distinguished from intentional forgery.
تدليس التسوية (tadlis al-taswiya): A type of tadlis where a narrator drops a weak link between two reliable narrators, making the chain appear stronger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct chain for the hadith 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of prayer' according to the majority?
A) al-Zuhri from Salim from Ibn 'Umar.
B) al-Zuhri from Abu Salama from Abu Hurayrah.
C) Baqiyya from Yunus from al-Zuhri from Salim from Ibn 'Umar.
D) Ibn al-Mubarak from Yunus from al-Zuhri from Abu Salama from Abu Hurayrah.

Key Takeaway
The correct version of the hadith is general; Baqiyya's addition of 'Friday' is an error in both chain and text, and the Hanafi school relies on the general wording to include Friday prayer.

Baqiyyah's Error in the Jumu'ah Hadith: Chain, Text, and Fiqh Impact
Analyzing chain and text error of Baqiyyah and its effect on Jumu'ah catching rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Baqiyyah's error in both chain and text of the Jumu'ah hadith and explain how this erroneous addition led to a specific fiqh dispute regarding what constitutes catching Jumu'ah prayer.

Core Idea
A narrator's addition of 'Jumu'ah' to a general hadith created a false fiqh opinion that must be rejected by authentic transmission.

In this lesson, we examine a case where the hadith transmitter Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid mistakenly added the word 'Jumu'ah' to the well-known hadith about catching a rak'ah. Multiple hadith critics, including Abu Hatim al-Razi and Ibn Hajar, identified this error in both the chain (isnad) and the text (matn). The error had a direct impact on a fiqh question: Does one who catches only a rak'ah of Jumu'ah prayer validly complete the prayer, or is catching part of the sermon also required? Understanding this case sharpens your ability to evaluate hadith evidence and its application in fiqh. The Hanafi school, relying on the correct transmission, holds that catching one rak'ah suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the correct hadith
The authentic version transmitted by al-Zuhri and the majority (jama'ah) is: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of prayer has caught the prayer' with no mention of Jumu'ah. Identify this as the baseline.
This hadith is general in wording: 'min al-salah' includes all prayers.
2
Detect Baqiyyah's addition
Baqiyyah narrated the hadith with the addition: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Jumu'ah prayer or other prayers…' and with a different chain (al-Zuhri from Salim from Ibn Umar instead of Abu Salamah from Abu Hurayrah).
This is an example of wahm (error) in both sanad and matn.
3
Confirm the error with external evidence
Scholars like Abu Hatim al-Razi explicitly declared it an error. Al-Bayhaqi noted that al-Zuhri himself only applied the hadith to Jumu'ah by interpretation, not because the word appeared in the text.
The testimony of imams of jarh wa ta'dil is crucial for establishing authenticity.
4
Assess the fiqh consequence
Based on the erroneous version, the Hadawiyyah Zaydiyyah (and some early scholars) argued that Jumu'ah is not valid unless one catches part of the sermon, because they thought the hadith specifically addressed Jumu'ah. The correct general hadith shows that catching one rak'ah is sufficient.
This demonstrates how a transmission error can generate a false fiqh opinion.
5
Understand the usul principle
The case illustrates that a narrator's wahm (error) must be identified through comparison with more reliable narrators (thiqat) and the majority (jama'ah). Relying on an erroneous text leads to unsound rulings.
In Hanafi usul, such ziyada (addition) by a single narrator is rejected if it contradicts the authentic riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول الاختلاف في السند
هُرَيْرَة، بِهِ . كرواية الأكثرين.
الثاني: أنه أخطأ في متن الْحَدِيث فرواه بلفظ: «من أدرك ركعة من صلاة الجمعة أو غيرها، فَقَدْ أدرك الصلاة». ولفظ الْحَدِيث في رِوَايَة الجمع: (من أدرك ركعة من الصلاة فَقَدْ أدرك الصَّلاة» أو نحوه لا ذكر في شيء من ألفاظه للجمعة، فتبين أنها من وهم بقية، يؤيده: كَانَ مذهب الزهري حمل هَذَا الْحَدِيث المطلق عَلَى صلاة الجمعة، فيرى أن من أدرك من الجمعة ركعة فقد أدركها، ورواه عَنْهُ البخاري في القراءة خلف الإمامِ بلفظ: ونرى لما بلغنا عن رَسُول الله الله أنه من أدرك من الجمعة ركعة واحدة فقد أدرك.
٢. ومما يدل عَلَى أنّ لا ذكر للفظ الجمعة في حَدِيث الزهري هَذَا، أن البيهقي بَعْدَ أن رَوَى الْحَدِيث من طريق معمر عن الزهري، نقل قَوْل الزهري عقبه: «والجمعة من الصلاة». وعقب عَلَيْهِ فَقَالَ: «هَذَا هُوَ الصَّحِيح ، وَهُوَ رِوَايَة الجماعة عن الزهري، وفي رِوَايَة معمر دلالة عَلَى أنّ لفظ الْحَدِيث في الصلاة مطلق، وأنها بعمومها تتناول الجمعة كَمَا تتناول غيرها من الصلوات».
ومن هَذَا يتبين وهم بقية إسناداً ومتناً، وَقَدْ نص عَلَى هَذَا الإمام أبو حاتم الرازي ، إِذْ سأله ابنه فَقَالَ: «سألت أبي عن حَدِيث رَوَاهُ بقية، عن يونس بن يزيد، عن الزهري عن سالم عن ابن عمر النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «من أدرك ركعة من الجمعة عن وغيرها فَقَدْ أدرك الصلاة. فسمعت أبي يقول: هَذا خطأ إنما هُوَ الزهري، عن أبي سلمة، عن أبي أبي هُرَيْرَة، عن النَّبِيِّ ) . وَقَالَ الحافظ ابن حجر: إن سَلِمَ من وهم بقية، ففيه تدليسه التسوية؛ لأنه عنعن لشيخه.
وَقَالَ ابن أبي حاتم أيضاً: سألت أبي عن حَدِيث رَوَاهُ بقية، عن يونس، عـن الزهري عن سالم عن ابن عمر عن النَّبي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «من أدرك ركعة من صلاة الجمعة وغيرها فَقَدْ أدرك». قَالَ أبي هَذا خطأ الْمَثْن والإسناد إنما هُوَ: الزهري، عن أبي سلمة، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة ، عن النبي ، من أدرك من صلاة ركعة فقد أدركها»، وأما قوله: «من صلاة الجمعة فليس هَذَا فِي الْحَدِيث، فوهم في كليهما».
أثر هذا الحديث في اختلاف الفقهاء المقدار الذي تدرك به صلاة الجمعة) : اختلف الفقهاء في حكم من سبق في صلاة الجمعة على ثلاثة مذاهب: الأول: لا تصح الجمعة لِمَنْ لَمْ يدرك شيئاً من خطبة الإمام. وبه قال الهادوية مـن الزيدية. وروي عن عمر بن بن الخطاب، ومجاهد، وعطاء، وطاووس، ومكحول. وحجتهم أن الإجماع منعقد عَلَى أن الإمام لَوْ لَمْ يخطب بالناس لَمْ يُصلوا إلا أربعاً، فدل ذلِكَ عَلَى أن الخطبة جزء من الصلاة). وهذا الرأي مخالف لصريح السنة كما يأتي.
Chapter One: Disagreement in Chain
The second [error]: He (Baqiyyah) made a mistake in the text of the hadeeth, narrating it with the wording: "Whoever catches one rak‘ah of Jumu‘ah prayer or other prayers has caught the prayer." But the wording of the hadeeth in the narration of the group is: "Whoever catches one rak‘ah of prayer has caught the prayer" or similar, with no mention of Jumu‘ah in any of its wordings. Thus it became clear that this is a mistake of Baqiyyah. Supporting this: the madhhab of al-Zuhri was to interpret this absolute hadeeth as applying to Jumu‘ah prayer, so he held that whoever catches one rak‘ah of Jumu‘ah has caught it. Al-Bukhari narrated from him in "al-Qira’ah Khalf al-Imam" with the wording: "And we hold, based on what has reached us from the Messenger of Allah — that whoever catches one rak‘ah of Jumu‘ah has caught (the prayer)."
2. Among the evidence that there is no mention of the word "Jumu‘ah" in this hadeeth of al-Zuhri is that al-Bayhaqi, after narrating the hadeeth via the route of Ma‘mar from al-Zuhri, quoted al-Zuhri’s statement after it: "And Jumu‘ah is among the prayers." Then al-Bayhaqi commented: "This is the correct (version), and it is the narration of the group from al-Zuhri, and in the narration of Ma‘mar there is an indication that the wording of the hadeeth applies to prayer in an absolute sense, and that it, by its generality, includes Jumu‘ah just as it includes other prayers."
From this the mistake of Baqiyyah, in both chain and text, becomes clear. Imam Abu Hatim al-Razi explicitly stated this: when his son asked him, "I asked my father about a hadeeth narrated by Baqiyyah from Yunus ibn Yazid from al-Zuhri from Salim from Ibn ‘Umar from the Prophet (ﷺ): 'Whoever catches one rak‘ah of Jumu‘ah or other prayers has caught the prayer.' I heard my father say: 'This is an error. It is only (from) al-Zuhri from Abu Salamah from Abu Hurayrah from the Prophet (ﷺ).'" Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: "Even if one is safe from Baqiyyah’s mistake, there is in it his tadlis al-taswiyah because he narrated with 'an‘anah from his shaykh."
Ibn Abi Hatim also said: "I asked my father about a hadeeth narrated by Baqiyyah from Yunus from al-Zuhri from Salim from Ibn ‘Umar from the Prophet (ﷺ) that he said: 'Whoever catches one rak‘ah of Jumu‘ah prayer and others has caught (the prayer).' My father said: 'This is an error in both text and chain. It is only (from) al-Zuhri from Abu Salamah from Abu Hurayrah from the Prophet (ﷺ): Whoever catches one rak‘ah of prayer has caught it. As for his saying "of Jumu‘ah prayer", this is not found in the hadeeth, so he erred in both (chain and text)."
The Impact of This Hadeeth on the Disagreement of the Jurists Concerning the Amount by Which Jumu‘ah Prayer Is Caught): The jurists differed regarding the ruling for one who is late for Jumu‘ah prayer into three madhhabs: The first: Jumu‘ah is not valid for one who does not catch anything of the imam’s sermon. This was held by the Hadawiyyah among the Zaydiyyah, and it was narrated from ‘Umar ibn al-Khattab, Mujahid, ‘Ata’, Tawus, and Makhul. Their evidence is that there is consensus that if the imam did not deliver the sermon to the people, they would pray only four (rak‘ahs), so this indicates that the sermon is part of the prayer. This opinion contradicts the clear Sunnah, as will follow.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of a hadith transmission error and its fiqh implications. The author first demonstrates that Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid mistakenly added the word 'Jumu‘ah' to the hadith about catching a rak‘ah. The correct narration from al-Zuhri is general: 'Whoever catches a rak‘ah of prayer has caught the prayer.' Multiple scholars, including Abu Hatim al-Razi and Ibn Hajar, confirm the error in both chain and text. The passage then transitions to the fiqh dispute: whether catching a rak‘ah of Jumu‘ah requires also catching part of the sermon. The first madhhab (Hadawiyyah Zaydiyyah and some early scholars) holds that Jumu‘ah is invalid if one misses the entire sermon, arguing that the sermon is part of the prayer. The author notes this contradicts clear Sunnah, implying preference for the other views not fully stated here. For Hanafi students, note that the Hanafi position (not fully given) is that one catches Jumu‘ah by catching one rak‘ah with the imam, and the sermon is not a condition for validity.

Key Terms
الوهم (al-wahm): Error in hadith narration, either in chain or text, due to narrator's mistake.
إسناد (isnad): Chain of narrators transmitting a hadith.
متن (matn): Text/content of a hadith.
تدليس التسوية (tadlis al-taswiyah): A type of tadlis where the narrator omits a weak link between trustworthy narrators, making the chain appear continuous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct hadith (without Baqiyyah's addition), what is the condition for being considered to have caught Jumu'ah prayer?
A) Catching the entire sermon and one rak'ah
B) Catching one rak'ah with the imam
C) Catching two rak'ahs with the imam
D) Catching the sermon only

Key Takeaway
The correct transmission of the hadith 'man adraka rak'atan min al-salah' is general; Baqiyyah's addition is a proven error, and this error led to a fiqh dispute that must be resolved by authentic texts.

Second Model: Hadith on Looking at Private Parts
Presents a weak hadith and its chain of narrators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a weak narrator in a hadith chain and evaluate why the hadith is not considered authentic evidence in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
A weak narrator in the chain invalidates the hadith; even if listed in multiple works, if those works specialize in weak narrations, the hadith is rejected.

This passage presents a second model of how differences in chains (asanid) affect the acceptability of a hadith. The hadith prohibits looking at private parts during intercourse, but its chain includes Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid, a narrator known for tadlis. Scholars like Ibn Hibban recorded it in al-Majruhin, a book that collects weak narrators, signaling that this hadith is weak. Understanding such chain analysis is crucial for usul al-fiqh, as only authentic hadith can serve as evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full chain
Write out the chain of narrators from the text: Hisham ibn Khalid → Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid → Ibn Jurayj → 'Ata' → Ibn 'Abbas → the Prophet ﷺ.
The chain is also known as sanad.
2
Check each narrator’s reliability
Research or recall the status of each narrator. Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid is known for tadlis and is considered weak by major hadith critics. The others are generally reliable.
Tadlis means concealing defects in the chain.
3
Note the books that record this hadith
The text mentions Ibn Abi Hatim's al-'Ilal, Ibn Hibban's al-Majruhin, Ibn 'Adi's al-Kamil, al-Bayhaqi's al-Sunan al-Kubra, and Ibn 'Asakir's Tarikh Dimashq. These are works that often include weak narrations for critical study.
Al-Majruhin specifically lists criticized narrators.
4
Conclude on hadith strength
Since the chain includes a weak narrator (Baqiyyah) and the hadith appears in books of weak narrations, the hadith is classified as da'if (weak) or munkar (rejected). It is not authentic.
Weak hadith cannot be used as evidence for rulings (ahkam).
5
Assess impact on fiqh evidence
Because the hadith is weak, it cannot be used to prove that looking at private parts causes blindness or that it is prohibited. Hanafi fiqh does not rely on this hadith.
Authentic hadith must have a continuous chain of trustworthy narrators.

النموذج الثاني:
حديث هشام بن خالد، عن بقية بن الوليد، عن ابن جريج، عن عطاء، عن ابن عباس قال: قال رسول الله ﷺ: «إذا جامع أحدكم زوجته أو جاريته فلا ينظر إلى فرجها، فإن ذلك يورث العمى».
رواه من هذه الطريق ابن أبي حاتم في "العلل"، وابن حبان في "المجروحين"، وابن عدي في "الكامل"، والبيهقي في "السنن الكبرى"، وابن عساكر في "تاريخ دمشق".
The Second Model: The hadith of Hisham ibn Khalid, from Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid, from Ibn Jurayj, from 'Ata', from Ibn 'Abbas who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'When one of you has intercourse with his wife or his slave-woman, let him not look at her private part, for that causes blindness.' It is narrated via this route by Ibn Abi Hatim in al-'Ilal, Ibn Hibban in al-Majruhin, Ibn 'Adi in al-Kamil, al-Bayhaqi in al-Sunan al-Kubra, and Ibn 'Asakir in Tarikh Dimashq.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage presents a second example of how differences in the chain (sanad) affect the acceptability of a hadith. The hadith in question prohibits looking at the private part during intercourse, claiming that it causes blindness. The chain includes Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid, who is known for tadlis (concealing defects), and the hadith is considered munkar (rejected). The passage lists several hadith scholars (Ibn Abi Hatim, Ibn Hibban, Ibn 'Adi, al-Bayhaqi, Ibn 'Asakir) who recorded this hadith, but in works that often collect weak narrations (like al-'Ilal, al-Majruhin, al-Kamil). This indicates that the hadith is known but not accepted as authentic. The passage illustrates how the strength of a chain determines whether a hadith can be used as evidence in fiqh.

Key Terms
بقية بن الوليد (Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid): A narrator known for tadlis, often considered weak.
المجروحين (al-Majruhin): A book by Ibn Hibban listing narrators who are criticized and their narrations are weak.
العلل (al-'Ilal): A book by Ibn Abi Hatim that discusses hidden defects in hadith.
الكامل (al-Kamil): A book by Ibn 'Adi that collects weak narrators and their narrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Hisham ibn Khalid
B) Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid
C) Ibn Jurayj
D) 'Ata'

Key Takeaway
A hadith with a weak narrator in its chain is not acceptable as evidence in Hanafi fiqh, even if recorded in multiple books.

Hadith Criticism and Its Impact on Fiqh: Looking at Spouse's Private Parts
Analyzing a disputed hadith chain and its juristic impact

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the impact of hadith chain criticism (tadlis and 'an'ana) on juristic disagreement, and apply the Hanafi principle of rejecting weak hadith in favor of original permissibility (ibaha asliyya).

Core Idea
A weak hadith cannot establish a prohibition; the Hanafi school relies on original permissibility in the absence of authentic proof.

This passage presents a concrete case study of how differences in hadith chains directly translate into differences in fiqh rulings. We examine a hadith that apparently forbids looking at the spouse's private parts during intercourse. The hadith is scrutinized by major critics who identify tadlis and weak narrators, rendering it unreliable. Consequently, Hanafi jurists uphold the default permissibility, while Shafi'is and Hanbalis, considering other factors, deem it disliked. This lesson sharpens your ability to trace the link between chain authenticity and legal rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its chain
Read the hadith text and its chain: Hisham ibn Khalid ← Baqiyya ← Ibn Jurayj ← 'Ata' ← Ibn 'Abbas. Note the key narrators and how they transmit.
Baqiyya and Ibn Jurayj are known for tadlis and 'an'ana respectively.
2
Analyze the criticism from hadith scholars
Review the statements of Abu Hatim, Ibn Hibban, and Ibn 'Adi. They identify Baqiyya's tadlis as the core defect; he inserted weak or unknown narrators between himself and Ibn Jurayj.
Also note that Ibn Jurayj's 'an'ana raises suspicion since he rarely narrated except from criticized narrators.
3
Assess the authenticity of the hadith
Based on the criticism, determine the reliability of the hadith. The consensus of critics is that it is fabricated (mawdu') or extremely weak.
Thus, the hadith cannot serve as a valid proof (dalil) for prohibition.
4
Identify the resulting juristic positions
The text states two positions: Shafi'is/Hanbalis consider looking disliked; Hanafis and majority permit it. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical difference in ruling.
The Hanafi position is based on the principle that what is not explicitly forbidden remains permissible (ibaha asliyya).
5
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
Connect the hadith criticism to the fiqh ruling: Because the hadith is weak, it does not overcome the default of permissibility. Hanafi usul holds that a zanni dalil cannot establish a prohibition when the default is ibaha.
This illustrates the process of istidlal: deriving rulings from valid sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النموذج الثاني:
حديث هشام بن خالد، عن بقية بن الوليد، عن ابن جريج، عن عطاء، عن ابن عباس قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إذا جامع أحدكم زوجته أو جاريته فلا ينظر إلى فرجها، فإن ذلك يورث العمى».
رواه من هذه الطريق ابن أبي حاتم في " العلل " وابن حبان في " المجروحين "، وابن عدي في " الكامل "، والبيهقي في " السنن الكبرى "، وابن عساكر في " تاريخ دمشق ".
والحديث هذا أورده ابن الجوزي في " الموضوعات "، وقال أبو حاتم بعد أن أورده مع حديثين آخرين: هذه الثلاث الأحاديث موضوعة لا أصل لها، وكان بقية يدلس، فظن هؤلاء أنه يقول في كل حديث «حدثنا» ولم يفتقدوا الخبر منه. وقال ابن حبان: يشبه أن يكون بقية سمعه من إنسان ضعيف عن ابن جريج، فدلس عنه، فالتزق كل ذلك به. وقال ابن عدي بعد روايته: حدثناه بهذا الإسناد ثلاثة أحاديث أخر مناكير، وهذه الأحاديث يشبه أن تكون بين بقية وابن جريج بعض المجهولين أو بعض الضعفاء؛ لأن بقية كثيراً ما يدخل بين نفسه وبين ابن جريج بعض الضعفاء أو بعض المجهولين. فمن هذا كله يتضح أن بقية قد دلسه عن بعض الواهين، أو لربما دلّس مشيخة ابن جريج، لاسيما وقد عنعن ابن جريج، وهو لا يكاد يدلس إلا عن مطعون فيه.
أثر الحديث في اختلاف الفقهاء (نظر الزوج إلى فرج زوجته أو حليلته): اختلف الفقهاء في جواز نظر الزوج إلى فرج زوجته أو ملك يده على مذهبين: الأول: يكره للزوج النظر إلى فرج زوجته كما يكره للزوجة النظر إلى فرج زوجها، وإليه ذهب الشافعية والحنابلة. الثاني: ذهب جمهور الفقهاء إلى إباحة نظر كل من الزوجين إلى فرج الآخر، ونظر المالك إلى فرج مملوكته، ونظر المملوكة إلى فرج مالكها. وبه قال الحنفية.
The second model: Hadith of Hisham ibn Khalid, from Baqiyya ibn al-Walid, from Ibn Jurayj, from 'Ata', from Ibn 'Abbas, who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When one of you has intercourse with his wife or his slave-girl, let him not look at her private part, for that causes blindness.' It was narrated through this chain by Ibn Abi Hatim in al-'Ilal, Ibn Hibban in al-Majruhin, Ibn 'Adi in al-Kamil, al-Bayhaqi in al-Sunan al-Kubra, and Ibn 'Asakir in Tarikh Dimashq. Ibn al-Jawzi mentioned this hadith in al-Mawdu'at, and Abu Hatim said after mentioning it along with two other hadiths: 'These three hadiths are fabricated, with no basis. Baqiyya used to practice tadlis, and these narrators thought he said "haddathana" in every hadith, but they did not verify the report from him.' Ibn Hibban said: 'It appears that Baqiyya heard it from a weak narrator from Ibn Jurayj, then he practiced tadlis from him, so all of that became attached to him.' Ibn 'Adi said after narrating it: 'We narrated through this chain three other hadiths that are munkar. It seems that between Baqiyya and Ibn Jurayj there are some unknown or weak narrators, because Baqiyya often inserts weak or unknown narrators between himself and Ibn Jurayj.' From all this, it becomes clear that Baqiyya practiced tadlis from some weak narrators, or perhaps he practiced tadlis from the teachers of Ibn Jurayj, especially since Ibn Jurayj narrated with 'an'ana, and he hardly ever practiced tadlis except from a criticized narrator. The effect of the hadith on the disagreement of jurists (regarding the husband looking at his wife's or his concubine's private part): The jurists differed on the permissibility of a husband looking at his wife's private part or his slave-girl's private part into two schools: First: It is disliked for the husband to look at his wife's private part, just as it is disliked for the wife to look at her husband's private part. This is the view of the Shafi'is and Hanbalis. Second: The majority of jurists permit both spouses to look at each other's private parts, and the owner looking at his female slave's private part, and the female slave looking at her owner's private part. This is the view of the Hanafis.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage presents a case study (النموذج الثاني) of how differences in hadith chains lead to differences in fiqh rulings. The hadith under discussion prohibits looking at the spouse's private parts during intercourse, with a severe warning that it causes blindness. The author then examines the chain, citing major hadith critics: Abu Hatim declares it fabricated, Ibn Hibban identifies tadlis by Baqiyya, and Ibn 'Adi notes the presence of unknown narrators. The conclusion is that the hadith is unreliable due to Baqiyya's tadlis and Ibn Jurayj's 'an'ana. Following this chain criticism, the author shows the impact on fiqh: Two opinions emerge. The first (Shafi'is, Hanbalis) holds that looking at the private parts is disliked, relying perhaps on this hadith or other evidences. The second (Hanafis and majority) permits it, likely because they do not accept this hadith as valid and see no prohibition in the Quran or authentic sunnah. The Hanafi position is based on the principle that what is not explicitly forbidden is permissible, and there is no authentic text prohibiting it. This lesson illustrates how critical hadith analysis directly affects the derivation of fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
تدليس (tadlis): Concealing a weak link in the chain by using ambiguous wording like 'an (from) instead of haddathana (he narrated to us).
عنعنة (an'ana): A narrator's habit of using 'an (from) without specifying how he heard the hadith, which required investigation to ensure actual hearing.
مطعون فيه (mat'un fihi): A narrator who is criticized and not reliable; his narrations are suspect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason the Hanafi school permits looking at the spouse's private parts?
A) The hadith prohibiting it is weak due to tadlis and 'an'ana.
B) The Quran explicitly permits it.
C) The Hanafis follow a different hadith that allows it.
D) The act is considered a sunnah.

Key Takeaway
A weak hadith cannot establish a prohibition; the default of permissibility (ibaha asliyya) remains until an authentic proof is presented.

Criticism of a Hadith Due to Tadlis by Bqiyya
Analyzing the weakness of a hadith from tadlis of narrator Bqiyya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the nature of tadlis and explain how it weakens a hadith according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Tadlis by a known mudallis can render a hadith unreliable if he conceals weak narrators.

The authenticity of a hadith depends not only on the chain's continuity but also on the honesty of narrators. Tadlis, or concealing defects in the chain, is a serious flaw. This lesson examines how critics identified tadlis by Bqiyya and why his narrations are judged weak.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and the critics
Note that the hadith was recorded by Ibn al-Jawzi and criticized by Abu Hatim, Ibn Hibban, and Ibn Adi.
These critics are known for rigorous evaluation.
2
Understand the claim of tadlis
Tadlis involves using ambiguous terms like 'an (from) to hide a weak or unknown narrator. Bqiyya is known for inserting weak narrators between himself and Ibn Juraij.
3
Analyze the critics' statements
Abu Hatim declared the hadith fabricated and noted that Bqiyya's tadlis misled others. Ibn Hibban suggested Bqiyya heard it from a weak source then deluded. Ibn Adi observed that Bqiyya often inserts unknown or weak narrators.
Each critic provides a different angle but agrees on weakness.
4
Conclude on the hadith's status
Due to Bqiyya's tadlis, the hadith is considered weak (da'if) or even fabricated (mawdu').
This aligns with Hanafi usul that such narrations are not valid for establishing rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحديث هَذَا أورده ابن الجوزي في " الموضوعات (۱)، وَقَالَ أبو حاتم – بَعْدَ أن أورده مع حديثين آخرين -: هَذِهِ الثلاث الأحاديث موضوعة لا أصل لها، وَكَانَ بقية يدلس، فظن هؤلاء أنه يقول في كُلّ حَدِيث «حَدَّثَنَا» وَلَمْ يفتقدوا الخبر مِنْهُ»). وَقَالَ ابن حبان: يشبه أن يَكُون بقية سمعه من إنسان ضعيف عن ابن جريج، فدلس عَنْهُ، فالتزق كُلّ ذَلِكَ بِهِ». وَقَالَ ابن عدي بَعْدَ روايته: حدثناه بهذا الإسناد ثلاثة أحاديث أخر مناكير، وهذه الأحاديث يشبه أن تكون بين بقية وابن جريج بعض المجهولين أو بعض الضعفاء؛ لأن بقية كثيراً ما يدخل بَيْنَ نفسه وبين ابن جريج بعض الضعفاء أو بعض المجهولين). فمن هَذَا كله يتضح أن بقية قد دلسه عن بعض الواهين، أو لربما دلّس مشيخة ابن جريج، لاسيما وَقَدْ عنعن ابن جريج، وَهُوَ لا يكاد يدلس إلا عن مطعون فيه ) .
This hadith was recorded by Ibn al-Jawzi in 'al-Mawdu'at'. Abu Hatim said after citing it with two other hadiths: 'These three hadiths are fabricated, having no basis. Bqiyya used to practice tadlis, and these people thought that he said in every hadith 'he narrated to us' and did not investigate the report from him.' Ibn Hibban said: 'It is likely that Bqiyya heard it from a weak person from Ibn Juraij, and then deluded from him, so all that stuck to him.' Ibn Adi said after narrating it: 'We narrated with this chain three other munkar hadiths. These hadiths are likely that between Bqiyya and Ibn Juraij there are some unknown or weak narrators, because Bqiyya often inserted between himself and Ibn Juraij some weak or unknown narrators.' From all this it becomes clear that Bqiyya has deluded it from some weak narrators, or perhaps he deluded the shaykhs of Ibn Juraij, especially since Ibn Juraij himself practiced 'an'anah, and he hardly ever deludes except from someone criticized.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a hadith criticism example demonstrating how tadlis (concealed transmission) can weaken a hadith. The author presents the opinions of prominent hadith critics: Abu Hatim declares the hadith fabricated, Ibn Hibban suggests Bqiyya heard it from a weak source and then deluded, and Ibn Adi notes that Bqiyya often inserts unknown or weak narrators between himself and Ibn Juraij. The conclusion is that the hadith is unreliable due to Bqiyya's tadlis.

Key Terms
تدليس (tadlis): Concealing a defect in the isnad by using ambiguous terms like 'an (from) to make it appear continuous
بقية (Bqiyya): A narrator known for tadlis, often criticized for inserting weak narrators
عنعن (an'anah): Using the term 'an (from) in narration, which can be a sign of tadlis if the narrator is known to do so
مجهول (majhul): Unknown narrator whose identity or reliability is not established

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is authentic
B) It is fabricated and has no basis
C) It is weak but usable
D) It has a broken chain

Key Takeaway
A hadith narrated by a known mudallis through ambiguous terms is considered weak unless proven otherwise.
