Hadith Criticism: The Story of the Ring in the Toilet
Examining a munkar hadith about removing the ring in the toilet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a munkar hadith by its chain and content, and explain why narrator errors (wahm) undermine legal derivation.

Core Idea
A narrator's error can turn a sound report into a munkar hadith, halting its use as legal proof.

In this lesson, we examine a hadith that many compilations record but scholars declare munkar (denounced) due to a narrator's error. Understanding this critical process is essential for usul al-fiqh: only sound hadith can serve as legal evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hadith and its Claimed Ruling
The hadith states that the Prophet would remove his ring when entering the toilet. If authentic, it would indicate a recommended act of respecting places named after Allah.
This would be a sunnah ruling.
2
Examine the Chain of Narration
Trace the chain: Hammam ibn Yahya from Ibn Juraij from al-Zuhri from Anas. Note that only Hammam narrated it in this wording.
Unique transmission raises suspicion.
3
Recognize the Critic's Declaration
Abu Dawud declared the hadith munkar. He points to a correct narration about the Prophet taking a silver ring and then discarding it, not removing it each time.
Munkar means contradicts more reliable narrations.
4
Locate the Narrator Error (Wahm)
The error is attributed to Hammam ibn Yahya. He likely confused the two reports. No other narrator transmitted this version.
Wahm is a common cause of hadith weakness.
5
Consequences for Legal Derivation
Because the hadith is munkar, it cannot be used as a legal proof (dalil) in Hanafi usul. The ruling of removing the ring is not established from this report.
Only authentic hadith (sahih/hasan) are valid evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النموذج الثالث: ، عن ابن جريج عن الزهري، عن أنس، قَالَ: «كَانَ حَدِيث همام بن يحيى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا دخل الخلاء وضع خاتمه». رَوَاهُ أبو داود وابن ماجه ) ، والترمذي ()، والنسائي)، وابن حبان)، والحاكم (١) ، والبيهقي قال أبو داود عقب تخريجه لهذا الْحَدِيْثِ: «هَذَا حَدِيْث منكر، وإنما يعرف عن ابن جريج عن زياد بن سعد ، عن الزهري عن أنس أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم اتخذ خاتماً من وَرِقٍ ثُمَّ ألقاه، والوهم فيه من همام، وَلَمْ يروه إلا همام». والحديث الذي عناه أبو داود أخرجه أحمد (١٤)، ومسلم(١٥)، (۱۸)
The third model: From Ibn Juraij from al-Zuhri from Anas, he said: 'The hadith of Hammam ibn Yahya: The Prophet, peace be upon him, when he entered the toilet, he would remove his ring.' Narrated by Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Hibban, al-Hakim, and al-Bayhaqi. Abu Dawud said after its takhrij: 'This is a munkar hadith. It is only known from Ibn Juraij from Ziyad ibn Sa'd from al-Zuhri from Anas that the Prophet took a silver ring then discarded it. The error is from Hammam, and no one else narrated it.' And the hadith that Abu Dawud referred to was narrated by Ahmad, Muslim, (18).
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a hadith criticism example showing how a narrator's error (wahm) can produce a munkar (denounced) hadith. The hadith in question states that the Prophet would remove his ring when entering the toilet. Critics, including Abu Dawud, point out that the correct narration is about the Prophet taking a silver ring and then discarding it, not removing it on each occasion. The error is attributed to Hammam ibn Yahya. This underscores the importance of careful isnad criticism in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
منكر (munkar): A hadith that contradicts more reliable narrations, often considered weak
وهم (wahm): An error in a narrator's memory or transmission

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because it contradicts the correct narration about the ring
C) Because Anas was not reliable
D) Because it was not in Muslim

Key Takeaway
A narrator's error (wahm) can render a hadith munkar, making it invalid as legal evidence.

Evaluating Hadith Authenticity: The Case of Hammam's Ring Narration
Critically examining a hadith narration and its chain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the reliability of a hadith by analyzing chains of narration and the concept of mutaba'ah, and apply the Hanafi criterion for accepting a hadith with supporting narrations.

Core Idea
A hadith is not rendered munkar by a single critic's accusation of wahm if there is a mutaba'ah, even if weak, that breaks the tafarud.

This lesson examines a real case where a hadith about the Prophet removing his ring in the toilet was criticized by Abu Dawood as munkar due to an alleged error by Hammam ibn Yahya. The author counters by showing that Hammam has a follow-up narration (mutaba'ah), which undermines the claim of isolation. You will learn how Hanafi usul handles such chain criticism and how it affects the derived fiqh ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its content
Read the hadith: 'When entering the toilet, the Prophet would put down his ring.' Note that this suggests a practice of removing impurity-bearing items.
The hadith is reported by multiple compilers.
2
Understand Abu Dawood's criticism
Abu Dawood declared the hadith munkar, attributing an error (wahm) to Hammam, and claimed it contradicts a more reliable chain from Ziyad ibn Sa'd.
The critical claim is that Hammam's narration is isolated (tafarud) and erroneous.
3
Analyze the author's counter-argument using mutaba'ah
The author demonstrates that Hammam is not alone; there is a mutaba'ah via Yahya ibn al-Mutawakkil, even though that chain itself is weak. This breaks the tafarud and weakens the accusation of wahm.
A mutaba'ah does not have to be strong; it only needs to show that the reporter is not unique.
4
Evaluate the strength of the defence
Consider that al-Bayhaqi weakened the mutaba'ah, but the author argues that any follow-up, even weak, removes the charge of absolute isolation. The Hanafi position accepts such support.
This reflects the Hanafi principle that a hadith can be elevated from shadh to acceptable if supporting narrations exist.
5
Connect to the fiqh ruling
The Hanafi school derives that it is mustahab (recommended) to remove any ring with Allah's name when entering the toilet. The acceptance of this hadith underpins that ruling.
Other schools may not consider it recommended due to the hadith's perceived weakness.

النموذج الثالث: حديث همام بن يحيى، عن ابن جريج عن الزهري، عن أنس، قَالَ: «كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا دخل الخلاء وضع خاتمه». رَوَاهُ أبو داود وابن ماجه، والترمذي، والنسائي، وابن حبان، والحاكم، والبيهقي. قال أبو داود عقب تخريجه لهذا الْحَدِيْثِ: «هَذَا حَدِيْث منكر، وإنما يعرف عن ابن جريج عن زياد بن سعد عن الزهري عن أنس أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم اتخذ خاتماً من وَرِقٍ ثُمَّ ألقاه، والوهم فيه من همام، وَلَمْ يروه إلا همام». والحديث الذي عناه أبو داود أخرجه أحمد، ومسلم، وأبو عوانة، وابن حبان، وأبو الشيخ من الطريق التي أشار إِلَيْهَا أبو داود، عن أنس بألفاظ مختلفة والمعنى واحد: «أنه أبصر فـي يـد رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم خاتماً مـن وَرِق يوماً واحداً، فصنع الناس خواتيمهم من وَرِق. قَالَ فطرح رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم خاتمه، فطرح الناس خواتيمهم». عَلَى أن نسبة الوهم فيه إلى همام فِيْهِ نظر، وهذا الْحَدِيث مشتمل عَلَى ما يأتي: إن توهيم همام في متن الْحَدِيث وإسناده إنما يتجه فيمَا لَوْ صحت دعوى تفرده ومخالفته متناً وإسناداً، ولكننا نجد أن هماماً متابع عَلَيْهِ متناً وإسناداً، فَقَدْ رَوَاهُ الْحَاكِم - ومن طريقه البيهقي - وأخرجه البغوي من طريق يحيى بن المتوكل البصري، عن ابن جريج عن الزهري، عن أنس، به مرفوعاً. إلا أن البيهقي ضعف هَذِهِ المتابعة، ظناً مِنْهُ أن يحيى هَذَا هُوَ: ابن المتوكل، يكنى أبا عقيل مكثر في الرّوَايَة عن بُهَيَّة، وَهُوَ مدني، ويقال: كوفي، ضعفه ابن المديني والنسائي، وَقَالَ ابن معين: ليس بشيء، ووهاه أحمد، ولينه أبو زرعة.
The third model: The hadith of Hammam ibn Yahya, from Ibn Jurayj from al-Zuhri from Anas, who said: 'The Prophet, peace be upon him, when entering the toilet, would put down his ring.' Abu Dawood, Ibn Majah, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Hibban, al-Hakim, and al-Bayhaqi narrated it. Abu Dawood said after citing this hadith: 'This is a munkar hadith; it is only known from Ibn Jurayj from Ziyad ibn Sa'd from al-Zuhri from Anas that the Prophet, peace be upon him, took a silver ring and then threw it away. The error (wahm) in it is from Hammam, and no one narrated it except Hammam.' The hadith that Abu Dawood referred to was narrated by Ahmad, Muslim, Abu 'Awanah, Ibn Hibban, and Abu al-Shaykh via the path Abu Dawood indicated, from Anas with different wordings but the same meaning: 'He saw on the hand of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, a silver ring for one day, so the people made silver rings. He said: Then the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, threw away his ring, so the people threw away their rings.' However, attributing the error to Hammam is open to scrutiny. This hadith includes: The claim that Hammam erred in text and chain is only plausible if his tafarud (isolation) and contradiction in text and chain were proven, but we find that Hammam has a follow-up (mutaba'ah) in text and chain, for al-Hakim—and via him al-Bayhaqi—and al-Baghawi narrated it via the path of Yahya ibn al-Mutawakkil al-Basri, from Ibn Jurayj from al-Zuhri from Anas, raised. Except that al-Bayhaqi weakened this follow-up, thinking that this Yahya is Ibn al-Mutawakkil, known as Abu 'Aqil, who narrated many reports from Bahiyyah, a Medinan (some say Kufan) whom Ibn al-Madini and al-Nasa'i declared weak, Ibn Ma'in said 'nothing', Ahmad declared him unreliable, and Abu Zur'ah considered him lenient.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of a specific hadith narration and the controversy surrounding its chain of transmission. The hadith in question states that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would remove his ring when entering the toilet. The author presents Abu Dawood's assessment that this hadith is munkar (denounced) due to a supposed error (wahm) in the narration by Hammam ibn Yahya, who allegedly contradicted a more reliable chain from Ziyad ibn Sa'd. However, the author then demonstrates that this claim of error is questionable because Hammam's narration is supported by a follow-up narration (mutaba'ah) via Yahya ibn al-Mutawakkil, even though al-Bayhaqi weakened that follow-up due to the weakness of Yahya ibn al-Mutawakkil. The author argues that the attribution of error to Hammam would only be valid if he were isolated and contradictory, but since he has a follow-up, the claim is weakened. This analysis highlights how differences in chains of narration can affect the acceptance of a hadith and consequently the fiqh rulings derived from it. In Hanafi fiqh, the ruling on removing the ring when entering the toilet is derived from this and other narrations; the debate over authenticity impacts whether the act is considered recommended or not.

Key Terms
وهم (wahm): Error or illusion in a narration; a defect in the memory of a narrator causing a mistake in the text or chain.
متابعة (mutaba'ah): A follow-up narration; another narrator who corroborates a hadith by transmitting it from the same or different chain, strengthening its authenticity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the author argues that Abu Dawood's claim of wahm is questionable?
A) Because many narrators transmitted the hadith
B) Because Hammam is a trustworthy narrator
C) Because there is a mutaba'ah that breaks tafarud
D) Because the hadith is in the Sahihain

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a hadith is not automatically rejected due to a single critic's accusation of error if there is any follow-up narration, even from a weaker chain, that removes the tafarud.

Analyzing a Hadith Chain: Refuting Tafarrud through Mutaba'ah and Identifying a Mudallis
Analyzing a hadith chain to refute tafarrud and identify tadlis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze a hadith chain to identify a mutaba'ah and evaluate the reliability of narrators to refute a claim of tafarrud, applying Hanafi usul principles.

Core Idea
A mutaba'ah from a lesser narrator can refute tafarrud; the error may shift upward to a mudallis.

This passage examines a dispute about the hadith of the Prophet's silver ring. Some claimed that Hammam was alone in narrating it, but the author shows a follow-up narration from Yahya ibn al-Mutawakkil. Al-Bayhaqi doubted it, but the author demonstrates his error and traces the defect to Ibn Jurayj, a mudallis. This analysis is crucial for establishing the hadith's strength, which supports the Hanafi ruling on men wearing silver rings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and its basis
Understand that the claim of tafarrud (uniqueness) against Hammam is undermined by a mutaba'ah (follow-up narration). The author asserts that the accusation of wahm (error) would only hold if Hammam were truly unique.
Tafarrud means a narrator is the sole transmitter of a hadith from a particular source.
2
Evaluate the mutaba'ah
Examine the chain through Yahya ibn al-Mutawakkil al-Basri: from Ibn Jurayj, from al-Zuhri, from Anas. Al-Bayhaqi considered it weak, assuming this Yahya was the weak Madani narrator.
The follow-up chain is: Yahya ibn al-Mutawakkil al-Basri → Ibn Jurayj → al-Zuhri → Anas → Prophet (marfu').
3
Critically assess the counter-argument
Recognize that al-Bayhaqi confused this Yahya with a different, weak narrator. The author shows that the Basri Yahya is acceptable for mutaba'ah, citing Ibn Hibban and al-‘Iraqi.
The condition for a mutaba'ah narrator is not the highest level of trustworthiness; lesser reliability suffices to refute tafarrud.
4
Shift the blame to the mudallis
Determine that the real defect lies not in the Basran narrators but in Ibn Jurayj, who is a mudallis (one who practices tadlis). The Basrans are reliable; Ibn Jurayj concealed his source.
Tadlis involves ambiguity in the isnad; Hanafi scholars treat it as weakening unless samā' is explicit.
5
Apply the conclusion to fiqh
Understand that the hadith is thus strengthened, supporting the Hanafi view that men may wear silver rings. This shows how chain analysis impacts fiqh rulings.
The thubut (transmission certainty) of the hadith is upgraded from possibly weak to hasan or sahih via mutaba'ah.

Chapter One / Difference in the Chain. (3) 79 And Abu ‘Awanah, and Ibn Hibban (3), and Abu al-Shaykh from the path that Abu Dawud indicated, from Anas with different wordings but one meaning: 'He saw on the hand of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, a ring of silver for one day, so the people made their rings of silver. He said: Then the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, threw away his ring, so the people threw away their rings.' However, attributing error (wahm) in it to Hammam is questionable. This hadith includes the following: The accusation of error against Hammam in the text and chain of the hadith would only be valid if his uniqueness (tafarrud) and contradiction in text and chain were established. But we find that Hammam has a follow-up (mutaba‘ah) in text and chain. Indeed, al-Hakim (4) – and through him al-Bayhaqi (5) – and al-Baghawi narrated it from the path of Yahya ibn al-Mutawakkil al-Basri, from Ibn Jurayj, from al-Zuhri, from Anas, marfu‘an. (4) However, al-Bayhaqi considered this follow-up weak, assuming that this Yahya is Ibn al-Mutawakkil, kunyah Abu ‘Uqayl, who narrated excessively from Baha’ah, and he is Madani, and it is said Kufi. Ibn al-Madini and al-Nasa’i declared him weak, Ibn Ma‘in said: 'He is nothing,' Ahmad considered him weak, and Abu Zur‘ah classified him as lenient (10). ... (continues) He said: 'I do not know him,' he meant something other than what comes to mind, which is unknown identity (‘ayn), for he meant unknown state (hal). Hence al-‘Iraqi said, as we quoted earlier: 'Others knew him.' Thus, the validity of Yahya ibn al-Mutawakkil’s follow-up to Hammam is established, and the claim of Hammam’s uniqueness in text and chain is invalid. So the blame, in this case, shifts to the one above him, namely Ibn Jurayj, and he is a mudallis. It appears that the error in this hadith is from Ibn Jurayj, especially since Ibn al-Mutawakkil and Hammam are Basrans, and the scholars have stated that the narration of Basrans from Ibn Jurayj contains defect from the side of Ibn Jurayj, not from the side of the people of Basra. Its explanation: that Ibn Jurayj concealed (dallas) the intermediary between him and al-Zuhri for the Basrans, namely Ziyad ibn...
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of a hadith chain dispute concerning the Prophet's silver ring. The author, a Hanafi scholar, refutes the claim that the narrator Hammam was unique (tafarrud) in narrating this hadith. He demonstrates that a follow-up (mutaba‘ah) from Yahya ibn al-Mutawakkil exists, even though al-Bayhaqi doubted it. The author argues that al-Bayhaqi was mistaken in his assessment because he confused this Yahya with a weaker narrator. By citing Ibn Hibban and al-‘Iraqi, the author shows that Yahya ibn al-Mutawakkil al-Basri is acceptable for mutaba‘ah, and that the condition for a follower is not the highest level of trustworthiness. The discussion shifts the error to Ibn Jurayj, who is known as a mudallis (one who practices tadlis). The author notes that Basran narrations from Ibn Jurayj are defective due to his tadlis, not due to the Basran narrators. This analysis is crucial for Hanafi fiqh because the hadith regarding the silver ring affects rulings on men wearing silver rings—a matter where the Hanafi school permits it based on such narrations. Understanding the chain's strength supports the Hanafi position against those who might reject the hadith based on alleged uniqueness or weakness.

Key Terms
وهم (wahm): Error or mistake attributed to a narrator in hadith criticism, often implying a lapse in memory or accuracy.
متابعة (mutaba‘ah): A follow-up narration that supports a hadith from another chain, reinforcing its authenticity and refuting claims of uniqueness (tafarrud).
مدلس (mudallis): A narrator who practices tadlis, i.e., concealing the identity of his teacher or using ambiguous phrasing to make the chain appear stronger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did al-Bayhaqi consider the follow-up (mutaba‘ah) to be weak?
A) Because he thought Yahya ibn al-Mutawakkil was the Madani narrator who was weak.
B) Because the hadith was only narrated by Hammam.
C) Because Ibn Jurayj was a mudallis.
D) Because the narrators were Basrans.

Key Takeaway
A mutaba'ah from a lesser-known narrator can refute a claim of tafarrud, and the real defect may lie in a mudallis above.

Tracing Hadith Errors: The Case of Ibn Jurayj's Tadlis
Critical analysis of a hadith chain to pinpoint the source of error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify tadlis in a hadith chain, evaluate mutaba'ah support, and assess the reliability of a narrator using critical statements from hadith critics.

Core Idea
Tadlis – concealing gaps in the chain – is a key source of weakness in hadith transmission.

This passage examines a hadith about the Prophet's ring. Al-Bayhaqi thought the chain was weak because a narrator was unknown. The author shows that the real problem is not the unknown narrator but the tadlis of Ibn Jurayj. By analyzing the chain step by step, we learn how to spot transmission errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested narrator
Find the narrator whose reliability is questioned. Here, Yahya ibn al-Mutawakkil is initially claimed unknown by Ibn Ma'in.
Ibn Ma'in said 'I do not know him' but others knew him.
2
Evaluate mutaba'ah support
Check if other narrators support the chain. The author argues Yahya's narration is a valid mutaba'ah for Hammam, so Hammam is not isolated.
Mutaba'ah means a follow-up narration from the same source.
3
Shift the burden of error upward
If the lower part of the chain is sound, the error must be from a higher narrator. Here, Ibn Jurayj is identified as the weak link.
Ibn Jurayj is a mudallis.
4
Identify tadlis signs
Ibn Jurayj concealed the intermediary (Ziyad ibn Sa'd) between him and al-Zuhri when narrating to Basrans.
Tadlis by omitting the intermediary weakens the chain.
5
Confirm with critic statements
Multiple critics (Abu Zur'a, Yahya al-Qattan, Ibn Ma'in) state Ibn Jurayj's narrations from al-Zuhri are unreliable.
This confirms the error source.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول/ الاختلاف في السند
وَلَمْ يصب البيهقي في ظنه هَذَا، فيحيى هَذَا هُوَ آخر باهلي بصري، يكنى أبا بكر، ذكره ابن حبان في ثقاته () ، قَالَ العراقي: «ولا يقدح فِيهِ قَوْل ابن معين: لا أعرفه، فَقَدْ عرفه غيره، وروى عَنْهُ نحو من عشرين نفساً»(۲).
وَقَالَ ابن حبان: «وَكَانَ راوياً لابن جريج» (۳) ، وفرّق هُوَ وابن معين بينهما (4) فمن هَذَا يظهر أن حال يحيى يصلح للمتابعة والاعتضاد، لاسيما وَقَـد نـص العلماء عَلَى عدم اشتراط أعلى مراتب الثقة في المُتابع (). أما قول ابن معين: «لا أعرفه»، فأراد بِهِ غَيْر المتبادر إلى الذهن وَهُوَ جهالة العين، فَقَدْ عنى جهالة الحال) ولذا قَالَ العراقي - كَمَا نقلناه آنفاً : «قد عرفه غيره».
وبهذا تظهر صحة متابعة يحيى بن المتوكل لهمام، وعدم صحة دعوى تفرد همام بالمتن والإسناد، فيتجه الحمل - والحالة هَذِهِ - إلى من فوقه وَهُوَ ابن جريج، وَهُوَ مدلس (۷).
والذي يبدو أن الخطأ في هَذَا الْحَدِيث من ابن جريج، ولاسيما أن ابن المتوكل وهماماً بصريان (۸) ، وَقَدْ نص العلماء عَلَى أن رِوَايَة البصريين عن ابن جريج فيها خلل من جهة ابن جريج لا من جهة أهل البصرة).
وبيانه: أن ابن جريج دلّس للبصريين الواسطة بينه وبين الزهري، وَهُوَ زياد بن سعد، وصرّح بِهِ لغيرهم كَمَا أنه - وعند تحديثه لأهل البصرة - لَمْ يَكُنْ متقناً لحفظ الْمَتْن فأخطأ فِيْهِ، لذا قَالَ النسائي عقب تخريجه: «هَذَا حَدِيث غَيْر محفوظ»). فانحصر الخطأ في تدليس ابن جريج، ولهذا نجد الحافظ ابن حجر يقول: «ولا علة لَهُ عندي إلا تدليس ابن جريج، فإن وجد عَنْهُ التصريح بالسماع فلا مانع من الحكم بصحته في نقدي). ومما يزيدنا يقيناً بكون الخطأ في هَذَا الْحَدِيث من ابن جريج: أن أكثر الحفاظ عَلَى تضعيف روايته عن الزهري مطلقاً، فَقَالَ أبو زرعة الرازي: «أخبرني بعض أصحابنا، عن قريش بن أنس (۳)، عن ابن جريج، قَالَ : ما سَمِعْتُ من الزهري شيئاً، إنما أعطاني الزهري جزءاً فكتبته وأجازه»(4). وَقَالَ يحيى بن سعيد القطان: «كَانَ ابن جريج يصحح أنه – سَمِعَ من الزهري شَيْئاً قَالَ - يعني الفلاس(۹) - فجهدت بِهِ في حَدِيث إن ناساً من اليهود غزوا مع رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فأسهم لَهُمْ، فَلَمْ يصحح أنه سَمِعَ من الزهري » ) . وَقَالَ ابن معين: «ليس بشيء في الزهري». ونقل ابن محرز عـن ابـن أنه قَالَ: «كَانَ يحيى بن سعيد لا يوثقه في الزهري ) . ومما تجدر الإشارة إِلَيْهِ أن أكثر الحفاظ يرون أن الزهري نفسه أخطأ في هَذَا الْحَدِيث، إذ خالف جمهور الرُّوَاة عن أنس في لفظ الْحَدِيث عَلَى النحو الآتي: رَوَاهُ ثابت عن أنس بن مالك: أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم صنع مالك: أن النَّبِي صنع خاتماً من ورق، فنقش فِيْهِ: مُحَمَّد رَسُول الله ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: لا تنقشوا عَلَيْهِ». الْحَدِيث أخرجه عبد الرزاق)
Chapter One: Difference in the Chain. Al-Bayhaqi was not correct in his assumption; this Yahya is another Basri Bahili, nicknamed Abu Bakr, mentioned by Ibn Hibban in his trustworthy narrators. Al-Iraqi said: 'Ibn Ma'in's statement 'I do not know him' does not harm him, for others knew him, and about twenty people narrated from him.' Ibn Hibban said: 'He was a narrator of Ibn Jurayj,' and he and Ibn Ma'in differentiated between them. From this it appears that Yahya's situation is suitable for follow-up and support, especially since the scholars have stated that the highest level of trustworthiness is not required in the follow-up transmitter. As for Ibn Ma'in's statement 'I do not know him,' he meant other than what comes to mind, which is ignorance of his identity; he meant ignorance of his condition. Hence al-Iraqi said, as we quoted earlier: 'Others knew him.' And by this the correctness of Yahya ibn al-Mutawakkil's follow-up of Hammam is established, and the claim of Hammam's singularity in the text and chain is invalid. Consequently, the burden shifts, in this case, to the one above him, namely Ibn Jurayj, who is a mudallis. It seems that the error in this hadith is from Ibn Jurayj, especially since Ibn al-Mutawakkil and Hammam are Basrans, and the scholars have stated that the narration of the Basrans from Ibn Jurayj has a defect from Ibn Jurayj's side, not from the people of Basra. Explanation: Ibn Jurayj concealed the intermediary between him and al-Zuhri, who is Ziyad ibn Sa'd, while he explicitly mentioned it for others. Moreover, when narrating to the people of Basra, he was not proficient in memorizing the text, so he erred in it. Hence al-Nasa'i said after its citation: 'This is an unmemorized hadith.' Thus the error is confined to Ibn Jurayj's tadlis. For this reason, al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar says: 'In my view there is no defect in it except Ibn Jurayj's tadlis; if explicit hearing from him is found, there is no obstacle to judging it authentic in my criticism.' What increases our certainty that the error in this hadith is from Ibn Jurayj is that most hadith masters consider his narration from al-Zuhri absolutely weak. Abu Zur'a al-Razi said: 'Some of our companions informed me, from Quryash ibn Anas, from Ibn Jurayj, who said: I did not hear anything from al-Zuhri; rather, al-Zuhri gave me a book and I wrote it and he granted it to me.' And Yahya ibn Sa'id al-Qattan said: 'Ibn Jurayj used to affirm that he heard something from al-Zuhri,' he said—meaning al-Fallas—'so I pressed him about a hadith that a group of Jews raided with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and he gave them a share, and he did not affirm that he heard from al-Zuhri.' And Ibn Ma'in said: 'He is nothing regarding al-Zuhri.' And Ibn Mahraz transmitted from Ibn Ma'in that he said: 'Yahya ibn Sa'id did not consider him trustworthy regarding al-Zuhri.' And it is noteworthy that most hadith masters believe that al-Zuhri himself erred in this hadith, as he contradicted the majority of narrators from Anas in the wording of the hadith as follows: Thabit narrated from Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet (peace be upon him) made a ring of silver, engraved on it: 'Muhammad the Messenger of Allah,' then said: 'Do not engrave on it.' The hadith was recorded by Abd al-Razzaq.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the chain of a hadith concerning the Prophet's ring. The author begins by refuting al-Bayhaqi's assumption that Yahya ibn al-Mutawakkil is unknown; he shows that Yahya is known and considered reliable by Ibn Hibban. He then argues that Yahya's narration supports the chain, so the error is not from him but from the narrator above him, Ibn Jurayj. The author points out that Ibn Jurayj is a mudallis (one who conceals gaps in the chain) and that his narrations from al-Zuhri are weak. The author concludes that the mistake originates from Ibn Jurayj's tadlis, and that many hadith critics consider Ibn Jurayj's narrations from al-Zuhri unreliable. Finally, the author mentions that some scholars even think al-Zuhri himself erred, but the main point is clear: the chain's weakness is due to Ibn Jurayj.

Key Terms
تدليس (tadlis): The act of a narrator concealing a deficiency in the chain, such as narrating from someone he did not meet or using ambiguous phrasing.
متابعة (mutaba'ah): A follow-up narration that supports a weaker narrator's version from the same source.
مدلس (mudallis): A narrator who practices tadlis, i.e., who conceals gaps in the chain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the primary cause of error in this hadith?
A) Yahya ibn al-Mutawakkil's weakness
B) Ibn Jurayj's tadlis
C) Al-Zuhri's mistake
D) Hammam's isolation

Key Takeaway
In chain analysis, an apparent unknown narrator can often be rehabilitated through mutaba'ah, shifting the error to a hidden defect like tadlis.

Differences in Sanad: The Hadith of the Ring
Listing multiple chains for the hadith of the Prophet's ring

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify variations in hadith chains (isnad) and explain how they can lead to differences in fiqh rulings according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Different chains of a hadith often introduce textual variations that require tarjih.

This passage presents three chains of the famous hadith of the Prophet's ring, transmitted from Anas ibn Malik. Each chain adds or omits details about the ring's engraving and usage. As a student of Hanafi usul, you need to recognize that such textual differences can influence the legal rulings derived from the hadith and must be resolved through rigorous chain evaluation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Common Narrator
All three chains trace back to Anas ibn Malik. Note that having a single companion as source means these are variations of the same report, not independent confirmations.
This limits the hadith to ahad status, not mutawatir.
2
List the Three Chains and Their Key Elements
Write down each chain: Qatada → Anas, Thumama → Anas, Humaid al-Tawil → Anas. For each, note the specific details mentioned (reason for ring, engraving text, material, use by Abu Bakr).
3
Compare the Matn Variations
Identify differences: Qatada mentions engraving as 'Muhammad Rasul Allah' and the Prophet's action; Thumama adds three-line engraving and Abu Bakr's use; Humaid only states the ring was silver. These variations can affect rulings on the form of engraving and hand placement.
Differences in matn are a direct result of differences in sanad.
4
Consider the Usul Implications
In Hanafi usul, when multiple ahad narrations differ, the stronger chain (by number of transmitters or reliability) is preferred. The additional details in Thumama's chain may be accepted or rejected based on tarjih.
The hadith remains zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah.
5
Apply to Fiqh Rulings
These textual variations are used as evidence for differing opinions on wearing a ring on the right vs left hand, and the permissibility of engraving. Hanafi jurists weigh the chains to determine the sunnah practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول / الاختلاف في السند
ورواه قتادة عن أنس بن مالك، قَالَ: «لما أراد النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يكتب إلى الروم، قيْلَ لَهُ: إنهم لن يقرؤا كتابك إذا لَمْ يَكُنْ مختوماً، فاتخذ خاتماً من فضة ونقشه: مُحَمَّد رَسُوْل الله، فكأنما أنظر إلى بياضه في يده». الْحَدِيث أخرجه ابن سعد، وابن الجعد، وأحمد، والبخاري، ومسلم، وأبو داود، والترمذي، والنسائي، وأبو يعلى، وأبو عوانة، والطحاوي، وابن حبان، والطبراني، وأبو الشيخ، والبيهقي، والبغوي.
ورواه ثمامة بن عَبْد الله عن أنس بن مالك: أن أبا بكر لما استخلف بعثه إلى البحرين وكتب لَهُ هَذَا الكتاب وختمه بخاتم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وَكَانَ نقش الخاتم ثلاثة أسطر: مُحَمَّد سطر، ورسول سطر، والله سطر. أخرجه ابن سعد، والبخاري، والترمذي، والطحاوي، وابن حبان، وأبو الشيخ، والبغوي.
ورواه حميد الطويل، عن أنس بن مالك: «أن النَّبِيِّ كَانَ خاتمه فضة».
Chapter One: Difference in the Chain
And Qatada narrated from Anas ibn Malik, he said: 'When the Prophet, peace be upon him, wanted to write to the Romans, it was said to him: They will not read your letter if it is not sealed. So he took a silver ring and engraved on it: Muhammad the Messenger of Allah. It is as if I am looking at its whiteness in his hand.' The hadith is reported by Ibn Sa'd, Ibn al-Ja'd, Ahmad, al-Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, Abu Ya'la, Abu Awana, al-Tahawi, Ibn Hibban, al-Tabarani, Abu al-Shaykh, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Baghawi.
And Thumama ibn 'Abd Allah narrated from Anas ibn Malik: that when Abu Bakr became caliph, he sent him to Bahrain and wrote this letter for him and sealed it with the seal of the Prophet, peace be upon him, and the engraving of the seal was three lines: Muhammad a line, Messenger a line, and Allah a line. Reported by Ibn Sa'd, al-Bukhari, al-Tirmidhi, al-Tahawi, Ibn Hibban, Abu al-Shaykh, and al-Baghawi.
And Humaid al-Tawil narrated from Anas ibn Malik: 'The Prophet's ring was of silver.'
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the hadith of the Prophet's ring, presented as the first chapter on difference in chains (isnad). The author lists multiple chains through which the hadith is transmitted from Anas ibn Malik. The first chain from Qatada includes details about the reason for taking a ring and its engraving. The second chain from Thumama adds that Abu Bakr used the same ring after the Prophet, and specifies the engraving as three lines. The third chain from Humaid al-Tawil simply states the material of the ring. These variations in isnad and matn can lead to differences in fiqh rulings, such as the permissibility of wearing a ring on the right or left hand, or the form of engraving. The author provides extensive source references for each narration, demonstrating the scholarly method of verifying hadith.

Key Terms
الاختلاف في السند (al-ikhtilaf fi al-sanad): Difference in the chain of transmission, which may lead to variations in the text (matn) and subsequently in legal rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what variation appears in the narration of Thumama compared to Qatada's narration?
A) Thumama's narration mentions the ring was made of gold.
B) Thumama's narration states that Abu Bakr used the same ring and describes the engraving as three lines.
C) Thumama's narration says the Prophet never wore a ring.
D) Thumama's narration says the ring was lost in the well of Aris.

Key Takeaway
Differences in hadith chains (isnad) can introduce variations in the text (matn), and Hanafi usul weighs these chains through tarjih to determine the stronger evidence.

Analyzing Differences in Hadith Chains: The Ring of the Prophet
Listing multiple chains for the ring hadith from Anas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify variations in hadith chains from the same companion and explain how these differences affect the textual content and reliability.

Core Idea
Multiple chains from a single companion can yield different details — careful evaluation of each chain is essential.

Hadiths often reach us through multiple chains from the same companion. This passage presents several narrations from Anas ibn Malik about the Prophet's ring. Each chain adds or omits specific details, and one chain is disputed. Understanding these differences is crucial for a correct fiqh understanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify each chain and its unique detail
List each narrator chain (Thumama, Humaid, Aban, al-Zuhri) and note the specific detail each one provides about the Prophet's ring.
Thumama: engraving; Humaid: material and stone; Aban: prohibition; al-Zuhri: incident with gold ring.
2
Compare the chains for consistency
Check which details are consistent across chains (e.g., ring of silver) and which are unique or contradictory.
All mention silver except al-Zuhri's (iron). None mention discarding the ring except al-Zuhri's disputed version.
3
Evaluate the strength and issues of each chain
Assess the reliability of narrators and any criticisms (e.g., Abu Hatim's correction of al-Zuhri's chain).
The al-Zuhri chain has an error according to Abu Hatim; the correct chain goes through Abu Idris.
4
Determine the impact on the overall hadith understanding
Decide which details are most reliable and how the differences might affect fiqh rulings (e.g., permissibility of gold rings, engraving).
The majority of sound chains support the ring being silver and not discarded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورواه ثمامة بن عبد الله عن أنس بن مالك: أن أبا بكر رضي الله عنه لما استخلف بعثه إلى البحرين وكتب له هذا الكتاب وختمه بخاتم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وكان نقش الخاتم ثلاثة أسطر: محمد سطر، ورسول سطر، والله سطر. أخرجه ابن سعد والبخاري والترمذي والطحاوي وابن حبان وأبو الشيخ والبغوي. ورواه حميد الطويل عن أنس بن مالك: أن النبي كان خاتمه فضة وكان فصه منه. أخرجه ابن سعد والحميدي وأحمد والبخاري وأبو داود والترمذي والنسائي وأبو يعلى وابن حبان وأبو الشيخ والبغوي. ورواه أبان بن أبي عياش عن أنس بن مالك: أن رسول الله اصطنع خاتماً كله من فضة وقال: لا يصنع أحد على صفته. أخرجه ابن سعد. فكل هذه الروايات عن أنس ليس فيها: أن رسول الله طرح خاتم الورق. أما رواية الزهري عن أنس فاختلف عليه، إذ رواه إبراهيم بن سعد عن الزهري عن أنس: أن النبي رأى في يد رجل خاتم ذهب فضرب إصبعه بقضيب كان معه حتى رمى به. قال أبو حاتم في العلل: هكذا رواه إبراهيم بن سعد عن الزهري عن أنس، والخطأ من عبد العزيز أبي سلمة العمري، والصحيح من حديث الزهري عن أبي إدريس عن رجل من أصحاب النبي. وذكر في العلل لابن أبي حاتم: إن الخاتم كان حديداً. أقول: الرواية التي ذكرها أبو حاتم هي عند النسائي (٩٥٠٥).
And Thumama ibn Abdullah narrated from Anas ibn Malik: that when Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, became caliph, he sent him to Bahrain and wrote this document for him and sealed it with the seal of the Prophet, peace be upon him, and the engraving of the seal was three lines: Muhammad a line, Messenger a line, Allah a line. Recorded by Ibn Sa'd, al-Bukhari, al-Tirmidhi, al-Tahawi, Ibn Hibban, Abu al-Shaykh, and al-Baghawi. And Humaid al-Tawil narrated from Anas ibn Malik: that the Prophet's seal was of silver and its stone was from it. Recorded by Ibn Sa'd, al-Humaydi, Ahmad, al-Bukhari, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, Abu Ya'la, Ibn Hibban, Abu al-Shaykh, and al-Baghawi. And Aban ibn Abi Ayyash narrated from Anas ibn Malik: that the Messenger of Allah made a ring entirely of silver and said: 'Let no one make one like it.' Recorded by Ibn Sa'd. All these narrations from Anas do not contain that the Messenger of Allah threw away the silver ring. As for the narration of al-Zuhri from Anas, there is disagreement on it: Ibrahim ibn Sa'd narrated from al-Zuhri from Anas: that the Prophet saw a gold ring on a man's hand and struck his finger with a stick he had until he threw it away. Abu Hatim said in al-'Ilal: thus narrated Ibrahim ibn Sa'd from al-Zuhri from Anas, and the error is from Abd al-Aziz Abi Salama al-Amari, and the correct version is from al-Zuhri from Abu Idris from a man from the Prophet's companions. And in al-'Ilal by Ibn Abi Hatim it is mentioned that the ring was of iron. I say: the narration that Abu Hatim mentioned is found in al-Nasa'i (9505).
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of different chains (asanid) for the hadith of the Prophet's ring narrated by Anas ibn Malik. The author lists three distinct chains: from Thumama, from Humaid, and from Aban. Each chain adds different details: Thumama's version focuses on the ring's engraving (three lines: Muhammad, Messenger, Allah), Humaid's mentions it was silver with a stone of the same material, and Aban's says it was entirely silver and the Prophet forbade making an identical one. The author notes that none of these include the Prophet discarding the silver ring, which is a point of contention. Then he examines the narration of al-Zuhri from Anas, which has a variation: Ibrahim ibn Sa'd narrates that the Prophet struck a man's hand to remove a gold ring, but Abu Hatim criticizes this, saying the correct chain is al-Zuhri from Abu Idris from an unnamed companion, and the ring was iron. This shows how differences in chains affect the text and can lead to different fiqh rulings—e.g., on the material of the ring and whether it was discarded.

Key Terms
سند (sanad): The chain of narrators transmitting a hadith
رواية (riwaya): A particular narration or version of a hadith with its chain

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which narration states that the ring's engraving was in three lines?
A) Thumama's narration
B) Humaid's narration
C) Aban's narration
D) Al-Zuhri's narration

Key Takeaway
Different chains from a single companion can provide different details; careful analysis of asanid is essential for accurate hadith understanding.

Analyzing the Hadith of the Ring: Chain Variations and Hanafi Ruling
Textual analysis of hadith chain variation and fiqh derivation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify chain variations in a hadith and apply the Hanafi principle that an ahad hadith provides zanni proof for permissibility.

Core Idea
A hadith with chain variations remains valid proof; ahad hadith suffices for permissibility.

This passage examines how different narrations of the same hadith—the Prophet wearing a silver ring—are reconciled by scholars, and then extracts the fiqh ruling on silver rings for men. As a usul exercise, we will analyze the hadith's chain classification and the Hanafi method of deriving permission from a zanni text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core hadith and its chain
Extract the main narration: al-Zuhri from Anas that the Prophet wore a silver ring on his right hand. Note the chain and the alternate narration by al-Layth.
The core text is ahad, though narrated through multiple chains.
2
Identify the chain variation and reconciliations
Some narrations mention the Prophet throwing a ring. Ibn Hajar collects four reconciliations. List them briefly: (1) al-Ismaili's, (2) adornment then sealing, (3) gold replaced with silver, (4) Ibn Hajar's own elaborate sequence.
Reconciliations show that the apparent contradiction does not weaken the hadith's proof.
3
Classify the hadith in Hanafi usul
Determine its textual category: it is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and its meaning is clear (zahir). In Hanafi usul, ahad hadith can establish a ruling that is not fard (obligatory) but permissible or recommended.
Zanni thubut does not prevent using it as evidence for non-obligatory rulings.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle of permissibility
The Hanafi principle 'al-asl fi al-ashya' al-ibaha' (the default is permissibility) combined with the Prophet's practice indicates that wearing a silver ring is permissible. The hadith is not abrogated by other texts.
The Hanafi position distinguishes between wearing for need versus arrogance.
5
Derive the ruling with conditions
From the hadith and reconciliations, derive the mufta bihi: wearing a silver ring is permitted; disliked only if intended for arrogance; better if under one mithqal.
This ruling contrasts with some Shafi'i views that restrict quantity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول/ الاختلاف في السند

كَانَ

نقل كلامه المباركفوري في تحفة الأحوذي ٤٨٤/٥.
(٦) تحفة الأحوذي ٤٨٤/٥
Chapter One: Disagreement in the Chain(87) It was: al-Zuhri from Anas: 'The Messenger of God wore a silver ring on his right hand, with an Abyssinian stone, placing its stone towards his palm.' While al-Layth alone from Yunus from al-Zuhri from Anas narrated it similarly to the narration of Ibrahim ibn Sa'd and those who followed him. (3) Ibn Hajar collected some scholars' statements in reconciling the two narrations: First: al-Ismaili said: The Messenger of God took a ring of silver in some color and disliked that anyone took one like it. When they took a similar one, he threw it away. Then after they threw their rings, he took another ring and engraved it to seal with it. Second: He took the ring for adornment, then when people followed him in that, he threw it and they threw their rings after that. Then when he needed a seal, he took another ring. Third: The saying of al-Muhallab, al-Nawawi, and al-Kirmani: That when he threw the gold ring, he took a silver ring in its place because he could not do without a seal for his letters. So the throwing of the ring in al-Zuhri's narration refers to the gold ring, making the described - i.e., the gold ring in his statement 'He threw his ring so they threw their rings.' Al-Qadi Iyad said: 'This would be acceptable if the wording came as a whole,' and indicated that al-Zuhri's narration does not bear this interpretation. Ibn Hajar went for a fourth interpretation: That he took a gold ring for adornment, and people followed him in it, then its prohibition occurred so he threw it and said, 'I will never wear it,' so people threw their rings following him. Then he needed a ring for sealing, so he took one of silver and engraved his noble name on it, and people also followed him in those engraved rings. He threw it until people threw those engraved rings so that the benefit of engraving his name would not be lost due to confusion. When all their rings were gone, he returned to his own ring and began wearing it. Effect of the Hadith on Juristic Disagreement: Ruling on Men Wearing a Silver Ring: The jurists differed on the ruling of wearing a silver ring for men as follows: 1. The majority of scholars, early and late, allowed taking a silver ring, whether a ruler or otherwise. The Shafi'is hold this view (majority). 2. The Hanafis held that if one intends by wearing it arrogance and haughtiness, it is disliked; if not, it is not disliked. Nevertheless, leaving it for one who does not need a seal is better. They see no dislike in wearing it for adornment if free from harm. It is better for the ring to be less than one mithqal because it is further from extravagance. Ibn al-Malik said this. 3. Some Shafi'is held that wearing a silver ring is prohibited for a man if it exceeds one mithqal. And dislike of wearing a silver ring for every legally responsible person, ruler or otherwise, was reported by Ibn Abd al-Barr from ...
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of a hadith about the Prophet's ring, followed by a derived fiqh ruling. It first presents the core hadith narration through al-Zuhri from Anas describing the Prophet wearing a silver ring with an Abyssinian stone on his right hand. Then it notes a chain variation where al-Layth alone narrates similarly. The main issue is reconciling narrations that mention the Prophet throwing away a ring, with those that show him wearing a silver ring. The author, through Ibn Hajar, summarizes three earlier reconciliations: (1) al-Ismaili's view that the Prophet took a silver ring, disliked imitation, threw it, then took another for sealing; (2) that he took it for adornment, threw it when people imitated, then took another for sealing; (3) al-Muhallab, al-Nawawi, and al-Kirmani's view that the thrown ring was gold, replaced with silver. Al-Qadi Iyad criticizes this as requiring the narration to be taken as a whole. Ibn Hajar adds a fourth: the Prophet initially wore gold, then after prohibition threw it, later took silver for sealing, and eventually even that was thrown to avoid confusion, before finally returning to his own ring. The fiqh section then lists opinions: the majority (including Shafi'is) permit silver rings; Hanafis allow with conditions—disliked if for arrogance, not disliked for adornment if free from harm, and better less than one mithqal; some Shafi'is prohibit if over one mithqal; and there is a view of general dislike.

Key Terms
خاتم (khatam): A ring worn on the finger, often used for sealing or adornment.
فضة (fidda): Silver metal, used for rings and other items.
كراهة (karaha): Dislike, a legal category between permissible and prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi usul, what is the classification of the hadith 'the Prophet wore a silver ring' as narrated by al-Zuhri from Anas?
A) Mutawatir, because it is narrated by multiple chains.
B) Ahad, because it does not reach the level of tawatur.
C) Mursal, because the chain has a missing link.
D) Mawquf, because it is a saying of a companion.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of the Prophet's silver ring, despite chain variations and reconciliations, provides valid ahad evidence for the Hanafi ruling that wearing a silver ring is permissible for men, with conditions.

Definition of Tafarrud (Solitary Narration) in Language and Terminology
Linguistic and technical definition of tafarrud in hadith terminology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and technical definitions of tafarrud and distinguish it from related hadith concepts.

Core Idea
Tafarrud means a trustworthy narrator being the sole reporter from his sheikh — not automatically weak, but subject to scrutiny.

This lesson introduces the concept of tafarrud (solitary narration) in both language and hadith terminology. You will learn its linguistic root, the technical definition given by hadith scholars, and how this classification affects the acceptance of narrations in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic root
Recognize that tafarrud derives from the root f-r-d, indicating oneness and singularity. Note the verb forms and Ibn Faris's comment.
The root appears in words like fard (odd number) and farid (solitary).
2
State the technical definition
Recall Abu Hafs al-Mayanashi's definition: a hadith that some trustworthy narrators are alone in narrating from their sheikh.
The key elements: solitary narrator (thiqah), from his sheikh.
3
Identify conditions and preventers
The condition for calling it tafarrud is that no other narrator reports from that sheikh. A preventer: if others also report from the same sheikh, it is not tafarrud.
The narrator must be trustworthy; otherwise it's shadhdh, not fard.
4
Understand the legal effect
In Hanafi usul, a solitary narration (khabar al-wahid) is zanni in thubut, but if the narrator is trustworthy and other conditions met, it is accepted as proof.
Tafarrud alone does not imply weakness; additional scrutiny applies.
5
Connect to broader usul
Recognize that tafarrud is one factor in evaluating hadith. Hanafi scholars differentiate between fard mutlaq and fard nisbi, but this lesson focuses on the basic definition.
This sets the stage for understanding ikhtilaf arising from differing transmissions.

Source Text

المبحث الثاني
أثر التَّفَرَّد في اختلاف الحديث، وأثر ذلك في اختلاف الفقهاء
التَّفَرُّدُ في اللغة:
مأخوذ من الفعل الثلاثي المزيد بحرفين (تَفَرَّدَ). يقال: فَرَدَ بالأمر والرأي انْفَرَدَ وفَرَدَ الرجلُ : كَانَ وحده مُنْفَرِداً لا ثاني مَعَهُ.
وَفَرَّدَ برأيه : اسْتَبَدَّ.
وَقَدْ أشار ابن فارس) إلى أن جميع تراكيب واشتقاقات هَذَا الأصل تدل عَلَى الوحدة . إِذْ قَالَ: «الفاء والراء والدال أصل صَحِيح يدل عَلَى وحدة. من ذَلِكَ: الفرد وَهُوَ الوتر، والفارد والفرد: الثور المنفرد ...»( ).
التفرد في الاصطلاح
عرفه أبو حفص الميانشي (٦) الفرد بأنه: ما انفرد بروايته بعض الثقات عن شيخه
Second Section: The Effect of Tafarrud (Solitary Narration) on Hadith Disagreement and Its Effect on Juristic Disagreement. Tafarrud in Language: It is derived from the triliteral verb with two additional letters (tafarrada). It is said: 'farada bil-amri war-ra'y' he was alone; 'farada ar-rajulu' he was alone, with no second. 'Farrada bira'yihi' he was independent. Ibn Faris indicated that all constructions and derivations of this root indicate oneness. He said: 'The letters fa, ra, dal are a sound root indicating oneness. Examples: al-fard (the odd number), al-farid and al-fard (the solitary bull).' Tafarrud in Terminology: Abu Hafs al-Mayanashi defined al-fard as: what some trustworthy narrators are alone in narrating from their sheikh.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a definition of tafarrud (solitary narration) in both linguistic and technical senses. Linguistically, tafarrud derives from the root f-r-d, which connotes oneness, singularity, and being alone. This is supported by the lexicographer Ibn Faris. In hadith terminology, the definition given by Abu Hafs al-Mayanashi is that a hadith is considered 'fard' (singular) when only one trustworthy narrator reports it from his teacher, even if other narrators also report it from other teachers. This concept is important in usul because a solitary narration (khabar al-wahid) carries different evidentiary weight than mutawatir. The passage sets the stage for discussing how tafarrud can lead to juristic disagreement, since if a hadith is only transmitted through a single chain, scholars may differ on its authenticity and interpretation.

Key Terms
التفرد (al-tafarrud): A narrator being alone in reporting a hadith from his sheikh
الفرد (al-fard): The hadith that a narrator is alone in transmitting from his sheikh

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In hadith terminology, what does tafarrud refer to?
A) A hadith with many chains of transmission
B) A narrator being alone in reporting from a particular sheikh
C) A weak hadith that contradicts stronger narrations
D) A hadith that has been abrogated

Key Takeaway
Tafarrud alone does not weaken a hadith; it only indicates limited transmission, and the Hanafi school accepts such narrations if the narrator is trustworthy and other conditions are met.

Tafarud in Hadith Criticism: Definition and Ruling
Defines tafarud and discusses its impact on hadith authenticity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tafarud (singular narration) and explain why it is not an automatic defect in Hanafi usul, citing the conditions that determine its acceptability.

Core Idea
Tafarud does not automatically weaken a hadith; it depends on the narrator's reliability and context.

In Hanafi usul, the acceptance of a hadith as evidence often hinges on the reliability of its narrators. A common concern is tafarud—when a hadith is narrated by only one person from a particular source. This passage from a classical work on hadith criticism clarifies that tafarud is not inherently a defect but a clue that requires scrutiny. By understanding the nuances of tafarud, you will be better equipped to evaluate the strength of singular narrations in legal derivation.

Guided Path
1
Define tafarud linguistically and terminologically
Examine the Arabic root f-r-d (alone) and note the two definitions given: one restricts tafarud to trustworthy narrators (by al-Miyanashi), while a broader definition (by Dr. Hamza al-Malibari) includes any narrator who narrates singly. The passage prefers the broader definition, as critics use it for both reliable and weak narrators.
The broader definition aligns with the linguistic sense of 'being alone'.
2
Distinguish the two definitions and their implications
Identify why al-Miyanashi restricted the definition (because weak narrators' solitary narrations are ignored if unsupported), but note that from a theoretical perspective, critics apply tafarud regardless of the narrator's reliability.
The chosen definition affects how tafarud is applied in hadith criticism.
3
Understand the ruling: tafarud is not an inherent defect
From the passage, extract the central ruling: 'al-tafarud laysa bi-illah fi kulli ahwalihi' (tafarud is not a defect in all its circumstances). It is a 'kashif' (revealer) of a potential defect, like a fever indicates illness. Support this with quotes from Ibn Rajab, Muslim, Ibn Hajar, and al-Zayla'i.
The permissibility of tafarud depends on the narrator's memory, reliability, and context.
4
Identify when tafarud is harmful and when it is not
Using Ibn Rajab's and al-Mu'allimi's conditions: tafarud harms when the narrator is not a reliable memorizer (like al-Zuhri), or when the narrator has many strange narrations from trustworthy sources without being known for extensive seeking of hadith. Conversely, trustworthy memorizers like al-Zuhri are not harmed by tafarud.
This nuance is critical for usul al-fiqh: Hanafis accept khabar al-wahid from reliable narrators even if they are alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول الاختلاف في السند
دون سائر الرُّوَاة عن ذَلِكَ الشيخ). ويظهر من هَذَا التعريف بعض القصور في دخول بعض أفراد المُعَرَّف في حقيقة التعريف، إِذْ قَصَرَه عَلَى انفراد الثقة فَقَطْ شیخه (۲). عن
وعرّف الدكتور حمزة المليباري التفرد وبيّن كيفية حصوله، فَقَالَ: «يراد بالتفرد:
أن يروي شخص من الرُّوَاة حديثاً دون أن يشاركه الآخرون»(۳).
وهذا التعريف الأخير أعم من التعريف الأول، فإنه شامل لتفرد الثقة وغيره، وعليه تدل تصرفات نقاد الْمُحَدِّثِينَ وجهابذة الناقلين، ولقد كثر في تعبيراتهم: حَدِيث غريب، أو تفرّد بهِ فُلان، أو هَذَا حَدِيث لا يعرف إلا من هَذَا الوجه، أو لا نعلمه يروى عن فُلان إلا من حَدِيث فُلان، ونحوها من التعبيرات(4).
ولربما كَانَ الحامل للميانشي عَلَى تخصيص التعريف بالثقات دون غيرهم، أن رِوَايَة الضعيف لا اعتداد بِهَا عِنْدَ عدم المتابع والعاضد ولكن من الناحية التنظيرية نجد الْمُحَدِّثِيْنَ عِنْدَ تشخيصهم لحالة التفرد لا يفرقون بَيْنَ كون المتفرد ثقة أو ضعيفاً،
فيقولون مثلاً: تفرد به الزهري كَمَا يقولون: تفرد به ابن أبي أويس (9) . وبهذا المعنى يظهر الترابط الواضح بَيْنَ المعنى اللغوي والمعنى الاصطلاحي، إِذْ
إنهما يدوران في حلقة التفرد عما يماثله. والتفرد ليس بعلة في كُلّ أحواله، ولكنه كاشف عن العلة مرشد إلى وجودها، وفي هَذَا يقول الحافظ ابن رجب الحنبلي: (وأما أكثر الحفاظ المتقدمين فإنهم يقولون في الْحَدِيْث إذا تفرد بِهِ واحد - وإن لَم يرو الثقات خلافه -: إنه لا يتابع عليه. ويجعلون ذَلِكَ علة فِيْهِ، اللهم إلا أن يَكُون ممن كثر حفظه واشتهرت عدالته وحديثه كالزهري ونحوه، وربما يستنكرون بعض تفردات الثقات الكبار أيضاً ولهم في كُلِّ حَدِيث نقد خاص، وليس عندهم لِذلِكَ ضابط يضبطه»(۱).
ومعنى قوله : ويجعلون ذَلِكَ علة»، أن ذَلِكَ مخصوص بتفرد من لا يحتمل تفرده، بقرينة قوله: «إلا أن يَكُون ممن كثر حفظه ... فتفرده هُوَ خطؤه، إِذْ هُوَ مظنة عدم الضبط ودخول الأوهام، فانفراده دال عَلَى وجود خلل ما في حديثه، كما أن الحمّى دالة عَلَى وجود مرض ما، وقد وجدنا غير واحد من النقاد بأن تفرد فُلان صرح لا يضر ، فَقَدْ قَالَ الإمام مُسْلِم: «هَذَا الحرف لا يرويه غَيْر الزهري، قال: وللزهري نحو من تسعين حديثاً يرويها عن النبي له لا يشاركه فيها أحد بأسانيد جياد»(۲). وَقَالَ الحافظ ابن حجر: وكم من ثقة تفرد بما لم يشاركه فِيْهِ ثقة آخر، وإذا كَانَ الثقة حافظاً لم يضره الانفراد»(۳). وَقَالَ الزيلعي): «وانفراد الثقة بالحديث لا يضره»). وتأسيساً عَلَى ما أصلناه من قبل من أن تفرد الرَّاوِي لا يضر في كُلّ حال، ولكنه الناقد عَلَى أمر ما، قَالَ المعلمي اليماني: وكثرة الغرائب إنما تضر الرَّاوِي في أحد حالين: الأولى: أن تكون مع غرابتها منكرة عن شيوخ ثقات بأسانيد جيدة. الثانية: أن يَكُون مع كثرة غرائبه غَيْر معروف بكثرة الطلب).
وتمتع هذا الجانب من النقد الحديثي باهتمام النقاد، فنراهم يديمون تتبع هذه الحالة وتقريرها، وأفردوا من أجل ذَلِكَ المصنفات، مِنْهَا: كتاب " التفرد ) للإمام أبي داود، و" الغرائب والأفراد (1) للدارقطني، و" المفاريد (9) لأبي يعلى، واهتم الإمام
Chapter One: Disagreement in the Chain. ... (defining tafarud) ... And tafarud is not a defect in all its circumstances, but it is a revealer of the defect, guiding to its existence. ... And the meaning of his statement 'and they make that a defect' is that it is specific to the tafarud of one whose tafarud is not acceptable, by the context of his statement 'except if he is one whose memory is abundant and whose reliability and hadith are famous, like al-Zuhri and the like.' ... And some critics explicitly stated that the tafarud of so-and-so does not harm, for Imam Muslim said: 'This word is not narrated by other than al-Zuhri...' And al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: 'How many a trustworthy narrator narrated singly what no other trustworthy narrator shared with him, and if the trustworthy narrator is a memorizer, his tafarud does not harm him.' ...
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the concept of tafarud (singular narration) in hadith criticism, which is a key topic in the study of chain differences. The author begins by presenting different definitions of tafarud: one restricts it to trustworthy narrators, while a more comprehensive definition includes any narrator who narrates alone, regardless of reliability. The author sides with the latter, noting that hadith critics use the term for both reliable and weak narrators. The central ruling discussed is that tafarud is not an inherent defect; rather, it serves as a clue to potential defects. The author supports this with statements from major scholars: Ibn Rajab distinguishes between narrators who are widely accepted like al-Zuhri and others whose tafarud is considered a problem. Muslim and Ibn Hajar explicitly state that tafarud does not harm the hadith if the narrator is reliable. Al-Zayla'i and others concur. The passage also mentions conditions under which numerous strange narrations can harm a narrator, as explained by al-Mu'allimi al-Yamani. Finally, it lists specialized works on tafarud and gharib hadith. From a Hanafi usul perspective, this discussion reinforces that a singular narration can be accepted as evidence if the narrator is trustworthy and competent, aligning with the Hanafi principle of accepting khabar al-wahid from reliable sources.

Key Terms
التفرد (al-tafarud): That a narrator narrates a hadith alone without others sharing in that narration from the same source.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following best describes the ruling on tafarud?
A) Tafarud always makes a hadith weak and unacceptable.
B) Tafarud is never a problem and all singular narrations are accepted.
C) Tafarud is not an automatic defect but may indicate a problem depending on the narrator's stature and context.
D) Only tafarud by a weak narrator is considered a defect.

Key Takeaway
Tafarud is a clue, not a defect; its impact on a hadith's authenticity depends on the narrator's reliability and memory.

Al-Sunnah as Source

Tafarruḍ and Its Role in Accepting or Rejecting Narrations
Explaining tafarruḍ and its nuanced evaluation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that tafarruḍ alone does not determine acceptance or rejection, and evaluate a narration's reliability using qara'in.

Core Idea
Tafarruḍ alone does not reject or accept; qara'in decide the fate of a unique narration.

In this passage, the author explains that a narrator's uniqueness (tafarruḍ) is not a sufficient criterion for accepting or rejecting a hadith. Both weak and trustworthy narrators' unique reports require evaluation through indications (qara'in) and weightings (tarjih). This nuanced approach is essential for usul al-fiqh because the validity of a legal ruling often depends on the strength of its supporting hadith. We will walk through the key concepts and see how early scholars applied this principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim about tafarruḍ
Read the opening statements: tafarruḍ by itself is not a valid criterion for rejection. Note that even for weak narrators, their unique narrations are not absolutely rejected. Critics select reliable ones using qara'in.
Focus on the phrase 'التفرد بحد ذاته لا يصلح ضابطاً'.
2
Analyze the applied examples
Examine the quotations from Sufyan al-Thawri, Imam Ahmad, and Abu Dawud. Each shows a different aspect: al-Thawri's discernment of truth from lie in a weak narrator (al-Kalbi); Ahmad's warning about labels like 'ghareeb'; Abu Dawud's statement that ghareeb hadiths are not evidence.
Notice the practical interplay between tafarruḍ and qara'in.
3
Distinguish between early and later layers
The passage divides tafarruḍ by sanad position: early layers (Sahabah, senior Tabi'un) and later layers. Early layer tafarruḍ is common and acceptable if the narrator is trustworthy; later layer tafarruḍ raises suspicion.
Reason: limited travel and exchange in early times.
4
Understand the role of qara'in (indications)
Qara'in include the presence of mutabi' and shahid, conformity to established narrations, and the narrator's overall reliability. The term 'selecting' (انتقاء) is key: critics pick what they know to be correct.
This shows that reliability is not binary but graded.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider the hadith of Salat al-Tasbih. Even though the chain approximates hasan, it is declared shadhdh due to extreme individuality without mutabi' or shahid. This illustrates how extreme tafarruḍ, combined with lack of corroboration, leads to rejection despite apparent trustworthiness.
Apply the principles from this lesson to explain why.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول / الاختلاف في السند
الحفظ،
الطبراني في معجميه الأوسط والصغير بذكر الأفراد، وكذا فعل البزار في مسنده، والعقيلي في ضعفائه. وَهُوَ ليس بالعلم الهين، فهو يحتاج لاتساع الباع في وكثيراً ما يدعي الحافظ التفرد بحسب علمه، ويطلع غيره على المتابع». وفي كُلّ الأحوال فإن التفرد بحد ذاته لا يصلح ضابطاً لرد الروايات، حَتَّى في حالة تفرد الضعيف لا يحكم على جميع ما تفرد به بالرد المطلق، بل إن النقاد يستخرجون من أفراده ما يعلمون بالقرائن والمرجحات عدم خطئه فِيْهِ، وَهُوَ ما نسميه بعملية الانتقاء، قَالَ سفيان الثوري: «اتقوا الكلبي، فقيل لَهُ: إنك تروي عَنْهُ، قَالَ: إِني أعلم صدقه من كذبه». و مثلما أن تفرد الضعيف لا يرد مطلقاً، فكذلك تفرد الثقة – وكما سبق في كلام ابن رجب - لا يقبل عَلَى الإطلاق، وإنما القبول والرد موقوف على القرائن والمرجحات. قَالَ الإمام أحمد : «إذا سَمِعْتَ أصحاب الْحَدِيث يقولون: هَذَا حَدِيْثِ غريب أو فائدة. فاعلم أنه خطأ أو دخل حَدِيث في حَدِيث أَوْ خطأ من المُحدّث أَوْ حَدِيث ليس لَهُ إسناد، وإن كَانَ قَدْ رَوَى شعبة وسفيان، فإذا سمعتهم يقولون: هَذَا لا شيء، فاعلم أنه حَدِيث صَحِيح).
وَقَالَ أبو داود: «والأحاديث التي وضعتها في كتاب " السنن " أكثرها مشاهير، وَهُوَ عِنْدَ كُلّ من كتب شَيْئاً من الْحَدِيث، إلا أن تمييزها لا يقدر عَلَيْهِ كُلّ الناس والفخر بِهَا: بأنها مشاهير، فإنه لا يحتج بحديث غريب، وَلَوْ كَانَ من رِوَايَة مالك ويحيى بن سعيد والثقات من أئمة العلم».
ونحن نجد أمثلة تطبيقية متعددة في ممارسة النقاد مِنْهَا قَوْل الحافظ ابن حجر في حَدِيث صلاة التسبيح: وإن كَانَ سند ابن عَبَّاس يقرب من شرط الحسن إلا أنه شاذ لشدة الفردية وعدم المتابع والشاهد من وجه معتبر). ويمكننا أن نقسم التفرد - حسب موقعه في السند – إلى قسمين:
الأول: تفرد في الطبقات المتقدمة:
كطبقة الصَّحَابَة، وطبقة كبار التَّابِعِيْنَ، وهذا التفرد مقبول إذا كَانَ راويه ثقة - وهذا الاحتراز فيما يخص طبقة التَّابِعِينَ -- فهو أمر وارد جداً لأسباب متعددة يمكن حصرها في عدم توفر فرص متعددة تمكّن الْمُحَدِّثِينَ من التلاقي وتبادل المرويات، وذلك لصعوبة التنقل في البلدان، لا سيما في هذين العصرين.
فوقوعه فيهما لا يولد عِنْدَ الناقد استفهاماً عن كيفيته، ولاسيما أن تداخل الأحاديث فيما بينها شيء لا يكاد يذكر، نظراً لقلة الأسانيد زيادة على قصرها. هَذَا فِيْمَا إذا لَمْ يخالف الثابت المشهور، أو من هُوَ أولى مِنْهُ حفظاً أَوْ عدداً.
الرد (٢).
وإن كَانَ المتفرد ضعيفاً أو مجهولاً - فيما يخص التَّابِعِيْنَ- فحكمه بين وَهُوَ
الثاني: التفرد في الطبقات المتأخرة
فبعد أن نشط الناس لطلب العلم وأداموا الرحلة فيه والتبحر في فنونه، ظهرت مناهج متعددة في الطلب والموقف مِنْهُ، فكانت الغرس الأول للمدارس الحديثية التي نشأت فِيْمَا بَعْد، فكان لها جهدها العظيم في لَم شتات المرويات وجمعها، والحرص عَلَى تلقيها من مصادرها الأصيلة، فوفرت لهم الرحلات المتعددة فرصة لقاء المشايخ والرواة وتبادل المرويات، فإذا انفرد من هَذِهِ الطبقات أحدٍ بشيء ما فإن ذَلِكَ أمر يوقع الريبة عند الناقد، لا سيما إذا تفرد عمن يجمع حديثه أو يكثر أصحابه، كالزهــري ومالك وشعبة وسفيان وغيرهم). إن العلماء قسموا الأفراد من حَيْثُ التقييد وعدمه إلى قسمين:
الأول: الفرد المطلق وَهُوَ ما ينفرد بِهِ الرَّاوِي عن أحد الرُّوَاة).
Chapter One: Difference in Sanad. ... The Tabarani in his two Mu'jams al-Awsat and al-Sagheer mentions individuals, and likewise al-Bazzar in his Musnad, and al-Uqayli in his Du'afa. And it is not an easy science, as it requires vast knowledge. Often a memorizer claims uniqueness based on his knowledge, while others find a follow-up. In all cases, tafarruḍ by itself is not a valid criterion for rejecting narrations, even in the case of a weak narrator's tafarruḍ – one does not absolutely reject all his unique narrations. Rather, critics extract from his individuals what they know through indications and weightings that he did not err in it, which we call the process of selection. Sufyan al-Thawri said: 'Beware of al-Kalbi.' It was said to him: 'You narrate from him.' He said: 'I know his truthfulness from his lie.' And just as a weak narrator's tafarruḍ is not absolutely rejected, similarly the tafarruḍ of a trustworthy narrator – as mentioned in Ibn Rajab's statement – is not absolutely accepted. Rather, acceptance and rejection depend on indications and weightings. Imam Ahmad said: 'When you hear hadith scholars say: This hadith is ghareeb or fa'idah, know that it is a mistake, or a hadith mixed into another, or a mistake from the narrator, or a hadith with no chain, even if Shu'bah and Sufyan narrated it. And when you hear them say: This is nothing, know that it is a sound hadith.' Abu Dawood said: 'The hadiths I placed in my Sunan are mostly well-known and present with everyone who wrote something of hadith, but not all people can distinguish them. The pride in them being well-known is that a ghareeb hadith is not used as evidence, even if it is from the narration of Malik, Yahya ibn Sa'id, and other trustworthy imams.' We find multiple practical examples in the practice of critics, including the statement of Ibn Hajar regarding the hadith of Salat al-Tasbih: 'Even if the chain of Ibn Abbas approximates the condition of hasan, it is shadhdh due to its extreme individuality and lack of a follow-up or supporting witness from a reliable source.' We can divide tafarruḍ – according to its position in the chain – into two types: First: Tafarruḍ in the early layers: such as the layer of the Companions and the layer of the senior Tabi'un. This tafarruḍ is acceptable if its narrator is trustworthy – this caution concerns the Tabi'un layer – for it is very common due to multiple reasons that can be summarized as the lack of multiple opportunities enabling hadith scholars to meet and exchange narrations, due to the difficulty of traveling between lands, especially in these two eras. Its occurrence in them does not generate doubt in the critic about its quality, especially since mixing of hadiths is negligible due to the small number and shortness of chains. This is when it does not contradict the established well-known [narration] or one who is more reliable in memory or number. The rejection. But if the individual narrator is weak or unknown – concerning the Tabi'un – then its ruling is between... Second: Tafarruḍ in the later layers: After people became active in seeking knowledge, traveling extensively and delving into its branches, multiple methodologies emerged in seeking and positioning towards it. They were the early seeds of the hadith schools that later developed, and they made great efforts to gather scattered narrations and collect them, and were keen to receive them from their original sources. The multiple travels provided them with the opportunity to meet shaykhs and narrators and exchange narrations. So if anyone from these layers stands alone with something, that raises suspicion in the critic, especially if he is unique from someone whose hadith is collected or who has many companions, such as al-Zuhri, Malik, Shu'bah, Sufyan, and others. The scholars divided afrad (singular narrations) from the perspective of restriction and its absence into two types: First: al-fard al-mutlaq (absolute individual), which is what the narrator is alone in narrating from one of the narrators.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage discusses the concept of tafarruḍ (individual narration) in hadith criticism and its role in accepting or rejecting narrations. The author begins by stating that tafarruḍ alone is not a valid criterion for rejection, even for weak narrators. Critics select from weak narrators' unique narrations those they know through qara'in (indications) and tarjih (weightings) are not erroneous. Sufyan al-Thawri's example with al-Kalbi illustrates that a weak narrator's tafarruḍ can sometimes be accepted if the critic knows his truthfulness. Similarly, the tafarruḍ of a trustworthy narrator is not automatically accepted; it depends on qara'in. The author quotes Imam Ahmad and Abu Dawud to show that even well-known hadiths are distinguished by critics, and ghareeb (strange) hadiths are not used as evidence. As a practical example, Ibn Hajar declared the hadith of Salat al-Tasbih as shadhdh due to extreme individuality despite its chain meeting hasan conditions. The passage then divides tafarruḍ into two types based on position in the sanad: (1) Tafarruḍ in early layers (Sahabah and senior Tabi'un) is generally acceptable if the narrator is trustworthy, due to the difficulty of travel and limited opportunities for meeting. (2) Tafarruḍ in later layers raises suspicion, especially if the narrator is from a scholar whose hadith is widely collected (like al-Zuhri, Malik). Finally, the passage notes that scholars divide afrad into al-fard al-mutlaq (absolute individual) and other types, though the definition of al-fard al-mutlaq is given as a narrator being alone in narrating from one of the narrators. This text is crucial for usul al-fiqh because it shows that the reliability of hadith transmission is not binary; it requires nuanced evaluation by qualified critics.

Key Terms
التفرد (al-tafarruḍ): A narrator being the sole transmitter of a narration
الفرد المطلق (al-fard al-mutlaq): A narration in which the narrator is alone in narrating from one specific narrator
شاذ (shādhdh): A narration from a reliable narrator that contradicts a more reliable source

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on tafarruḍ from a weak narrator?
A) It is always rejected without exception.
B) It is always accepted if the narrator is known for truthfulness.
C) It is not absolutely rejected; critics may select reliable portions using qara'in.
D) It is automatically considered shadhdh.

Key Takeaway
Tafarruḍ is not a binary criterion; its acceptance or rejection depends on qara'in, the narrator's layer, and the presence of mutabi'/shahid.

Classification of Tafarud in Hadith Chains
Classifies tafarud by chain position and narrator reliability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify tafarud in hadith chains by position and type, and apply the Hanafi principle that its acceptance depends on contextual factors.

Core Idea
Tafarud is not automatically accepted or rejected; its acceptance depends on chain position and contextual evidence.

In Hanafi usul, evaluating solitary reports (khabar al-wahid) requires understanding tafarud (individuality in transmission). This lesson classifies tafarud by its position in the chain and by its nature, and explains why critics do not apply a fixed ruling. You will learn to distinguish between acceptable and suspect cases of tafarud based on the narrator's layer and the presence of supporting evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the chain position
Determine whether the tafarud occurs in the early layers (Companions, senior Followers) or later layers. Early tafarud is more acceptable due to limited travel; later tafarud raises suspicion.
Early tafarud: rare and excusable. Later tafarud: questions the narrator's reliability.
2
Assess narrator trustworthiness
Check if the individual narrator (al-mufrid) is thiqah (trustworthy) or da'if (weak). Even a thiqah can have tafarud accepted only with caution; da'if's tafarud is usually rejected unless supported.
Thiqah's tafarud may be accepted if no contradiction with well-known narrations.
3
Classify tafarud type
Determine if the tafarud is absolute (fard mutlaq) – the narrator is the only one from a particular source – or relative (fard nisbi) – uniqueness relative to a specific aspect (e.g., region, teacher).
Absolute: unique in the chain from a specific narrator. Relative: unique in a specific context.
4
Consider contextual factors
Look for supporting mutaba'at (follow-ups) or shawahid (witnesses). The absence of such support combined with tafarud in later layers weakens the hadith. Also check if the narration contradicts well-known hadiths.
Contextual factors can raise a tafarud from rejection to acceptance.
5
Determine the ruling
Apply the principle: no fixed ruling for tafarud. Rely on the overall strength of the hadith based on chain, narrator, and supporting evidence. Tafarud alone does not render a hadith invalid; it is a factor in a broader evaluation.
Hanafi usul emphasizes istihsan and contextual analysis over rigid rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول الاختلاف في السند لشدة الفردية وعدم المتابع والشاهد من وجه معتبر). ويمكننا أن نقسم التفرد - حسب موقعه في السند – إلى قسمين:
الأول: تفرد في الطبقات المتقدمة: كطبقة الصَّحَابَة، وطبقة كبار التَّابِعِيْنَ، وهذا التفرد مقبول إذا كَانَ راويه ثقة - وهذا الاحتراز فيما يخص طبقة التَّابِعِينَ -- فهو أمر وارد جداً لأسباب متعددة يمكن حصرها في عدم توفر فرص متعددة تمكّن الْمُحَدِّثِينَ من التلاقي وتبادل المرويات، وذلك لصعوبة التنقل في البلدان، لا سيما في هذين العصرين. فوقوعه فيهما لا يولد عِنْدَ الناقد استفهاماً عن كيفيته، ولاسيما أن تداخل الأحاديث فيما بينها شيء لا يكاد يذكر، نظراً لقلة الأسانيد زيادة على قصرها. هَذَا فِيْمَا إذا لَمْ يخالف الثابت المشهور، أو من هُوَ أولى مِنْهُ حفظاً أَوْ عدداً.
الرد (٢).
وإن كَانَ المتفرد ضعيفاً أو مجهولاً - فيما يخص التَّابِعِيْنَ- فحكمه بين وَهُوَ
الثاني: التفرد في الطبقات المتأخرة فبعد أن نشط الناس لطلب العلم وأداموا الرحلة فيه والتبحر في فنونه، ظهرت مناهج متعددة في الطلب والموقف مِنْهُ، فكانت الغرس الأول للمدارس الحديثية التي نشأت فِيْمَا بَعْد، فكان لها جهدها العظيم في لَم شتات المرويات وجمعها، والحرص عَلَى تلقيها من مصادرها الأصيلة، فوفرت لهم الرحلات المتعددة فرصة لقاء المشايخ والرواة وتبادل المرويات، فإذا انفرد من هَذِهِ الطبقات أحدٍ بشيء ما فإن ذَلِكَ أمر يوقع الريبة عند الناقد، لا سيما إذا تفرد عمن يجمع حديثه أو يكثر أصحابه، كالزهــري ومالك وشعبة وسفيان وغيرهم). إن العلماء قسموا الأفراد من حَيْثُ التقييد وعدمه إلى قسمين:
الأول: الفرد المطلق وَهُوَ ما ينفرد بِهِ الرَّاوِي عن أحد الرُّوَاة).
الثاني: الفرد النسبي: وَهُوَ ما كَانَ التفرد فِيْهِ نسبياً إلى جهة ما(۱)، فيقيد بوصف يحدد هَذِهِ الجهة.
وما قِيْلَ من أن لَهُ أقساماً أخر، فإنها راجعة في حقيقتها إلى هذين القسمين. أما الحكم على الأفراد باعتبار حال الرَّاوِي المتفرد فَقَط من غير اعتبار للقرائن والمرجحات، فهو خلاف منهج الأئمة النقاد المتقدمين، إذن فليس هناك حكم مطرد بقبول تفرد الثقة أو رد تفرد الضعيف، بَلْ تتفاوت أحكامهما، ويتم تحديدها وفهمها عَلَى ضوء المنهج النقدي النزيه ؛ وذلك لأن الثقة يختلف ضبطه باختلاف الأحوال والأماكن والشيوخ لخلل يحدث في كيفية التلقي للأحاديث أو لعدم توفر الوسائل التي تمكنه من ضبط ما سمعه من بعض شيوخه، أو لحدوث ضياع في بعض ما كتبه عن بعض شيوخه حَتَّى وَلَوْ كَانَ من أثبت أصحابهم ، وألزمهم، ولذا ينكر النقاد من أحاديث الثقات - حَتَّى وَلَوْ كانوا أئمة – ما ليس بالقليل. ومن أمثلة التفرد ما يأتي:
النموذج الأول:
حَدِيث العلاء بن عَبْد الرَّحْمن (۳) ، عن أبيه (۳) ، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة، أَن رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إذا انتصف شعبان فلا تصوموا». أخرجه عبد الرزاق)، وابن أبي شيبة) ، وأحمد ()، والدارمي، وأبو داود)،
