Chapter One: Differences in the Chain
(Shaddu al-fardiyyah wa 'adam al-mutaba' wa al-shahid min wajh mu'tabar). We can divide individuality (tafarud) - according to its position in the chain - into two categories:
First: Individuality in the early layers: Like the layer of the Companions and the layer of the senior Followers. This individuality is acceptable if its narrator is trustworthy - this caution specifically concerns the layer of the Followers - for it is a very common occurrence due to multiple reasons that can be summarized in the unavailability of multiple opportunities that would enable hadith scholars to meet and exchange narrations, due to the difficulty of traveling between countries, especially in these two eras. Its occurrence among them does not raise a question in the critic about how it happened, especially since the intermingling of hadiths among each other is negligible, due to the scarcity of chains in addition to their shortness. This is when he does not contradict the established and well-known, or one who is superior to him in memory or number. The rejection (2). And if the individual narrator is weak or unknown - regarding the Followers - then its ruling is between.
Second: Individuality in the later layers: After people became active in seeking knowledge and undertook journeys for it and delved into its arts, multiple methods emerged in seeking and engaging with it. This was the first planting of the hadith schools that arose later. They had a great effort in gathering scattered narrations and collecting them, and being keen to receive them from their original sources. The multiple journeys provided them the opportunity to meet scholars and narrators and exchange narrations. So if someone from these layers becomes individual with something, that raises suspicion in the critic, especially if he is individual from someone whose hadith is collected or whose students are many, like al-Zuhri, Malik, Shu'bah, Sufyan, and others. The scholars divided individuals in terms of restriction and non-restriction into two categories:
First: The absolute individual (al-fard al-mutlaq): it is what the narrator is individual with from one of the narrators.
Second: The relative individual (al-fard al-nisbi): it is what the individuality is relative to a particular aspect, so it is restricted by a description that specifies this aspect.
What has been said that it has other categories, they in reality revert to these two categories.
As for the ruling on individuals considering only the state of the individual narrator without considering circumstantial evidence and preponderators, it is contrary to the methodology of the early critical imams. Therefore, there is no consistent ruling accepting the individuality of the trustworthy or rejecting the individuality of the weak. Rather, their rulings vary, and they are determined and understood in light of the honest critical methodology. This is because the precision of the trustworthy differs based on circumstances, places, and teachers, due to a defect in the way of receiving hadiths, or the unavailability of means that enable him to precisely retain what he heard from some teachers, or due to loss of some of what he wrote from some teachers, even if he was one of the most established and attached of their companions. Hence, the critics reject not a few of the hadiths of trustworthy narrators - even if they were imams.
Examples of individuality include:
The first model: The hadith of al-'Ala' ibn 'Abd al-Rahman (3), from his father (3), from Abu Hurairah, that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "When half of Sha'ban comes, do not fast." It was reported by 'Abd al-Razzaq (4), Ibn Abi Shaybah (5), Ahmad (6), al-Darimi (7), Abu Dawud (8).

Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the concept of tafarud (individuality) in hadith chains from a Hanafi usul perspective, though it draws on common hadith terminology. The author begins by classifying tafarud according to its position in the chain: first, tafarud in early layers (Companions and senior Followers) is generally acceptable if the narrator is trustworthy, due to the limited travel and exchange of narrations in those early periods. However, if the narrator is weak or unknown, the ruling is between acceptance and rejection. Second, tafarud in later layers raises suspicion because scholars had more opportunities to travel and collect narrations, so a narrator's isolation from well-known figures like al-Zuhri or Malik is questionable. The author then divides tafarud into two types: absolute (al-fard al-mutlaq) where a narrator is unique in reporting from a particular source, and relative (al-fard al-nisbi) where the uniqueness is relative to a specific aspect (e.g., a narrator being the only one from a particular region). The key lesson is that there is no fixed ruling: the acceptance or rejection of a solitary narration depends on contextual factors, not merely on the narrator's trustworthiness. The example given is the hadith prohibiting fasting after mid-Sha'ban, narrated by al-'Ala' ibn 'Abd al-Rahman. This hadith is well-known and has been transmitted by multiple scholars, yet it remains a case of tafarud because al-'Ala' is the only one from his father from Abu Hurairah. The author emphasizes that the critics consider such factors, and tafarud alone does not necessarily invalidate a hadith; other proofs (mutaba'at, shawahid) are needed. This nuanced approach is characteristic of Hanafi usul, which relies on istihsan and other principles to evaluate hadith.

Key Terms
التفرد (al-tafarud): Individuality or uniqueness in narration, where a narrator reports a hadith that no other narrator in the chain shares at that level.
الفرد المطلق (al-fard al-mutlaq): An absolute individual narration: one where the narrator is the only one reporting from a particular narrator or source.
الفرد النسبي (al-fard al-nisbi): A relative individual narration: where the uniqueness is relative to a specific aspect (e.g., being the only narrator from a city or the only one hearing from a teacher in a certain way).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the individuality of a trustworthy narrator?
A) It is always accepted.
B) It is always rejected.
C) It varies and depends on context and circumstantial evidence.
D) It is only accepted in the early layers.

Key Takeaway
Tafarud in hadith chains is evaluated based on chain position, narrator reliability, and contextual evidence; there is no blanket acceptance or rejection.

The Concept of Relative Solitary Narration (al-Fard al-Nisbi)
Definition of relative solitary narration with methodological critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a narration as 'fard nisbi' and explain why relative solitariness does not automatically determine acceptance or rejection in Hanafi hadith criticism.

Core Idea
Relative solitary narration depends on context; reliability of narrator alone is not decisive.

In hadith criticism, a narration is called 'fard nisbi' when its uniqueness is relative to a particular aspect, such as a specific narrator or chain. The early critics did not apply a blanket rule of acceptance or rejection based solely on the narrator's trustworthiness. Instead, they weighed the solitary report against other evidence. This lesson defines the term and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of al-fard al-nisbi
Recognize that it is solitariness relative to a specific aspect, not absolute uniqueness.
2
Contrast with uniform judgment
The passage criticizes judging solitary narrations solely on the narrator's condition without considering contextual evidence (qara'in and tarjihat).
3
Recognize the variability of narrators
Even trustworthy narrators can vary in precision due to circumstances, such as changes in reception or loss of notes.
This is why critics do not automatically accept solitary reports from thiqah narrators.
4
Connect to critical methodology
Early imams used a holistic approach, weighing a solitary report against other evidence, not simply accepting or rejecting based on thiqah or da'if.
5
Preview the example
The hadith of al-'Ala' on fasting after mid-Sha'ban will illustrate the principle in action.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول الاختلاف في السند
الثاني: الفرد النسبي: وهو ما كان التفرد فيه نسبياً إلى جهة ما، فيقيد بوصف يحدد هذه الجهة.
وما قيل من أن له أقساماً أخر، فإنها راجعة في حقيقتها إلى هذين القسمين. أما الحكم على الأفراد باعتبار حال الراوي المتفرد فقط من غير اعتبار للقرائن والمرجحات، فهو خلاف منهج الأئمة النقاد المتقدمين، إذن فليس هناك حكم مطرد بقبول تفرد الثقة أو رد تفرد الضعيف، بل تتفاوت أحكامهما، ويتم تحديدها وفهمها على ضوء المنهج النقدي النزيه ؛ وذلك لأن الثقة يختلف ضبطه باختلاف الأحوال والأماكن والشيوخ لخلل يحدث في كيفية التلقي للأحاديث أو لعدم توفر الوسائل التي تمكنه من ضبط ما سمعه من بعض شيوخه، أو لحدوث ضياع في بعض ما كتبه عن بعض شيوخه حتى ولو كان من أثبت أصحابهم، وألزمهم، ولذا ينكر النقاد من أحاديث الثقات - حتى ولو كانوا أئمة – ما ليس بالقليل.
ومن أمثلة التفرد ما يأتي:
النموذج الأول:
حديث العلاء بن عبد الرحمن، عن أبيه، عن أبي هريرة، أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «إذا انتصف شعبان فلا تصوموا».
أخرجه عبد الرزاق، وابن أبي شيبة، وأحمد، والدارمي، وأبو داود، وابن ماجه، والترمذي، والنسائي، والطحاوي، وابن حبان، والطبراني، والبيهقي، والخطيب، جميعهم من هذه الطريق. قال أبو داود: «لم يجئ به غير العلاء، عن أبيه». وقال النسائي: «لا نعلم أحداً روى هذا الحديث غير العلاء بن عبد الرحمن». وقال الترمذي: «لا نعرفه إلا من هذا الوجه على هذا اللفظ». وأورده الحافظ أبو الفضل بن طاهر المقدسي في أطراف الغرائب والأفراد. وقد أنكره الحفاظ من حديث العلاء بن عبد الرحمن: فقال أبو داود: كان عبد الرحمن - يعني ابن مهدي - لا يحدث به. قلت لأحمد: لم؟ قال: لأنه كان عنده أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يصل شعبان برمضان، وقال: عن النبي خلافه. وقال الإمام أحمد: العلاء ثقة لا ينكر من حديثه إلا هذا. وقال في رواية المروذي: «سألت ابن مهدي عنه فلم يحدثني به،
Chapter One: Disagreement in the Chain of Transmission
Second: The Relative Solitary Narration: It is that in which the solitariness is relative to a certain aspect, so it is restricted by a description that specifies this aspect.
And what has been said that it has other divisions, they are in reality reducible to these two types. As for the judgment on solitary narrations based solely on the condition of the solitary narrator without consideration of supporting evidence and preferencing factors, it is contrary to the methodology of the early critical imams. Therefore, there is no uniform ruling in accepting the solitary narration of a trustworthy narrator or rejecting the solitary narration of a weak narrator; rather, their rulings vary, and they are determined and understood in light of the impartial critical methodology. This is because the precision of a trustworthy narrator varies according to different conditions, places, and teachers, due to a defect that occurs in the manner of receiving hadiths, or the lack of means enabling him to precisely retain what he heard from some of his teachers, or the loss of some of what he wrote from some of his teachers, even if he was among the most reliable of their companions and the most adhering. Hence, critics reject not a few of the hadiths of trustworthy narrators, even if they were imams.
Among the examples of solitariness are the following:
First Model:
The hadith of al-'Ala' ibn 'Abd al-Rahman, from his father, from Abu Hurayra, that the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: 'When the middle of Sha'ban passes, do not fast.'
It was reported by 'Abd al-Razzaq, Ibn Abi Shayba, Ahmad, al-Darimi, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, al-Tahawi, Ibn Hibban, al-Tabarani, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Khatib, all of them from this chain. Abu Dawud said: 'None reported it besides al-'Ala', from his father.' Al-Nasa'i said: 'We do not know anyone who narrated this hadith other than al-'Ala' ibn 'Abd al-Rahman.' Al-Tirmidhi said: 'We do not know it except from this chain in this wording.' Al-Hafiz Abu al-Fadl ibn Tahir al-Maqdisi listed it in 'Atraf al-Ghara'ib wa al-Afarid'. And the critics rejected it from the hadith of al-'Ala' ibn 'Abd al-Rahman: Abu Dawud said: 'Abd al-Rahman – meaning Ibn Mahdi – would not narrate it.' I asked Ahmad: 'Why?' He said: 'Because in his view, the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to connect Sha'ban with Ramadan, and he said that the Prophet said the opposite of it.' Imam Ahmad said: 'Al-'Ala' is trustworthy; nothing of his hadith is rejected except this one.' And in the narration of al-Marwadhi: 'I asked Ibn Mahdi about it, and he did not narrate it to me,'

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'al-fard al-nisbi' (relative solitary narration) in hadith criticism. The author explains that a narration is considered 'fard nisbi' if its tafarud (solitariness) is relative to a particular aspect, such as a specific narrator or chain. The author then critiques the idea that solitary narrations can be uniformly accepted or rejected based solely on the narrator's reliability; rather, they must be evaluated in light of contextual evidence and the critical methodology of early scholars. The example given is the hadith of al-'Ala' ibn 'Abd al-Rahman from his father from Abu Hurayra: 'When half of Sha'ban comes, do not fast.' This hadith is reported by many compilers but all through the same chain, and it is criticized because it contradicts the established practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who used to connect Sha'ban with Ramadan (i.e., fast in the latter part of Sha'ban). Prominent critics like Abu Dawud and Ahmad ibn Hanbal note that this hadith is rejected by many scholars, despite al-'Ala' being a trustworthy narrator, because it opposes stronger evidence. This shows that tafarud (uniqueness of narration) is not automatically acceptable even from a thiqah (trustworthy narrator) if it contradicts established norms or stronger proofs.

Key Terms
الفرد النسبي (al-fard al-nisbi): ما كان التفرد فيه نسبياً إلى جهة ما (solitariness relative to a particular aspect)
تفرد (tafarud): انفراد الراوي بالحديث (the narrator's uniqueness in reporting)
ثقة (thiqah): الراوي الموثوق به في ضبطه وعدالته (trustworthy narrator in precision and integrity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following best describes the basis for judging a solitary narration?
A) The narrator's reliability alone.
B) The narrator's reliability combined with contextual evidence and critical methodology.
C) The number of chains.
D) The length of the hadith.

Key Takeaway
A solitary narration must be evaluated with contextual evidence (qara'in) and critical principles, not merely by the narrator's trustworthiness.

Case Study: The Hadith of al-'Ala' on Fasting After Mid-Sha'ban
Specific example of a rejected solitary narration despite trustworthy narrator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the critical methodology of early hadith scholars to evaluate the hadith of al-'Ala' ibn 'Abd al-Rahman and explain why it was rejected despite al-'Ala' being a trustworthy narrator.

Core Idea
Even a trustworthy narrator's solitary report is rejected if it contradicts established practice.

The hadith of al-'Ala' ibn 'Abd al-Rahman, 'When half of Sha'ban comes, do not fast,' is a classic example of a relative solitary narration that was critically evaluated by early imams. Although al-'Ala' is considered thiqah, the hadith was rejected because it contradicted the known practice of the Prophet ﷺ who used to connect Sha'ban with Ramadan by fasting in the latter part. This lesson examines the transmission, the criticism, and the principles derived from this case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the tafarud
All chains go through al-'Ala' from his father. The hadith is solitary to this chain.
Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i confirmed its uniqueness.
2
Verify narrator reliability
Al-'Ala' is considered trustworthy (thiqah) by Ahmad ibn Hanbal and others.
This eliminates the narrator's weakness as the cause of rejection.
3
Detect contradiction
The hadith contradicts established practice: the Prophet used to connect Sha'ban with Ramadan by fasting in the latter part.
Ibn Mahdi and Ahmad cited this contradiction.
4
Understand the critics' reasoning
They rejected it because it opposes stronger evidence, despite al-'Ala' being thiqah.
Ahmad said: 'Al-'Ala' is trustworthy; nothing of his hadith is rejected except this one.'
5
Extract the methodological lesson
A solitary hadith from a thiqah may be rejected if it contradicts established practice or stronger evidence.
This shows the need for contextual evaluation, not uniform acceptance.

الفصل الأول الاختلاف في السند
الثاني: الفرد النسبي: وهو ما كان التفرد فيه نسبياً إلى جهة ما، فيقيد بوصف يحدد هذه الجهة.
وما قيل من أن له أقساماً أخر، فإنها راجعة في حقيقتها إلى هذين القسمين. أما الحكم على الأفراد باعتبار حال الراوي المتفرد فقط من غير اعتبار للقرائن والمرجحات، فهو خلاف منهج الأئمة النقاد المتقدمين، إذن فليس هناك حكم مطرد بقبول تفرد الثقة أو رد تفرد الضعيف، بل تتفاوت أحكامهما، ويتم تحديدها وفهمها على ضوء المنهج النقدي النزيه ؛ وذلك لأن الثقة يختلف ضبطه باختلاف الأحوال والأماكن والشيوخ لخلل يحدث في كيفية التلقي للأحاديث أو لعدم توفر الوسائل التي تمكنه من ضبط ما سمعه من بعض شيوخه، أو لحدوث ضياع في بعض ما كتبه عن بعض شيوخه حتى ولو كان من أثبت أصحابهم، وألزمهم، ولذا ينكر النقاد من أحاديث الثقات - حتى ولو كانوا أئمة – ما ليس بالقليل.
ومن أمثلة التفرد ما يأتي:
النموذج الأول:
حديث العلاء بن عبد الرحمن، عن أبيه، عن أبي هريرة، أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «إذا انتصف شعبان فلا تصوموا».
أخرجه عبد الرزاق، وابن أبي شيبة، وأحمد، والدارمي، وأبو داود، وابن ماجه، والترمذي، والنسائي، والطحاوي، وابن حبان، والطبراني، والبيهقي، والخطيب، جميعهم من هذه الطريق. قال أبو داود: «لم يجئ به غير العلاء، عن أبيه». وقال النسائي: «لا نعلم أحداً روى هذا الحديث غير العلاء بن عبد الرحمن». وقال الترمذي: «لا نعرفه إلا من هذا الوجه على هذا اللفظ». وأورده الحافظ أبو الفضل بن طاهر المقدسي في أطراف الغرائب والأفراد. وقد أنكره الحفاظ من حديث العلاء بن عبد الرحمن: فقال أبو داود: كان عبد الرحمن - يعني ابن مهدي - لا يحدث به. قلت لأحمد: لم؟ قال: لأنه كان عنده أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يصل شعبان برمضان، وقال: عن النبي خلافه. وقال الإمام أحمد: العلاء ثقة لا ينكر من حديثه إلا هذا. وقال في رواية المروذي: «سألت ابن مهدي عنه فلم يحدثني به،
Chapter One: Disagreement in the Chain of Transmission
Second: The Relative Solitary Narration: It is that in which the solitariness is relative to a certain aspect, so it is restricted by a description that specifies this aspect.
And what has been said that it has other divisions, they are in reality reducible to these two types. As for the judgment on solitary narrations based solely on the condition of the solitary narrator without consideration of supporting evidence and preferencing factors, it is contrary to the methodology of the early critical imams. Therefore, there is no uniform ruling in accepting the solitary narration of a trustworthy narrator or rejecting the solitary narration of a weak narrator; rather, their rulings vary, and they are determined and understood in light of the impartial critical methodology. This is because the precision of a trustworthy narrator varies according to different conditions, places, and teachers, due to a defect that occurs in the manner of receiving hadiths, or the lack of means enabling him to precisely retain what he heard from some of his teachers, or the loss of some of what he wrote from some of his teachers, even if he was among the most reliable of their companions and the most adhering. Hence, critics reject not a few of the hadiths of trustworthy narrators, even if they were imams.
Among the examples of solitariness are the following:
First Model:
The hadith of al-'Ala' ibn 'Abd al-Rahman, from his father, from Abu Hurayra, that the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: 'When the middle of Sha'ban passes, do not fast.'
It was reported by 'Abd al-Razzaq, Ibn Abi Shayba, Ahmad, al-Darimi, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, al-Tahawi, Ibn Hibban, al-Tabarani, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Khatib, all of them from this chain. Abu Dawud said: 'None reported it besides al-'Ala', from his father.' Al-Nasa'i said: 'We do not know anyone who narrated this hadith other than al-'Ala' ibn 'Abd al-Rahman.' Al-Tirmidhi said: 'We do not know it except from this chain in this wording.' Al-Hafiz Abu al-Fadl ibn Tahir al-Maqdisi listed it in 'Atraf al-Ghara'ib wa al-Afarid'. And the critics rejected it from the hadith of al-'Ala' ibn 'Abd al-Rahman: Abu Dawud said: 'Abd al-Rahman – meaning Ibn Mahdi – would not narrate it.' I asked Ahmad: 'Why?' He said: 'Because in his view, the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to connect Sha'ban with Ramadan, and he said that the Prophet said the opposite of it.' Imam Ahmad said: 'Al-'Ala' is trustworthy; nothing of his hadith is rejected except this one.' And in the narration of al-Marwadhi: 'I asked Ibn Mahdi about it, and he did not narrate it to me,'
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'al-fard al-nisbi' (relative solitary narration) in hadith criticism. The author explains that a narration is considered 'fard nisbi' if its tafarud (solitariness) is relative to a particular aspect, such as a specific narrator or chain. The author then critiques the idea that solitary narrations can be uniformly accepted or rejected based solely on the narrator's reliability; rather, they must be evaluated in light of contextual evidence and the critical methodology of early scholars. The example given is the hadith of al-'Ala' ibn 'Abd al-Rahman from his father from Abu Hurayra: 'When half of Sha'ban comes, do not fast.' This hadith is reported by many compilers but all through the same chain, and it is criticized because it contradicts the established practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who used to connect Sha'ban with Ramadan (i.e., fast in the latter part of Sha'ban). Prominent critics like Abu Dawud and Ahmad ibn Hanbal note that this hadith is rejected by many scholars, despite al-'Ala' being a trustworthy narrator, because it opposes stronger evidence. This shows that tafarud (uniqueness of narration) is not automatically acceptable even from a thiqah (trustworthy narrator) if it contradicts established norms or stronger proofs.

Key Terms
الفرد النسبي (al-fard al-nisbi): ما كان التفرد فيه نسبياً إلى جهة ما (solitariness relative to a particular aspect)
تفرد (tafarud): انفراد الراوي بالحديث (the narrator's uniqueness in reporting)
ثقة (thiqah): الراوي الموثوق به في ضبطه وعدالته (trustworthy narrator in precision and integrity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the main reason for the rejection of the hadith of al-'Ala' on fasting after mid-Sha'ban?
A) Al-'Ala' was an unreliable narrator.
B) The hadith contradicted the established practice of the Prophet.
C) The hadith was not found in any major collection.
D) The hadith had a broken chain.

Key Takeaway
A solitary hadith may be rejected even from a trustworthy narrator if it contradicts established practice or stronger evidence.

Hadith Weakness and Fiqh Disagreement: The Case of Mid-Sha'ban Fasting
Analysis of hadith chain and its fiqh impact

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key weaknesses in the hadith on mid-Sha'ban fasting and explain how these weaknesses lead to differing fiqh rulings among scholars.

Core Idea
A hadith's chain weakness can cause jurists to disagree on its ruling, as seen in the dispute on fasting after mid-Sha'ban.

In this lesson, we examine a specific hadith that has sparked disagreement among jurists: the prohibition of fasting after the middle of Sha'ban. The passage you're about to read analyses the hadith's chain of transmission, revealing multiple weaknesses. This analysis directly explains why some scholars consider the fasting makruh, while others see no prohibition. By understanding the hadith criticism, you will see how usul al-fiqh principles and hadith evaluation interact to produce different legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith text
Locate the exact wording of the hadith under discussion: 'When Sha'ban reaches its middle, then break the fast.'
This hadith is the center of the dispute.
2
Examine the primary chain and its criticisms
The passage discusses the chain through al-‘Ala’ ibn ‘Abd al-Rahman. Note the critics (Ibn Mahdi, Ahmad, etc.) who deemed it munkar.
Al-‘Ala’ is not the only narrator; there is a supporting chain via al-Munkadir.
3
Analyze the supporting chain
The passage then examines the chain from al-Tabarani, showing it contains unknown and weak narrators. Note the comments on ‘Abdullah ibn al-Munkadir and al-Munkadir ibn Muhammad.
This chain is even weaker and is dismissed as a delusion.
4
Observe the scholarly disagreement on authenticity
Some scholars (al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Hibban) authenticated the hadith, while major critics (Ahmad, Ibn Mahdi) rejected it. This split in evaluation leads to differing fiqh rulings.
The passage lists both sides.
5
Connect authenticity to fiqh disagreement
The majority of Shafi‘is, who accept the hadith as at least admissible for non-obligatory matters, rule fasting after mid-Sha'ban as makruh. Ibn Hazm, combining hadiths, restricts the prohibition to the 16th day only. Those who reject the hadith entirely see no prohibition.
Thus, the chain's weakness directly shapes the ikhtilaf.

المتفرد بهذا الْحَدِيث ، قَالَ فِيْهِ العقيلي: «عن أبيه، ولا يتابع عَلَيْهِ». وَقَالَ الذهبي: «فيه جهالة، وأتى بخبر منكر ». وَقَالَ مرة: «لا يعرف». والمنكدر بن مُحَمَّد - الَّذِي لَمْ يرو هَذَا الْحَدِيث عن أبيه غيره - And he used to avoid it. Then Abu Abdullah said: This contradicts the hadiths narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him). Ibn Ma'in also deemed it objectionable. Al-Sakhawi claimed that al-‘Ala’ was not unique in this and that he had a follower in his narration from his father, for al-Tabarani narrated the hadith saying: 'Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Nafi‘ narrated to us, saying: ‘Ubaydullah ibn ‘Abdullah al-Munkadiri informed us, my father narrated to me, from his father, from his grandfather, from ‘Abd al-Rahman ibn Ya‘qub al-Haraqi, from Abu Hurayrah, who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: “When Sha‘ban reaches its middle, then break the fast.”' Al-Tabarani said after it: 'This hadith was not narrated from Muhammad ibn al-Munkadir except by his son al-Munkadir, and his son ‘Abdullah was unique in it.' The truth is that this hadith is not suitable for citation, let alone to strengthen the narration of al-‘Ala’, because it is a chain of weak and unknown narrators: starting from the shaykh of al-Tabarani, Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Nafi‘, for whom I found no biography except what al-Dhahabi mentioned in Mizan al-I‘tidal, saying: 'I do not know who this is? Ibn al-Jawzi mentioned him once and said: They accused him, so he said, he did not add more.' And ‘Abdullah ibn al-Munkadir, who was unique in this hadith, al-‘Uqayli said about him: 'From his father, and no one follows him in it.' Al-Dhahabi said: 'There is ignorance in him, and he brought a rejected report.' And he said once: 'He is unknown.' And al-Munkadir ibn Muhammad, from whom no one else narrated this hadith from his father, Abu Hatim said about him: 'He was a righteous man who did not establish hadith well, he made many mistakes, and he was not a memorizer of his father's hadith.' Al-Nasa’i said: 'Weak,' and he said once: 'Not strong,' and similar was said by Abu Zur‘ah. Ibn Hibban said: 'Worship distracted him from maintaining memory and consistency in precision, so he would bring things that have no basis from his father due to delusion.' Al-Dhahabi said: 'There is some weakness in him.' Thus it became clear that the witness is not fit for consideration; it is definitely one of the delusions of al-Munkadir ibn Muhammad. As for al-‘Ala’ ibn ‘Abd al-Rahman, from his father, Ibn Rajab said: The scholars differed about the authenticity of this hadith and then acting upon it. More than one authenticated it, among them al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Hibban, al-Hakim, and Ibn ‘Abd al-Barr. But those greater and more knowledgeable than these criticized it, saying it is a rejected hadith, among them: ‘Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi, Ahmad, Abu Zur‘ah al-Razi, and al-Athram. Imam Ahmad rejected it with the hadith: 'Do not precede Ramadan by fasting a day or two days,' for its implication permits preceding by more than two days. The effect of the hadith on the jurists' disagreement: Ruling on fasting the second half of Sha‘ban. The jurists differed on the ruling of fasting the second half of Sha‘ban as follows: First: Some people went to the dislike of fasting after the middle of Sha‘ban until Ramadan. This is what al-Tahawi narrated without specifying the proponents, and it is the view of the majority of Shafi‘is. Ibn Hazm narrated it from some people. Second: Ibn Hazm – as a combination of the hadiths of the chapter – specified the prohibition to the sixteenth day of Sha‘ban.

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of the hadith 'When Sha'ban reaches its middle, then break the fast' and its effect on juristic disagreement. It first examines the chain of transmission, noting that the primary narrator al-‘Ala’ ibn ‘Abd al-Rahman has been criticized, and a supporting chain via al-Munkadir is even weaker. The passage then shows that despite some scholars authenticating the hadith, major critics like Ahmad ibn Hanbal and Ibn Mahdi deemed it munkar. This disagreement over authenticity directly impacts fiqh: the majority of Shafi'is consider fasting after mid-Sha'ban as makruh, while Ibn Hazm, trying to reconcile conflicting hadiths, restricts the prohibition to the 16th day only. The author here demonstrates how differences in evaluating a hadith's sanad lead to divergent legal rulings.

Key Terms
متفرد (mutafarrid): A narrator who is alone in narrating a hadith from his shaykh.
منكر (munkar): A hadith narrated by a weak narrator contradicting stronger narrations.

Dispute over Fasting in Second Half of Sha'ban: Usul Analysis
Case study of hadith chain dispute affecting fasting rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the impact of a weak hadith chain on a fiqh ruling by analyzing the Hanafi response to the hadith of 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-'Ala'.

Core Idea
A weak hadith cannot override the basic principle of permissibility.

This lesson examines how a hadith's chain weakness (da'f al-sanad) leads to disagreement among jurists over the ruling of fasting in the second half of Sha'ban. By analyzing the criticism of narrator al-Munkadir ibn Muhammad, you will understand why the Hanafi school and the majority of scholars uphold permissibility despite the existence of a hadith that appears to prohibit fasting after mid-Sha'ban.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting rulings
Read the four positions recorded in the text: (1) dislike (karahah) from some Shafi'is, (2) restriction of prohibition to the 16th by Ibn Hazm, (3) outright prohibition (tahrim) by al-Ruyani, and (4) permissibility without dislike by the majority including Hanafis.
Note that the Hanafi school falls under the fourth position.
2
Analyze the hadith used as evidence
The proponents of the first three positions rely on the hadith of 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-'Ala' from his father from Abu Hurayra. Identify the chain and note the narrator al-Munkadir ibn Muhammad.
The hadith is not quoted verbatim; only the chain is discussed.
3
Evaluate the chain criticism (jarh)
The text presents criticisms from several hadith critics: Hatim calls him 'not a memorizer', al-Nasa'i says 'weak', Ibn Hibban says he would bring things with no basis, and al-Dhahabi says 'there is softness'. This shows the hadith is weak (da'if).
This is a parsing exercise: identify the type of criticism (jarh mufassar or mujmal).
4
Apply the usul principle
Apply the Hanafi usul principle that a weak hadith cannot establish a prohibition or dislike. The basic principle (al-asl) is permissibility until a valid proof (dalil sahih) of prohibition exists.
Hanafi usul: a hadith that is not authentic (sahih) cannot override the default ruling of ibahah.
5
Determine the preponderant view
The majority view (including Hanafis) is preponderant because the hadith is weak and there is no other evidence for prohibition. The basic principle remains, so fasting after mid-Sha'ban is permissible without dislike.
Tarjih: the view that is supported by stronger evidence (or absence of evidence for prohibition) prevails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول الاختلاف في السند

حاتم: «كَانَ رجلاً صالحاً لا يقيم الْحَدِيث وَكَانَ كثير الخطأ، لَمْ يَكُنْ بالحافظ لحديث أبيه». وَقَالَ النسائي: «ضعيف»، وَقَالَ مرة: «ليس بالقوي» وبنحوه قال أبو زرعة). وَقَالَ ابن حبان: قطعته العبادة عن مراعاة الحفظ والتعاهد في الإتقان، فكان يأتي بالشيء الذي لا أصل له عن أبيه توهما) (۳). وَقَالَ الذهبي: «فِيْهِ لين»(4).
وبهذا تبين أن الشاهد غَيْر صالح للاعتبار، فهو جزماً من أوهام المنكدر بن مُحَمَّد.
أما
أثر الحديث في اختلاف الفقهاء حكم صوم النصف الثاني من شعبان) اختلف الفقهاء في حكم صوم النصف الثاني من شعبان على النحو الآتي:

ثانياً: خص ابن حزم ) - جمعاً بَيْنَ أحاديث الباب - النهي باليوم السادس عشر من شعبان (۱).

رابعاً: ذهب جمهور كراهة (٤). العلماء إلى إباحة صوم النصف الثاني من شعبان من غير
واستدل أصحاب المذاهب الثلاثة الأول بحديث عَبْد الرَّحْمن بن العلاء، عَلَى اختلاف في تحديد نوع الحكم.
وأجاب الجمهور بتضعيف حديثه، وعدم وجود ما يقتضي التحريم أو الكراهة، بَلْ وجود ما يعضد القول بالاستحباب.
ومذهب الجمهور هُوَ الراجح في عدم الكراهة وجواز صيام النصف الثاني من شعبان لضعف حَدِيث العلاء وعدم صحته. والأصل الجواز حَتَّى يأتي دليل التحريم الكراهة.
Chapter One: Disagreement in the Chain

Hatim said: 'He was a righteous man who did not maintain the [precision of] hadith and made many mistakes; he was not a memorizer of his father's hadith.' Al-Nasa'i said: 'Weak,' and he said once: 'Not strong,' and similarly said Abu Zur'ah. Ibn Hibban said: 'Worship cut him off from caring about preservation and striving for precision, so he would bring something that has no basis from his father erroneously.' Al-Dhahabi said: 'There is softness in him.'
Thus it is clear that the [corroborating] witness is not suitable for consideration; it is definitely from the delusions of al-Munkadir ibn Muhammad.
As for the effect of the hadith on the disagreement of jurists regarding the ruling on fasting in the second half of Sha'ban: The jurists disagreed about the ruling on fasting in the second half of Sha'ban as follows:
First: Some people held that fasting after the middle of Sha'ban until Ramadan is disliked. Thus al-Tahawi reported it without specifying those who said it, and it is the view of the majority of Shafi'is. Ibn Hazm reported it from some people.
Second: Ibn Hazm specifically restricted the prohibition to the sixteenth day of Sha'ban, reconciling the hadiths of the chapter.
Third: Al-Ruyani from the Shafi'is held that fasting in the second half of Sha'ban is prohibited.
Fourth: The majority of scholars held that fasting in the second half of Sha'ban is permissible without any dislike.
The proponents of the first three schools used the hadith of 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-'Ala' as evidence, differing on the determination of the type of ruling.
The majority responded by weakening his hadith, and that there is nothing indicating prohibition or dislike, but rather there is something supporting the view of recommendation.
And the position of the majority is the preponderant view: there is no dislike and it is permissible to fast the second half of Sha'ban due to the weakness of the hadith of al-'Ala' and its lack of authenticity. The basic principle is permissibility until evidence of prohibition or dislike comes.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a case study demonstrating how disagreement over the authenticity of a hadith leads to disagreement among jurists in a fiqh ruling. The author first explains the weakness of a narrator (al-Munkadir ibn Muhammad) in the chain of a hadith, then presents the different rulings on fasting in the second half of Sha'ban. Four positions are recorded: (1) dislike (karahah) reported from some Shafi'is, (2) Ibn Hazm's restriction of prohibition to the 16th, (3) prohibition (tahrim) from al-Ruyani, and (4) permissibility without dislike from the majority of scholars, which includes the Hanafi school. The majority's argument is that the hadith of 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-'Ala' is weak and therefore cannot establish prohibition or dislike. The author concludes that the majority view is preponderant because the basic principle (asl) is permissibility until a valid proof of prohibition exists. Hanafis follow this view, as fasting in the second half of Sha'ban is permissible and not disliked.

Key Terms
الكراهة (al-karāhah): حكم شرعي يقتضي طلب الترك لا على سبيل الجزم
التحريم (al-taḥrīm): حكم شرعي يقتضي المنع الجازم ويترتب عليه الإثم
الحديث المنكر (al-ḥadīth al-munkar): الحديث الذي يتفرد به راو ضعيف مخالفاً لمن هو أوثق منه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of scholars (including the Hanafis), what is the ruling on fasting after the middle of Sha'ban?
A) It is disliked (makruh)
B) It is permissible without dislike
C) It is prohibited (haram)
D) It is recommended (mandub)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school and the majority hold that fasting after mid-Sha'ban is permissible because the hadith prohibiting it is weak, and the basic principle is permissibility until a valid proof of prohibition exists.

The Effect of Tafarrud on Hadith Acceptance
Analyzes a gharib hadith chain and its acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a hadith is considered tafarrud and explain how Hanafi usul evaluates such narrations for evidence.

Core Idea
A gharib hadith does not automatically imply weakness; reliability of the narrator is key.

This lesson examines a hadith on combining prayers that is narrated exclusively by Qutayba. We will see how hadith critics classify it as hasan gharib, and discuss how Hanafi usul handles such ahad. Understanding this helps in evaluating the strength of evidence used in fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Examine the hadith text and chain
Read the hadith from Mu'adh ibn Jabal describing the Prophet's practice of combining prayers during Tabuk. Note the chain: Qutayba → al-Layth → Yazid → Abu al-Tufayl → Mu'adh.
2
Identify the phenomenon of tafarrud
The author states that Qutayba alone narrated this hadith from al-Layth. This exclusive narration (tafarrud) makes the hadith gharib (strange) at that stage.
Tafarrud refers to a single narrator at any chain level.
3
Analyze the critics' statements
Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Khatib all confirm that Qutayba is the sole narrator. Al-Tirmidhi classifies it as hasan gharib.
Hasan gharib means good in terms of text but strange in chain.
4
Apply Hanafi usul principles
Hanafis accept khabar al-wahid if the narrator is reliable (thiqah). Here, Qutayba is thiqah, so the hadith is acceptable as evidence despite its gharaba.
In Hanafi usul, tafarrud does not automatically reject; it may reduce preference among conflicting narrations.
5
Determine the fiqh outcome
The hadith supports the permissibility of combining prayers during travel. Hanafis use it as one proof for jam' under certain conditions.
The practical ruling: combining prayers is allowed in travel with proper conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النموذج الثاني:
حديث قتيبة بن سعيد، عن الليث بن سعد، عن يزيد بن أبي حبيب)، عن أبي الطفيل عامر بن واثلة)، عن معاذ بن جبل (): «أن النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ في غزوة تبوك إذا ارتحل قَبْلَ زيغ الشمس أخر الظهر إلى أن يجمعها إلى العصر فيصليهما جميعاً، وإذا ارتحل بَعْدَ زيغ الشمس عجّل العصر إلى الظهر، وصلى الظهر والعصر جميعاً ثُمَّ سار.
وَكَانَ إذا ارتحل قَبْلَ المغرب أخر المغرب حَتَّى يصليها مع العشاء، وإذا ارتحل بَعْدَ المغرب عجل العشاء فصلاها مع المغرب».
رَوَاهُ أحمد (۱) ، وأبو داود (۳)، والترمذي (۳) ، وابن حبان)، والدارقطني والحاكم)، والبيهقي ) ، والخطيب البغدادي ) ، والذهبي ()، كلهم من طريق قتيبة هَذِهِ. ()
أقول: هَذَا الْحَدِيث تفرد به قتيبة عن الليث، ونص الحفاظ عَلَى ذَلِكَ:
قَالَ أبو داود: «لَمْ يروِ هَذَا الْحَدِيث إلا قتيبة وحده (۱). وَقَالَ الترمذي: حَدِيث معاذ حَدِيث حسن غريب، تفرّد به قتيبة، لا نعرف أحداً رَوَاهُ عن الليث غيره وحديث الليث عن يزيد بن أبي حبيب، عن أبي الطفيل، عن معاذ: حَدِيث غريب»(۱۱).
وَقَالَ البيهقي: تفرد به قتيبة بن سعيد، عن ليث، عن يزيد (۱۲). وَقَالَ الْخَطِيْب: «لَمْ يروِ حَدِيْث يزيد بن أبي حبيب، عن عن أبي الطفيل عن الليث:
The Second Model: The hadith of Qutayba ibn Sa'id, from al-Layth ibn Sa'd, from Yazid ibn Abi Habib, from Abu al-Tufayl 'Amir ibn Wathila, from Mu'adh ibn Jabal: 'That the Prophet, peace be upon him, during the expedition of Tabuk, when he set off before the sun's declination, he delayed Zuhr until he combined it with 'Asr and prayed both together; and when he set off after the sun's declination, he hastened 'Asr to Zuhr and prayed Zuhr and 'Asr together, then proceeded. And when he set off before Maghrib, he delayed Maghrib until he prayed it with 'Isha'; and when he set off after Maghrib, he hastened 'Isha' and prayed it with Maghrib.' Narrated by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Hibban, al-Daraqutni, al-Hakim, al-Bayhaqi, al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, and al-Dhahabi, all via this route of Qutayba. I say: This hadith is narrated exclusively by Qutayba from al-Layth, and the hadith scholars have stated this. Abu Dawud said: 'No one narrated this hadith except Qutayba alone.' Al-Tirmidhi said: 'The hadith of Mu'adh is hasan gharib, Qutayba alone narrated it; we do not know anyone who narrated it from al-Layth other than him; the hadith of al-Layth from Yazid ibn Abi Habib from Abu al-Tufayl from Mu'adh is gharib.' Al-Bayhaqi said: 'Qutayba ibn Sa'id alone narrated it from Layth from Yazid.' Al-Khatib said: 'No one narrated the hadith of Yazid ibn Abi Habib from Abu al-Tufayl from al-Layth:'
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage presents a second model of chain difference. It provides the full text of a hadith from Mu'adh ibn Jabal describing how the Prophet combined prayers during the Tabuk expedition. The hadith describes two scenarios: if departing before zawal (noon), he delayed Zuhr and combined with 'Asr; if after zawal, he brought 'Asr forward. Similarly for Maghrib and 'Isha'. The hadith is narrated by many scholars, but all through one chain: Qutayba from al-Layth. The author then highlights that this hadith is tafarruda bihi Qutayba (exclusive to Qutayba). He quotes several hadith critics (Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Bayhaqi, al-Khatib) who confirm that Qutayba alone narrated it. Al-Tirmidhi classifies it as hasan gharib (good but strange). This analysis demonstrates how a chain's uniqueness (gharaba) affects the hadith's authenticity and subsequent fiqh use. In Hanafi usul, such a hadith (khabar al-wahid) is accepted if the narrator is reliable, but the gharaba may affect preference between conflicting narrations.

Key Terms
تفرد (tafarrud): The characteristic of a hadith being narrated by only one person from a particular narrator.
غريب (gharib): A hadith that is narrated by only one person at some stage of the chain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which hadith critic stated that this hadith is 'hasan gharib' and that Qutayba alone narrated it?
A) Abu Dawud
B) Al-Tirmidhi
C) Al-Bayhaqi
D) Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi

Key Takeaway
Tafarrud does not automatically invalidate a hadith; the narrator's reliability is paramount in Hanafi usul.

Chain Dispute in the Hadith of Combining Prayers
Analysis of a chain dispute in combining prayers hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a gharib (strange) chain and a mahfuz (preserved) chain, and explain how Hanafi usul uses chain criticism to prefer one narration over another.

Core Idea
A hadith criticized for tafarrud (single narrator) may be set aside if a mahfuz chain exists.

This lesson examines a concrete example of how differences in hadith chains (sanad) impact the reliability of a legal proof. The hadith on combining prayers during travel is transmitted through two different chains: one via Qutayba (considered gharib) and another via Abu al-Zubayr (deemed mahfuz). Understanding this distinction is crucial for Hanafi usul when weighing ahadith for deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two chains
Locate the two chains mentioned: (1) Qutayba → Layth → Yazid ibn Abi Habib → Abu al-Tufayl → Mu'adh; (2) Abu al-Zubayr → Abu al-Tufayl → Mu'adh (with eight narrators including Malik).
The first chain is unique to Qutayba; the second is widely narrated.
2
Recognize the tafarrud (singularity)
Note the consensus of hadith critics (Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi, Bayhaqi, etc.) that Qutayba is the sole narrator from Layth. This makes the hadith 'gharib' in chain.
Tafarrud alone does not reject the hadith, but it raises scrutiny.
3
Understand the criticism and proposed error
Some scholars (Abu Sa'eed ibn Yunus) suggest Qutayba may have mistakenly substituted Abu al-Zubayr with Yazid ibn Abi Habib. Bayhaqi clarifies that the Abu al-Zubayr version is the authentic one.
This is an example of 'idraj' or confusion in the chain.
4
Apply Hanafi usul: prefer the mahfuz chain
Hanafi usul accepts ahad hadith but gives greater weight to a narration that is 'mahfuz' (preserved) over one that is 'shadh' (irregular). Here, the Abu al-Zubayr chain is mahfuz due to multiple narrators, so it is preferred for deriving the ruling on combining prayers.
The ruling on combining prayers is confirmed by other evidences as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول / الاختلاف في السند
وَكَانَ إذا ارتحل قَبْلَ المغرب أخر المغرب حَتَّى يصليها مع العشاء، وإذا ارتحل بَعْدَ المغرب عجل العشاء فصلاها مع المغرب.
أقول: هَذَا الْحَدِيث تفرد به قتيبة عن الليث، ونص الحفاظ عَلَى ذَلِكَ:
قَالَ أبو داود: «لَمْ يروِ هَذَا الْحَدِيث إلا قتيبة وحده. وَقَالَ الترمذي: حَدِيث معاذ حَدِيث حسن غريب، تفرّد به قتيبة، لا نعرف أحداً رَوَاهُ عن الليث غيره وحديث الليث عن يزيد بن أبي حبيب، عن أبي الطفيل، عن معاذ: حَدِيث غريب».
وَقَالَ البيهقي: تفرد به قتيبة بن سعيد، عن ليث، عن يزيد. وَقَالَ الْخَطِيْب: «لَمْ يروِ حَدِيْث يزيد بن أبي حبيب، عن أبي الطفيل عن الليث: غَيْر قتيبة».
وأورده الحافظ ابن طاهر المقدسي في : " أطراف الغرائب والأفراد وَقَالَ الذهبي: «ما رَوَاهُ أحد عن الليث سوى قتيبة».
وَقَدْ أنكر هَذَا الْحَدِيث عَلَى قتيبة سنداً ومتناً:
أما في السند: فالرواية المحفوظة هِيَ رِوَايَة أبي الزبير، عن أبي الطفيل، عن معاذ. قَالَ أبو سعيد بن يونس: «لَمْ يحدث به إلا قتيبة، ويقال: إنه غلط، وإن موضع يزيد بن أبي حبيب: أبو الزبير».
وَقَالَ البيهقي: «وإنما أنكروا من هَذَا رِوَايَة يزيد بن أبي حبيب، عن أبي الطفيل، فأما رِوَايَة أبي الزبير عن أبي الطفيل فهي محفوظة صحيحة». وَقَدْ وقفت عَلَى ثمانية أنفس رووه عن أبي الزبير عن أبي الطفيل، عن معاذ وهم:
مالك بن أنس: ومن طريقه الشَّافِعِي، وعبد الرزاق، وأحمد، والدارمي، ومسلم، وأبو داود، والنسائی، وابن خزيمة، والطحاوي، والشاشي، وابن حبان، والطبراني، والبيهقي
First chapter: Disagreement in the chain. And when he departed before Maghrib he delayed Maghrib until he prayed it with Isha', and when he departed after Maghrib he hastened Isha' and prayed it with Maghrib. I say: This hadith is unique to Qutayba from Layth, and the memorizers stated that: Abu Dawood said: 'No one narrated this hadith except Qutayba alone.' And Tirmidhi said: 'The hadith of Mu'adh is a hasan gharib hadith, unique to Qutayba; we do not know anyone who narrated it from Layth other than him, and the hadith of Layth from Yazid ibn Abi Habib from Abu al-Tufayl from Mu'adh is a gharib hadith.' And Bayhaqi said: 'Qutayba ibn Sa'eed alone narrated it from Layth from Yazid.' And al-Khatib said: 'No one narrated the hadith of Yazid ibn Abi Habib from Abu al-Tufayl from Layth except Qutayba.' And al-Hafiz Ibn Tahir al-Maqdisi recorded it in 'Aatraf al-Ghara'ib wa al-Afraad', and al-Dhahabi said: 'No one narrated it from Layth except Qutayba.' And this hadith was rejected regarding Qutayba in both chain and text: As for the chain: the preserved narration is the narration of Abu al-Zubayr from Abu al-Tufayl from Mu'adh. Abu Sa'eed ibn Yunus said: 'No one narrated it except Qutayba, and it is said that he erred, and that the place of Yazid ibn Abi Habib is Abu al-Zubayr.' And al-Bayhaqi said: 'They only rejected from this the narration of Yazid ibn Abi Habib from Abu al-Tufayl; as for the narration of Abu al-Zubayr from Abu al-Tufayl, it is preserved and authentic.' And I have come across eight individuals who narrated it from Abu al-Zubayr from Abu al-Tufayl from Mu'adh: Malik ibn Anas - and from his path al-Shafi'i, Abd al-Razzaq, Ahmad, al-Darimi, Muslim, Abu Dawood, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Khuzaymah, al-Tahawi, al-Shashi, Ibn Hibban, al-Tabarani, and al-Bayhaqi.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of a hadith chain related to combining prayers during travel. The author presents the hadith text describing the Prophet's practice when departing before Maghrib (delaying Maghrib to combine with Isha') or after Maghrib (bringing Isha' forward). The key issue is that this hadith is only known through a single chain: Qutayba ibn Sa'eed from Layth ibn Sa'd from Yazid ibn Abi Habib from Abu al-Tufayl from Mu'adh. Multiple hadith scholars (Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi, Bayhaqi, Khatib, Dhahabi) confirm that Qutayba is the sole narrator of this version. The hadith was criticized both in its chain (sanad) and text (matn). Regarding the sanad, the more reliable (mahfuz) narration is via Abu al-Zubayr from Abu al-Tufayl from Mu'adh, not via Yazid ibn Abi Habib. Abu Sa'eed ibn Yunus suggests Qutayba may have erred, confusing Yazid with Abu al-Zubayr. Bayhaqi clarifies that the narration via Abu al-Zubayr is the authentic one. The author then lists eight narrators who transmitted the hadith via Abu al-Zubayr, establishing its strength. This analysis shows how differences in chains (sanad) can lead to differences in juristic rulings: the weaker chain (Qutayba's) may be less reliable for deriving fiqh, while the stronger chain (Abu al-Zubayr's) is preferred. In Hanafi fiqh, combining prayers during travel is permitted under certain conditions, and the strength of evidence impacts the ruling.

Key Terms
تفرد به (tafarrada bihi): A hadith narrated by only one person from a particular authority, making it gharib (strange) in chain.
محفوظة (mahfuzah): A narration that is preserved and well-attested, opposite of shadh (irregular).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because Qutayba was a weak narrator.
B) Because only Qutayba narrated it from Layth, and the more preserved chain is via Abu al-Zubayr.
C) Because the hadith contradicts the Quran.
D) Because Abu Dawood rejected it completely.

Key Takeaway
Chain criticism (naqd al-isanid) is essential in hadith evaluation; a gharib chain may be set aside when a mahfuz chain exists, but the ruling can still be supported by the stronger chain.

Analyzing Hadith Chains: The Case of Mu'adh's Hadith
Examining the multiple chains of Mu'adh's hadith to determine the correct transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key features of a hadith chain analysis (sanad criticism) and apply the Hanafi method of weighing multiple chains to determine the reliability of a narration.

Core Idea
Multiple chains strengthen a hadith; an isolated chain may contain an error.

In this lesson, we examine a detailed example of chain analysis from a classical work. The author investigates a hadith from Mu'adh that was criticized. He shows that while one chain (via Qutayba from al-Layth) was rejected, the same hadith is preserved through multiple narrators from Abu al-Zubair. This illustrates how scholars use the accumulation of chains (turuq) to confirm a hadith's authenticity and overcome isolated weak transmissions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the criticized chain
Note the hadith narrated by Qutayba from al-Layth was rejected. The specific alleged error is the inclusion of Yazid ibn Abi Habib in the chain instead of Abu al-Zubair.
This is an example of chain substitution (idraj) in the sanad.
2
Locate the preserved chain
The author states the preserved narration is via Abu al-Zubair from Abu al-Tufail from Mu'adh, citing al-Bayhaqi's confirmation.
This chain is considered mahfuz (preserved) and sahih (authentic).
3
List the supporting narrators
The author enumerates eight narrators who transmitted from Abu al-Zubair, including Malik ibn Anas, Qurra ibn Khalid, Amr ibn al-Harith, Hisham ibn Sa'd, and Sufyan al-Thawri, and names the scholars who recorded them.
The multiplicity of narrators provides mutaba'at (supporting chains).
4
Evaluate the strength
The multiple chains from Abu al-Zubair show the hadith is well-attested and authentic in sanad, while the isolated chain via Yazid is considered weak (da'if) and a mistake.
This analysis is a form of tarjih in hadith criticism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غَيْر قتيبة»(1).
الفصل الأول / الاختلاف في السند
وأورده الحافظ ابن طاهر المقدسي في : " أطراف الغرائب والأفراد وَقَالَ الذهبي: «ما رَوَاهُ أحد عن الليث سوى قتيبة».
وَقَدْ أنكر هَذَا الْحَدِيث عَلَى قتيبة سنداً ومتناً:
أما في السند: فالرواية المحفوظة هِيَ رِوَايَة أبي الزبير، عن أبي الطفيل، عن معاذ. قَالَ أبو سعيد بن يونس: «لَمْ يحدث به إلا قتيبة، ويقال: إنه غلط، وإن موضع يزيد بن أبي حبيب: أبو الزبير».
وَقَالَ البيهقي: «وإنما أنكروا من هَذَا رِوَايَة يزيد بن أبي حبيب، عن أبي الطفيل، فأما رِوَايَة أبي الزبير عن أبي الطفيل فهي محفوظة صحيحة». وَقَدْ وقفت عَلَى ثمانية أنفس رووه عن أبي الزبير عن أبي الطفيل، عن معاذ وهم:
1. مالك بن أنس: ومن طريقه الشَّافِعِي، وعبد الرزاق، وأحمد، والدارمي، ومسلم، وأبو داود، والنسائی، وابن خزيمة، والطحاوي، والشاشي، وابن حبان، والطبراني، والبيهقي.
2. قرة بن خالد: عِند أبي داود الطيالسي، وأحمد، ومسلم، والبزار، وابن خزيمة، والطحاوي، وابن حبان، والطبراني.
3. عمرو بن الحارث: عِنْدَ الطبراني.
4. هشام بن سعد: عِنْدَ الإمام أحمد وعبد بن حميد، والبزار، والشاشي، والطبراني.
5. سفيان بن سعيد الثوري: ومن طريقه أخرجه عبد الرزاق، وابن أبي شيبة، وابن ماجه، والطبراني، وأبو نعيم، وأحمد.
Other than Qutayba. The first chapter: Disagreement in the chain. Al-Hafiz Ibn Tahir al-Maqdisi recorded it in 'Atraf al-Ghara'ib wa al-Afarad' and al-Dhahabi said: 'No one narrated it from al-Layth except Qutayba.' And this hadith was rejected from Qutayba in chain and text. As for the chain: The preserved narration is the narration of Abu al-Zubair, from Abu al-Tufail, from Mu'adh. Abu Sa'id ibn Yunus said: 'No one narrated it except Qutayba, and it is said that he made a mistake, and that the position of Yazid ibn Abi Habib is Abu al-Zubair.' And al-Bayhaqi said: 'What they denied from this is the narration of Yazid ibn Abi Habib, from Abu al-Tufail; as for the narration of Abu al-Zubair from Abu al-Tufail, it is preserved and authentic.' And I have come across eight individuals who narrated it from Abu al-Zubair from Abu al-Tufail from Mu'adh, and they are: 1. Malik ibn Anas: and through him al-Shafi'i, Abd al-Razzaq, Ahmad, al-Darimi, Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Khuzayma, al-Tahawi, al-Shashi, Ibn Hibban, al-Tabarani, and al-Bayhaqi. 2. Qurra ibn Khalid: according to Abu Dawud al-Tayalisi, Ahmad, Muslim, al-Bazzar, Ibn Khuzayma, al-Tahawi, Ibn Hibban, and al-Tabarani. 3. Amr ibn al-Harith: according to al-Tabarani. 4. Hisham ibn Sa'd: according to Imam Ahmad, Abd ibn Humayd, al-Bazzar, al-Shashi, and al-Tabarani. 5. Sufyan ibn Sa'id al-Thawri: and through him it was recorded by Abd al-Razzaq, Ibn Abi Shayba, Ibn Majah, al-Tabarani, Abu Nu'aym, and Ahmad.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of a specific hadith chain. It begins by noting that Qutayba was the only one to narrate this hadith from al-Layth, and it was criticized. The author then explains that the authentic chain is via Abu al-Zubair from Abu al-Tufail from Mu'adh, not via Yazid ibn Abi Habib. He lists eight narrators who transmitted the hadith from Abu al-Zubair: Malik ibn Anas (through him many scholars), Qurra ibn Khalid, Amr ibn al-Harith, Hisham ibn Sa'd, and Sufyan al-Thawri, among others. This demonstrates that the hadith is well-attested through Abu al-Zubair, contrary to Qutayba's isolated chain. The Hanafi school uses such textual analysis to weigh the authenticity of ahadith and resolve apparent contradictions.

Key Terms
سند (sanad): The chain of narrators of a hadith, indicating the path of transmission.
متن (matn): The textual content or body of the hadith.
رواية (riwayah): A particular transmission or version of a hadith from a narrator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many individuals did the author find who narrated the hadith from Abu al-Zubair?
A) Five
B) Six
C) Eight
D) Ten

Key Takeaway
Multiple transmitting chains (turuq) from a common source can establish a hadith's reliability, even when a single chain is disputed.
